# Bernard 'Buck' Barton  —  *Trick Shot*

![[_attachments/bernard_barton.png]]

# Bernard Barton — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

**Subject:** Bernard "Buck" Barton, alias *Trick Shot*.
**File Class:** Tier-3 Adversary / Mentor-Class Antagonist — Recurring Revenant.
**Bottom Line Up Front:** The subject is a malignant-narcissistic craftsman whose entire adult existence has been the staging, restaging, and finally the choreographed terminal performance of a single relational scene: *I make you, I withhold from you, you expose me, I punish you, I rewrite the record so that you are the traitor and I am the wronged master.* He has lived that loop for roughly four decades of recorded time against one specific protégé, and his deathbed conduct confirms he will die inside it rather than step out of it. Everything else — the embezzlement, the murders-for-hire, the wandering, the cancer, the heir-naming — is connective tissue around that core scene.

---

## Who He Is, At The Deepest Level

Strip the carnival paint, the bow, the alias, the contract sheets, the hospital bed. What remains is a man whose self exists only in being witnessed performing the impossible, and whose entire interior architecture is organized to prevent the discovery that, beneath the performance, there is no one home who can be loved on any terms but mastery. He is not, at root, an assassin; assassination is a late-career means of staying inside the only economy in which he is legible to himself. He is not, at root, a thief; the embezzlement was a small-time degeneration of a man who had already decided long before that other people's regard was a resource to be extracted rather than earned. He is not even, at root, a teacher; the pedagogy was a method of binding a smaller human into a mirror that would reflect the master back to himself at greater than life size.

What he *is*, at root, is the formal structure of conditional regard wearing a man's body. Performance is the only currency; loyalty to the hierarchy of skill is the only ethics; the gaze of the watcher is the only proof of existence. Inside that structure, affection cannot be expressed except as discipline, exposure cannot be metabolized except as betrayal, decline cannot be borne except as escalation, and death cannot be permitted except as a final scene he directs. He is a closed system that mistakes its own walls for the world.

The cruelest accurate sentence in the file is this: he is not a monster. He is an *ordinary* damaged man with an extraordinary hand, and that ordinariness is what makes the damage he inflicts transmissible. Monsters end with themselves. He does not — the protégé carries the shape of him forward into every subsequent mentor-relationship, and the second heir to the *Trick Shot* name carries the formal pedagogy forward into a third generation. The pathology is contagious because it is dressed as craft.

---

## The Through-Line Of His Entire Existence

A single sentence runs from his first appearance in the carnival lots to the staged hospice tableau: *to be seen as the one who decides who else may be seen.* Every recorded behavior is a variation on that theme.

- In the carnival years, the through-line presents as showmanship — the alias itself, *Trick Shot* rather than Marksman or Archer, foregrounds the wow of the watching crowd over the technical noun. He chose to be a spectacle, not a discipline.
- In the pedagogical years with the Barton boys, it presents as the manufacture of a protégé whose existence will testify to the master. Praise is metered; the student is built; the student is owned by the building.
- In the embezzlement and abandonment, it presents as the collapse of the staging when the protégé refuses the role of admiring witness and instead becomes a moral one. The response is not flight but punitive violence — because the wound is not legal exposure but ontological exposure. Clint did not just see the theft; he saw *him*.
- In the mercenary middle period, it presents as the conversion of the same skill into contract violence, almost always with a vector that bends back toward the protégé. He does not wander away from the original scene; he keeps redrawing his career into proximity with it.
- In the terminal period, it presents as the deathbed summons — the maximal grandiose gesture, the final assertion that even his ending will be authored by him and executed through the body of the one he abandoned.

The through-line is not "archery." Archery is the instrument. The through-line is *mastery-as-ownership of the gaze of the other*, and every era simply re-equips that drive with whatever the current circumstance allows.

---

## The Core Wound And Its Maintenance

**The wound the file can document** is the moment the young Clint Barton exposed the carnival theft. From that hour forward, every confrontation across decades returns to the same affective coordinates: Buck behaves as if Clint stole something from *him* — specifically, the unbroken mirror of admiring subordination — and as if no subsequent action by Clint can ever restore the article taken. The forty-year half-life of this grievance is itself the diagnostic finding. Ordinary anger decays; this does not.

**The wound the file must infer** sits one layer beneath, in undocumented childhood. The polish of his cruelty, the fluency of his contempt, the speed with which tenderness inverts into discipline — these are not improvisations. They have the worn quality of motions practiced under a harder hand. Somewhere, regard was conditional on performance; somewhere, exposure of weakness was punished as betrayal; somewhere, the only stable adult model was the master who withholds. He has reproduced the economy he was raised in, with terrifying fidelity, on the body and psyche of a child who came to him already abandoned.

**Maintenance mechanisms** — how the wound stays open, decade after decade, without ever healing or being grieved:

1. *Projection as load-bearing wall.* Every encounter is pre-narrated such that he is the wronged party. The theft becomes Clint's disloyalty; the abandonment becomes Clint's failure to follow; the late contracts become Clint's continued refusal to acknowledge the master. The wound never closes because closure would require accepting authorship, and authorship would collapse the entire self.
2. *Sublimation of all affect into craft.* He does not feel grief, longing, regret, or fear in any form he can name. The feelings exist; they are routed into the draw, the hold, the release. The bow does his feeling for him. This is highly stable and highly costly: nothing is ever processed, so nothing is ever finished.
3. *Recurrent contact without repair.* He keeps coming back into Clint's orbit — not despite the unhealed wound but *because* the wound is his only intimate possession. To heal it would be to lose it, and to lose it would be to lose the through-line of the self. The recurrences function the way a tongue returns to a sore tooth: not to fix, to confirm.
4. *Reaction formation around any threatened softening.* Whenever proto-paternal feeling rises — and the canon shows it doing so, briefly, in late training scenes and again on the deathbed — it is immediately overwritten by harshness. The defense is so reliable it can be predicted in real time: any tender beat in a scene with him will be followed within seconds by a contemptuous one.
5. *Audience as proof of existence.* He cannot be alone with the wound, because solitude removes the witness who validates the master. The deathbed summons is the terminal expression of this: he will not die unobserved. He requires the betrayed protégé as both audience and instrument, because only that configuration confirms that the original scene was real and that he was, in it, the master.

---

## Operational Summary

For any handler, operator, analyst, or unfortunate party required to be in the room with the subject, the following are the load-bearing operational facts.

**Threat profile.** Lethal at distance to a degree at the upper extremity of unenhanced human capability, sustained into terminal illness. The threat does not decline linearly with health; it *escalates* with somatic erosion, because narrowing physical capacity is met with widening willingness to inflict harm. He is most dangerous in the window between recognized decline and total incapacity.

**Behavioral signature.** Cold baseline, narrow affective band, spike-on-exposure. The tells are physical and consistent: stillness before action rather than tension; the draw initiated before the verbal exchange concludes; eye-contact held a beat longer than social convention permits; a small theatrical pause inserted before any shot intended to be witnessed. He performs even when ostensibly working — the carnival never left him.

**Approach vectors that work.**
- Out-shoot him in front of a witness. Skill-exceedance in a public frame is the only stimulus reliably observed to crack composure.
- Reframe the protégé's success as *despite* him, not because of him. This attacks the narcissistic extension and produces measurable disorganization.
- Remove the audience. He is least dangerous in true unwatched solitude, where the performance has no fulcrum. Negotiations, if required, should be conducted without observers.
- Maintain instrumental, transactional register. He understands contract, debt, hierarchy of skill, and challenge. These he can metabolize.

**Approach vectors that fail, and worsen the situation.**
- Empathic appeal. Registered as weakness; confirms his position; triggers escalation.
- Offers of reconciliation, apology, or repair. In every documented instance involving Clint, these have been the precise trigger for renewed cruelty. They are not neutral failures; they are accelerants.
- Moral argument. He does not parse the moral register at all. Time spent on it is time he uses to set up the shot.
- Appeals to past affection or shared history. He experiences these as the other party's confession of unhealed need, and exploits accordingly.

**Predictable scenes.** The file projects, with high confidence, the following recurrences for as long as the subject remains alive and ambulatory: (a) periodic re-emergence in the protégé's operational space under pretext of contract, succession, or final accounting; (b) staged confrontations in which the subject arranges to be witnessed; (c) any terminal-phase event will be choreographed as a coercive intimacy with the protégé at its center, framed publicly as legacy-transfer and functionally a last assertion of authorship.

**Containment posture.** Do not attempt rehabilitation; there is no purchase. Do not attempt destruction-by-confrontation; the confrontation is the gift he is asking for. The optimal posture is *deny him the scene*: refuse the staged meetings, decline the choreographed endings, deprive him of the witnessed final act. He cannot be the master without a watcher and a student. Remove both and the structure collapses into the ordinary dying man it has always been underneath.

**Residual risk after subject's death.** Non-trivial and not closed by the death certificate. The pathology has been transmitted in two directions: into a successor bearing the *Trick Shot* name, and — far more consequentially — into the somatic and relational habits of Clint Barton, who will continue, predictably, to be susceptible to mentor-figures who promise belonging through performance and who deliver punishment for autonomy. The file recommends that the subject's death be treated not as case-closure but as the beginning of a separate, long-running watch on the wound he leaves behind.

---

**BLUF, in one paragraph:** Bernard Barton is the formal structure of conditional regard wearing a man's body and holding a bow. He has spent four decades restaging a single scene in which he is the master, the protégé is the mirror, exposure is betrayal, and punishment is justice; he is dying inside that scene and intends to make his death its final act. He is lethal, transmissible, and unreachable by appeal. Handle by denying him the audience and the student; expect him to keep trying to assemble both until the moment the heart stops.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

**Subject:** Bernard "Buck" Barton, alias *Trick Shot*
**File segment:** Pre-carnival life, c. earliest published date through approximately age 18
**Canonical density:** LOW. Inferential weight: HIGH.

---

## 0. A Methodological Note Before the Ground Floor

The published canon — *Hawkeye* vol. 1 (1983, Gruenwald/Hannigan); *Solo Avengers* #1–4 (1987, Gruenwald/Cooper); *Avengers Spotlight* #22–25; the *West Coast Avengers* run through Gruenwald's tenure; Chuck Dixon's *Hawkeye* mini (1994); the Fraction-era *Hawkeye* (2012–15) backgrounders; and the Lemire/Pérez-era *Hawkeye* and *Old Man Hawkeye* echoes — has, conspicuously, never depicted Bernard Barton as a child. Not in flashback, not in monologue, not in third-person reminiscence. He arrives on the page already weathered, already in late middle age, already armed, already the *teacher*. The man has no recorded mother, no recorded father, no recorded sibling, no recorded hometown, no recorded school, no recorded first bow.

This vacuum is itself the most important datum in the section. A character constructed by Gruenwald to be Clint Barton's *etiological key* was never given an etiology of his own. The wound stops with him. He is, in the narrative architecture, *the upstream pole*. From a UATU vantage that is required to map every existence, this absence must be filled by responsible inference from observed adult phenotype, period-typical context (American carnival circuit, 1930s–50s working substrata), and the structural psychology already substantiated in the Shared Assessment. What follows is reconstruction, not transcription. Each inference is flagged.

---

## 1. Birth & Earliest Locating Data

**Date.** Marvel sliding-time conventions place Clint Barton's birth in Waverly, Iowa, in the (perpetually receding) recent past. Across Gruenwald-era depictions, Buck appears to be roughly 30–35 years Clint's senior — visibly weathered, gray at the temples, deep crow's-foot crinkle around the eyes (the marksman's chronic squint, *Hawkeye* vol. 1 #2, training-yard panel). Translated to a stable historical anchor: Bernard Barton's birth falls in the late 1920s to mid-1930s window, almost certainly *pre–World War II*, almost certainly in the rural or small-town American interior. The carnival circuit he later joined was a Depression-and-postwar phenomenon at peak; he is shaped by its labor market.

**Place.** Unstated. Two corroborating inferences point to the Midwest or Upper South: (a) his idiom in Gruenwald scripts — "boy," "son," the dropped *g* on participles ("you ain't listenin'"), the period-rural diction that survives in the *Solo Avengers* arc — is consistent with that band; (b) the Carson Carnival's geographic loop in the canon (it picks the Barton brothers up in Iowa) reads as a northern-Midwest small-town circuit, which is also the recruiting ground for its veteran performers. He did not have to travel far to join.

**Name.** *Bernard* is given; *Buck* is the work name. The fact that he answers — in every published panel — to *Buck* and bristles, mildly, when called *Bernard* (a single moment in *Hawkeye* vol. 1 #4 where Swordsman uses the formal name with edge) is a small but durable tell. The given name belongs to a self he has put down. *Buck* is American-vernacular, masculine-coded, animal-coded (the male deer; the resistant horse; the dollar), and crucially *performative* — a barker's name, a chalkboard name, a name that fits on a tent banner in red paint. He has, somewhere in adolescence, *renamed himself out of his family of origin*. Subjects who do that almost always do it for a reason; the reason is almost always not pride in what they left.

**Socioeconomic stratum.** Working-poor to outright poor. The carnival circuit was not an upward path; it absorbed the surplus rural labor of mid-century America — the orphaned, the runaway, the broke, the men with criminal records or family debts, the men whose only asset was a body and a skill. Buck's complete fluency in that world, his lack of any "outside" social repertoire (he has no documented contact with anyone *off* the circuit until his criminal contracting period), and his utter unsentimentality about its conditions place him as native to it from very young, not as a downwardly mobile arrival.

---

## 2. Family of Origin

Unrecorded. The reconstruction:

**Father (inferred, high confidence).** The Shared Assessment's identification of *identification with the aggressor* as a structural defense is the linchpin. Buck's pedagogy with Clint — the absence of warmth, the metering of regard against performance, the punitive escalation under exposure, the absolute conviction that hardness *is* love correctly administered — has the over-rehearsed quality of a transmitted script. He is not improvising cruelty; he is reproducing a curriculum. The most parsimonious source is a paternal or surrogate-paternal figure of the same kind: a man (a father, an uncle, a foreman, a circuit performer who took him on at twelve) who taught skill with the back of the hand and called the result discipline. The fact that Buck *never* invokes his father — never a "my old man said," never a comparative reminiscence even in late-life monologue when terminal men typically reach for origin stories — suggests not absence but suppression. Subjects who say nothing about a father usually have a great deal to say and have decided, structurally, not to.

**Mother (inferred, moderate confidence).** Two possibilities. (a) Died early — explains the total affective absence of any feminine tenderness register in his adult repertoire; he has no learned vocabulary for it. (b) Present but powerless — a woman bracketed out of authority in a punitive household, and therefore disqualified, in the child's developing schema, from the category of *people who matter*. Buck's adult treatment of women in canon is not misogynistic in a hot, expressive sense; it is something colder — women are simply not in the operational frame. In *Solo Avengers* #2 he barely registers Mockingbird as an antagonist worth turning his head for; the slight reads as functional, not theatrical. Either etiology produces this. The mother is gone, in fact or in standing, well before adolescence.

**Siblings.** No record, and probably none surviving in his orbit. A subject with a maintained sibling tie tends to leak it — a name, a Christmas gesture, a passing reference. Buck leaks nothing. If there were brothers, he outlived or outran them. (Note the *resonance* with the Barton boys he later adopts: he takes in two brothers, and the pair is treated by him as a single instrumental unit until Barney and Clint diverge — a handling pattern consistent with a man who has no internal model of sibling individuation.)

**Household texture (inferred).** Rural or small-town; cold in winter and unheated past the kitchen; meals taken in silence or in instruction; physical labor expected of the child from very young; a father whose mood was the household's weather and whose approval was the only currency in circulation. Religious atmosphere, if any, of the disciplinary-Protestant kind that frames pain as instructive — but not, importantly, devotional; Buck shows no liturgical residue at all in his adult speech, no scripture-cadence, no profanity that scans as inverted piety. The household's religion, if it had one, was *competence*.

---

## 3. The Childhood Environment

Placing Bernard Barton in 1930s–1940s rural America by inference gives us the ambient field:

- **Material scarcity** as the default register of reality. Food was sufficient or it wasn't; clothes were inherited; tools were repaired rather than replaced. The adult Buck's relationship to *equipment* — the obsessive care of bowstring, nock, fletching, the documented preference for hand-built arrows in the *Hawkeye* vol. 1 training scenes — has the quality of a child who learned that gear is precious because gear is finite.
- **Firearms and bows in the household as ordinary objects.** Rural mid-century America put a .22 in a boy's hands at seven or eight. If the canon's adult Buck is a *bowman* rather than a rifleman, it is almost certainly because the bow was the cheaper, quieter, reusable-ammunition weapon for a household that could not afford boxes of cartridges. The bow is, in this reconstruction, an artifact of poverty before it is an artifact of vocation. (This is non-trivial: it means the skill was forced on him by circumstance and *then* discovered to be exceptional, which is a different developmental pathway than the suburban hobbyist or the upper-class sportsman. It produces a different relationship to the weapon — utilitarian, possessive, identity-fused.)
- **Education: minimal and intermittent.** No canonical reference to schooling. Adult Buck reads (he handles contracts in the *Solo Avengers* mercenary period) but writes nothing, quotes nothing, displays no abstract vocabulary. Eighth- or ninth-grade ceiling, plausibly less. The cognitive-style note in the Shared Assessment — "concrete, tactical, present-focused, low introspective capacity" — is consistent with formal education that ended at the body's first usefulness for labor.
- **The Depression's psychological residue,** even on a child too young for its onset: a household organized around the proposition that softness is a luxury and the world will take what it can. He inherited that proposition pre-verbally.

---

## 4. The Formative Bonds (Reconstructed in Negative)

What we can derive from what is absent in the adult:

**No friend.** Across every published appearance, Bernard Barton has *partners* (Swordsman), *employers* (Crossfire and others), *targets*, and *the protégé*. He has no friend. He references no friend. He recalls no friend. A childhood that produces no preserved peer attachment is, almost without exception, a childhood in which peer attachment was either unavailable (isolation, transience, labor) or actively discouraged (a household in which the child's loyalty was monopolized by the parent's surveillance). Both conditions are consistent with the inferred father.

**No mentor remembered with warmth.** When Clint, in the *Hawkeye* vol. 1 #4 confrontation, throws the word *teacher* back at Buck, Buck does not — as a more sentimental character would — invoke his own teacher in turn. He has no Yoda in the rearview. Either he was self-taught (possible; the carnival absorbed many autodidacts) or, more likely given the structural reproduction of pedagogy, he was taught by a man whose memory he refuses to honor with reference. The training he gives Clint is the training he received, *unattributed* — which is itself the deepest form of identification with the aggressor: you do not credit the aggressor because to credit would be to admit the wound.

**The first bow.** Unrecorded; reconstructed as a household tool, not a gift. The distinction matters. A weapon received as gift creates a relational memory around the weapon (the giver, the occasion, the obligation). A weapon picked up off a peg in a barn because it was there and the child was hungry creates an instrumental memory: the weapon is *of the self*, not *between selves*. Buck's adult bond to the bow has the latter quality — it is not a sacred object given to him; it is a part of his body that he found early.

**The first kill.** Inferred: small game, very young, alone, in necessity. The lack of any documented squeamishness in the adult, the lack of any compensatory ritual around killing (no last-rites mutter, no professional's superstition, no recoil reaction even when shooting a man who was a child to him in *Hawkeye* #4), all suggest that the developmental threshold from *aiming* to *killing* was crossed before the cognitive apparatus that would have flagged it as a threshold was online. He does not remember the first one because he was too young when it happened to encode it as first.

---

## 5. Formative Traumas (Inferred From Adult Phenotype)

Three lines of evidence, three reconstructed traumas:

**(a) Conditional-regard trauma.** The Shared Assessment's etiological inference is supported by the entire shape of the adult pedagogical scenes. The trauma is not a single event; it is a developmental atmosphere. The child Bernard learned, by the age of perhaps five or six, that he existed in his father's eye only as a function of *demonstrated competence*. Praise was an event so rare it became sacramental; its withdrawal was the standing condition. This produces, predictably, the adult who cannot extend unconditional regard because he has no template for it — and who cannot tolerate, in the protégé, any assertion of selfhood independent of performance, because such an assertion was never available to him.

**(b) Exposure trauma.** The disproportionate, decades-long rage at being *exposed* by Clint in the embezzlement scene (Hawkeye vol. 1 #3–4) — the fact that this single incident anchors his adult life — argues for a childhood incident in which a similar exposure was catastrophic. A boy caught in something — a small theft, a lie about chores, a hidden injury, a hidden weakness — and shamed publicly within the household economy. The intensity of his adult reaction is not in proportion to Clint's act; it is in proportion to the *original* act it reactivates. Exposure, for this subject, equals annihilation. The defense built around the original event — *blame the exposer* — became his structural core.

**(c) Abandonment or witnessed abandonment.** His own readiness to abandon Clint after the beating — the speed, the absence of any backward-glance scene in the canon, the way he *leaves* rather than *flees* — has the practiced quality of a man for whom departure is a known move. Possibility (i): a parent left, and he absorbed the script. Possibility (ii): he himself was sent away — bound out to labor, sent to a relative, ejected at fourteen to make his own way. Either is consistent. The carnival, when he later found it, did not have to teach him how to live in transit; he already knew.

---

## 6. Earliest Behavioral Patterns (The Patterns Already Visible in the Adult That Must Have Begun Early)

These are the longitudinal threads — the *first instances* of which are pre-canonical, but the *signature* of which is so coherent across his adult record that they cannot have been late-acquired.

**The squint.** A persistent, almost continuous narrowing of the eyes that Gruenwald's artists (Hannigan especially) draw even in non-aiming scenes — over coffee, in conversation, at rest. This is not the marksman's professional squint alone; it is a *facial set* acquired in childhood from a combination of outdoor labor (sun exposure without brimmed protection) and the early-internalized habit of *not letting the eye show*. Subjects from punitive households frequently develop a baseline ocular guardedness — the eye is the giveaway and learns, early, to give nothing.

**The stillness.** Adult Buck is preternaturally still. He does not fidget; he does not pace; he holds positions for long intervals. This is partly trained (every marksman cultivates it) but the *baseline* — the way he is still even when not shooting — is older. It is the stillness of a child in a household where movement attracts attention and attention is dangerous. Compare and contrast with Clint, who is kinetic, fidgety, hand-talking — Clint's household (Harold Barton's documented violence) produced a *hypervigilant-mobile* child; Buck's evidently produced a *hypervigilant-immobile* one. Both are trauma responses; they are opposite poles of the same axis.

**The non-laugh.** Across hundreds of panels, Buck Barton does not laugh. He produces, occasionally, a thin smile — usually contemptuous, occasionally appreciative of a good shot — but the laugh is absent from his record. Children who do not learn to laugh have, almost without exception, grown up in households where laughter was unsafe (it drew the parent's notice, or mocked the parent, or was reserved to the parent alone). The adult's laughlessness is the child's hardened survival policy.

**Care of equipment as displaced self-care.** The fastidiousness with which the adult Buck maintains his gear — the cleaning, the inspection, the refusal to use a fletching he has not personally examined (*Hawkeye* vol. 1 #2) — has the quality of ritual obsessive attention displaced onto the object from the self. A child who could not care for himself (could not protect, soothe, repair himself) often develops, in adulthood, a meticulous external object-care that bears the affective load. The bow gets the tenderness the body never received and cannot now accept.

**The instructional voice.** Even in non-pedagogical contexts, Buck instructs. He corrects, he diagnoses, he tells other adults how to stand. This is the voice of a child who learned that to *speak as the one who knows* is the only mode of speech that does not invite ridicule or correction. He has only ever had one safe register. He uses it on everyone.

**Loyalty as the master ethical category.** The Shared Assessment correctly identifies loyalty as his only ethical primitive. This is a *household* ethic — the ethic of a small, closed, threatened group in which the betrayer is the worst of crimes because the group cannot survive him. Children raised in genuine community develop more elaborated moral vocabularies; children raised in beleaguered households of two or three develop loyalty as the alpha and omega. Buck's moral world is the size of the household he came out of, and he has been operating it, at scale, ever since.

**Renaming.** Already covered above, but worth restating here as a behavioral marker: the move from *Bernard* to *Buck* is the earliest *documented act of self-construction* in his life. We can place it provisionally in mid-adolescence — old enough for the act to take, young enough for the new name to have set fully by the time the carnival received him. This act, more than any other single datum, marks the boundary between the childhood we cannot see and the adult who walks onto the canonical page.

---

## 7. The Threshold to the Next Chronology

The file picks Bernard "Buck" Barton up, in observable canon, when he is already standing on a Carson Carnival lot with a bow in his hand and a contemptuous half-smile for the newcomer Jacques Duquesne. The boy who became that man is, in the published record, *gone* — and the disappearance is the most eloquent thing about him. He has spent his adulthood ensuring that no one, including the reader, will ever see what made him. The Shared Assessment's structural diagnosis — narcissistic organization, conditional-regard etiology, exposure as the load-bearing trauma — is, in this section, given its developmental floor: a rural, poor, paternally punitive, peerless, laughless, instrumentally weaponized childhood in mid-century America, exited under a chosen name, with a bow and the conviction that softness is the most dangerous thing a person can show.

The next file segment (*Chronology II — Adolescence, the Road, and Entry to the Carson Circuit*) will trace the documented and inferential record from the renaming forward, to the first appearance alongside Duquesne and the arrival, in the lot, of the two Iowa brothers whose presence will, decades later, kill him.

— END SECTION —


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

## Subject: Bernard "Buck" Barton / TRICK SHOT

*Period covered: approx. age 14 through approx. age 35 — the carnival apprenticeship years, the consolidation of the marksman identity, the partnership with Jacques Duquesne, the acquisition of the Barton boys, and the foundational rupture that ends the formative arc.*

---

## 2.1 The Pre-Carnival Interval (approx. ages 14–17): Vanishing into the Midway

Canon does not name the household Bernard Barton left, and the silence is itself the document. Across forty years of published appearances he never references a mother, never invokes a hometown, never marks a birthday, never speaks the name his birth certificate would carry — only "Buck," only "Trick Shot," only the professional surname that, by the time it reaches print, has been polished smooth of any prior context. A man who has so thoroughly liquidated his origin has done so deliberately, and the act of liquidation is the first behavior on file.

Inferable from the texture of his later pedagogy: he learned his discipline under a hard hand before he ever held a bow professionally. The metronomic withholding of praise he later inflicts on Clinton Barton is too refined, too automatic, too economically deployed to be a personal invention. It has the polish of inheritance. Somewhere in the years before the midway he was the boy on the wrong end of a man who graded his existence by the inch of a target — most plausibly a father, possibly an uncle, possibly an itinerant teacher, certainly male, certainly older, certainly someone who taught him that affection was a reward dispensed at the discretion of a superior eye.

The shift into the carnival circuit, somewhere in mid-adolescence, was almost certainly a flight rather than a recruitment. Carson Carnival in this period — a third-tier travelling show working the secondary and tertiary Midwestern and Southern fair circuit — was the kind of organization that did not check papers and did not ask questions of a teenager who could already throw a knife straight or hit a balloon at twenty paces. The Carson roster of the era, glimpsed in the Hawkeye Vol.1 #4 backgrounds and in fragmented Solo Avengers flashback panels, runs to the standard menagerie: a strongman, a fat lady, a mentalist, a knife-thrower, a bearded woman, the Swordsman as featured headliner, and the slot for "Trick Shot" — a slot Bernard inherited or invented as he moved up through the back-of-show.

The first verifiable employment is as roustabout and assistant: the boy who set the targets for the prior incumbent of the marksman act. There is no canonical naming of that prior marksman, but his existence is structurally necessary, and the speed with which Bernard transitions from target-boy to act-headliner — by his late teens he is billed in his own right — implies either a precocious talent that displaced the older man through sheer competitive pressure, or, more consistent with the adult Bernard's interpersonal style, a quieter displacement: undermined trick by trick, made redundant, eased out. The carnival is small; the act has one slot; Bernard ends up in it. Pattern-noted.

## 2.2 The Acquisition of the Bow (approx. ages 16–19): Choosing the Weapon

The published record is firm on a point that ought to be examined more carefully than it usually is: Bernard Barton specialized in archery, not in firearms, not in knives, not in the full carnival omnibus of thrown and shot weapons. This was a *choice*, and in the cultural context of his formative years — postwar America awash in cheap, reliable, scope-equipped rifles — it was a *deliberately archaic* choice.

The bow is the slowest of marksman disciplines to master. It rewards obsessive daily practice on a scale that firearms simply do not require. A man who selects the bow as his primary expressive instrument is selecting an apparatus that will demand of him precisely the regimen of unrelenting repetition that his prior conditioning has already trained him to provide. He is, in other words, choosing the weapon that fits the shape of the wound. The bow is also the weapon that *looks* most impressive in a small ring — the visible draw, the long flight of the arrow, the audible thump in the target — and Bernard from this early period is already calibrating every choice to the witnessing eye.

Equipment: documented as a recurve in the carnival years, transitioning to a heavier draw-weight recurve and eventually to compound elements in the mercenary decades. He fletches his own arrows from this period onward. He sharpens his own broadheads. The bow-case in the back of his trailer is, by every late-period testimony, the only personal object he treats with anything resembling tenderness. Surveillance note: any operator forced into proximity should observe his handling of the case versus his handling of every other possession. The case gets the careful hand; people do not.

## 2.3 The Partnership with Duquesne (approx. ages 19–28): Confederacy of Equals

Jacques Duquesne — Swordsman — arrives in Bernard's life as the only person he will ever treat as a peer. The relationship spans, by best reconstruction from cross-referenced flashbacks, the better part of a decade of shared carnival residency. They share top billing. They share the back office. They share, eventually, the embezzlement scheme that will detonate the entire arrangement.

The dynamic is worth dissecting. Duquesne is older, more travelled, more cosmopolitan, more obviously dissipated — already drinking heavily by the time Bernard's act stabilizes — and Bernard, for the first and only time on record, accepts a position of secondary status without converting it into resentment. Why? Because Duquesne offers something the rest of the world does not: he sees Bernard's skill and *names it skill*, peer to peer. Recognition from an equal-or-superior craftsman is the one currency Bernard's organization can metabolize without distortion. The confederacy holds because each man satisfies the other's narcissistic supply: Duquesne is admired by a man whose admiration is rare, and Bernard is graded by a man whose grading he respects.

The shared corruption follows. Embezzlement from carnival receipts is not an opportunistic late development; the cross-referenced timeline suggests it begins relatively early in their partnership, escalating through their late twenties. The mechanism, inferable from fragmentary later dialogue: the gate take, the ring-toss take, the marksmanship-gallery take — small, daily skims, professionalized, never enough at any one event to draw scrutiny. They split the proceeds. Neither man develops expensive habits visible to the carnival management; the money goes into traveling-light caches, with Duquesne (the more dissipated) burning through his share faster than Bernard accumulates his.

This is the period in which Bernard's *operational style* consolidates. He learns to maintain a perfectly clean professional surface — punctual, sober during performance hours, technically flawless on the line — while running a parallel undermining beneath it. He learns that respectability is a costume worn over appetite. He learns that the audience that comes to watch him shoot is also the audience whose pockets are being lightened, and that the watching crowd's admiration coexists comfortably with their exploitation. This double-stance — performer-above and predator-beneath — is the architectural template for everything that follows in his mercenary career.

## 2.4 The Acquisition of the Barton Boys (approx. age 30): The Pedagogy Begins

The arrival at the carnival of the brothers Barton — Charles ("Barney") and Clinton, runaways from the wreckage of a brutal upbringing — provides Bernard with the first object on which he can practice the inheritance he has been carrying. The brothers are taken in jointly by Duquesne and Bernard; Duquesne tends to gravitate toward Barney; Bernard claims Clinton.

The choice of Clinton over Barney is diagnostic. Barney is older, harder, already partially shaped by his own father's violence, less malleable. Clinton is the more pliant clay — and Bernard, surveying the brothers, selects on exactly the criterion a man organized around shaping rather than relating would select on. He picks the one he can mold most completely. The boy will become, in the precise technical sense, a narcissistic extension: a second body in which Bernard's discipline can be reproduced, witnessed, and admired.

The pedagogy that follows is documented in considerable detail across the Hawkeye Vol.1 flashbacks and the Solo Avengers #1–4 extended sequences. The structural features:

- **The dawn drill.** Clinton is roused before sunrise. The first hour is form work without an arrow nocked — stance, draw, release into empty air, repeated until the muscles learn the gesture below the level of thought. Bernard counts under his breath. He does not praise. If the form drops, he corrects with a tap of a switch on the wrist or the back of the knee — never hard enough to mark, always hard enough to recalibrate.

- **The midday gallery.** Practice on standard carnival targets — balloons, plates, the spinning wheel. Bernard sets each exercise and walks away to other tasks; Clinton must complete a quota by a stated time. Failure to complete the quota results in a doubling of the next day's quota, not in verbal reprimand. Punishment is procedural, not affective. This is the first lesson Clinton absorbs about how love is metered: by silence and by load.

- **The evening exhibition.** Clinton is brought to the back of the marksmanship tent and made to shadow Bernard's performance — observing the choreography, the patter, the moment of dramatic pause. He is not yet allowed to shoot for an audience. Bernard's instruction during these sessions is, by the textual evidence, entirely technical: *the eye goes here, the breath goes there, the release is on the bottom of the exhale*. Affect is absent. The boy is being machined.

- **The metered praise.** The single recurring documented compliment, across multiple flashback panels, is the same phrase delivered in the same tone: a curt acknowledgment that the shot was acceptable. Anything beyond competence is met with raised standards, never with celebration. Clinton, by adolescence, has internalized that the absence of correction is the highest reward available, and he will spend his adult life seeking that exact economy from every subsequent authority figure he encounters — a transmission of pathology so clean it could be modeled on a blackboard.

- **The use of the older brother.** Barney is occasionally deployed by Bernard as a comparative goad — *your brother could do this at your age* (a falsehood; Barney was never given the rigorous instruction Clinton received). The triangulation is deliberate, and it begins the slow corrosion of the brothers' bond that will culminate, years later, in Barney's own betrayal of Clint.

Bernard, in this period, is approximately the age his own teacher would have been when he himself was the boy on the line. He is reproducing the conditional-regard economy with mechanical fidelity, and there is no evidence anywhere in the record that he experiences this as repetition. He experiences it as *correct*. This is the load-bearing fact of his interior life: cruelty has the texture, for him, of competence.

## 2.5 The Emergence of "Trick Shot" as Identity (approx. ages 28–33): The Alias Hardens

It is during the years of Clinton's apprenticeship that the alias *Trick Shot* — initially a billing, a marquee — completes its migration into Bernard's interior self-naming. Carnival roustabouts and fellow performers, by the late period of his Carson tenure, address him as Buck or as Trick more often than as Bernard. He answers to Trick without correction. He begins, in private correspondence (the few business letters preserved in cross-referenced carnival management files), to sign with the alias.

This is the period in which the name *Bernard Barton* becomes vestigial. The man who left whatever house he came from is now, operationally, the act. There is no off-duty self underneath. The bow is in his hand from dawn until performance, and when it is not in his hand it is being maintained, or its arrows are being fletched, or the next day's drill is being designed. Even the embezzlement is an act of performance — performed unseen, but performed.

The identity is now sealed against re-entry. Any later attempt — by Clint, by the rare interlocutor who tries to address him as a man rather than as a marksman — to reach behind the alias will encounter not resistance but absence. There is no longer a Bernard to address.

## 2.6 The Embezzlement Discovery and the Beating (approx. age 33–35): The Defining Rupture

The terminal event of the formative arc is the discovery by the protégé of the mentor's theft. The precise sequence, reconstructable from Hawkeye Vol.1 #4 and corroborating Solo Avengers flashbacks:

Clinton, by this period nearing the end of his adolescence and approaching the technical ceiling of carnival marksmanship, has begun to perform secondary acts in his own right. His access to the back office has increased; he runs errands, carries cash bags, observes the daily reconciliation. He notices, over a period of weeks, discrepancies between the gate count and the receipts. He notices Duquesne's after-hours visits to the cashbox. He notices, eventually, that Bernard is part of it.

The moment of confrontation is the hinge on which the entire dossier turns. Clinton — formed by Bernard into a creature whose only ethical primitive is the loyalty Bernard himself taught — applies that loyalty *to the carnival itself*, to the institution, to the management that pays them. He goes to the owners. He does not first approach Bernard; he does not negotiate; he does not warn. He reports.

This is the catastrophic discovery: that the boy Bernard shaped has come out of the shaping with a moral instrument that points back at his shaper. The narcissistic extension has asserted independent ethical judgment, and in doing so has done the one thing the narcissistic structure cannot tolerate — it has *exposed the self*.

Bernard's response is documented in granular detail. He does not flee. Duquesne flees; Bernard stays. He finds Clinton in the practice tent — the very space where the apprenticeship has been conducted — and he beats him. Not with the bow (the bow is sacred, the bow is not used as a club). With his fists, methodically, with the same technical care he brings to a draw. The beating is not a loss of control; it is a *demonstration*. The boy is being shown, on his own body, what disloyalty costs.

The accompanying verbal content, preserved in flashback dialogue across multiple issues: the framing is total. Bernard does not say *I stole and you caught me*. He says, in the recurring formulation, that *Clint* has betrayed *him* — that the report to management was the violation, that the theft is unmentioned because the theft is not, in Bernard's interior accounting, the morally salient event. The blame-externalization is not strategic. It is *sincere*. He believes it. This is the moment at which the diagnostic structure becomes legible: a man capable of standing over a beaten teenager and locating the wrong in the teenager is a man whose perspective-taking apparatus has been surgically removed.

He leaves Clint in the tent and disappears from the carnival. He does not collect his caches in any hurry; the published continuity suggests he walks out with the bow, a working kit, and nothing else of consequence. The cleanness of the departure is itself a tell — he has been ready to leave at any moment for years. The carnival was always a posting, not a home.

## 2.7 The Immediate Aftermath (approx. ages 35–38): The Emergence of the Mercenary

The years immediately following the rupture are the least documented in the canon, and the dossier must work largely by inference. What can be established:

Bernard does not return to legitimate performance. The carnival circuit is small, blacklists travel, and a marksman with his profile would have been identifiable on any other midway within months. He moves instead into the adjacent shadow economy where his skill is monetizable without the burden of a billed identity: contract work. Initial assignments, reconstructable from his later professional reputation, are small — intimidation shots, property destruction, the occasional non-lethal wounding for collection enforcement. He works regionally, then nationally, building a reputation in criminal-procurement circles as a marksman who can be hired for jobs that require the specific impossible-looking accuracy of his particular instrument.

The bow is, in this market, a *signature*. A man who can be reliably identified by the weapon he uses is, in most contract work, a liability; in Bernard's case it becomes a brand. The arrow at the scene is the calling card. The clients who hire him are paying, in part, for the theatre of it — the message conveyed by the choice of weapon. He is, even in criminal anonymity, still performing for an audience.

In this period the second great consolidation of his identity occurs: he is no longer the carnival marksman, he is the *professional*, and the professionalism becomes the new performance. The discipline that was once organized around the dawn drill is now organized around the reconnaissance, the firing position, the egress. The structure of his day is unchanged in its rigor; only the targets have changed.

## 2.8 The First Re-Approach to Clinton (approx. age 38–40): The Compulsion Surfaces

Within several years of the rupture — the canonical sequence is fuzzy but the cross-referenced timeline suggests no more than a half-decade gap — Bernard accepts his first contract that brings him into direct opposition with Clinton Barton, now operating publicly as Hawkeye. The contract is, in surface terms, mercenary: a client wants Hawkeye neutralized, Bernard is the marksman most plausibly equipped to do it.

But the structural reading is unavoidable. Bernard *accepts* the contract. He could have declined; marksmen of his caliber have the standing to refuse particular jobs. He takes it. And in every subsequent appearance across the next four decades of publication, whenever the option to target Clint arises he takes it again. The mercenary frame is a fig leaf over a compulsion: he is repeatedly returning to the site of his single defining narcissistic injury, attempting to resolve through dominance what he cannot resolve through any other available mechanism.

The first encounter — the inaugural reappearance — establishes the template for every subsequent reappearance: Bernard frames himself as the wronged party, demands that Clint acknowledge it, attempts to demonstrate his superiority via the bow, and departs (either by Clint's escape or his own withdrawal) without the resolution he is seeking because the resolution he is seeking is structurally impossible. He wants Clint to concede that the beating was deserved. Clint, having grown into a man with his own functioning conscience, cannot concede it. The loop is permanent. The formative arc closes here, and the rest of the life is the loop.

---

## 2.9 Synthesis of the Formative Period

By approximately age 40 the architecture is complete and will not meaningfully change for the remaining decades of his life. The constituent elements, set in the period documented above:

- A pre-carnival origin liquidated so thoroughly that even the subject seems no longer to access it, leaving the inheritance of conditional-regard pedagogy as the only legible trace of whatever shaped him before he shaped himself.
- A weapon chosen for its archaic difficulty, suiting a temperament already trained to find selfhood in unrelenting repetition.
- An identity consolidated around being witnessed performing the impossible — the alias *Trick Shot* foregrounding spectacle, the carnival foregrounding audience, the later mercenary career preserving both via the signature arrow.
- A single confederate-equal relationship (Duquesne) that establishes the lifelong template of double-stance — clean surface, corrupt undercurrent — and that ends without rancor on Bernard's side because Duquesne never exposed him.
- A single shaped-protégé relationship (Clinton) that establishes the lifelong template of conditional-regard pedagogy, narcissistic extension, and unforgivable rupture upon the extension's assertion of independent moral judgment.
- A defining moment of exposure — the embezzlement caught by the boy he made — to which his response is methodical violence framed as just response to betrayal, executed without subsequent revision in his own accounting across the rest of his life.
- A post-rupture professionalization in which the same disciplined daily structure is preserved while the social context is stripped away, leaving the man alone with the bow and the next contract.
- A compulsion to return — under mercenary cover — to the only relationship that ever achieved the depth required to wound him, which is also the only relationship he is constitutionally incapable of repairing.

What the formative period produces, in short, is a man who has been so completely organized around a single perishable skill and a single unresolvable injury that the remainder of his life will be a forty-year exercise in defending both. The body will age. The skill will eventually erode. The injury will not. When the body fails — and the late-period cancer is the event in which it does — the only remaining theatre for the unresolved injury will be the deathbed, and the only audience available will be, as it has always been, the boy he made and lost.

The formative arc, in this sense, does not end. It is the only thing he has, and he will spend the rest of the dossier replaying it.

— END SECTION 2 —


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

*Subject: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON, alias TRICK SHOT*
*Period bracket: approx. the decade-and-a-half following the Carson Carnival abandonment through the late mercenary years preceding terminal diagnosis. The bulk of the longitudinal record.*

---

## 6.1 The Interregnum (Post-Carnival, Pre-Mercenary)

The first eighteen to thirty months after Buck walked away from the beaten Barton boy in the Iowa carnival lot are the least documented and most behaviorally diagnostic stretch in his entire record. The canon shows him absent; the surveillance file must reconstruct him from the shape of his absence.

What is known by inference and by his own later, oblique admissions during West Coast Avengers-era confrontations:

- He did **not** flee far. Carson Carnival's circuit ran the upper Midwest and the river towns; Buck's subsequent emergence in St. Louis, Kansas City, and the Gulf Coast carnival-and-club circuit suggests he stayed inside the same ecology — county fairs, sideshow exhibitions, paid trick-shooting demonstrations at sporting-goods openings, the occasional bonded-bow contest in the South. He was, in this period, still **professionally an entertainer** rather than a contractor.
- He did **not** seek out Clint or Barney. There is no record — not a postcard, not a back-channel inquiry through Carson regulars — of him attempting to track either Barton boy during the years they were vulnerable to him. This is structurally significant: the later compulsive return to Clint did not begin as longing; it began only after Clint became *visible* (the Hawkeye costume, the public arrests, the Avengers reserve roster). Buck's interest in his protégé is a function of the protégé's audience. Out of sight, out of his cosmology.
- He drank more in this period. Multiple second-hand carnival reports (the Carson roustabout testimonies Gruenwald draws on indirectly in the Hawkeye limited; a passing remark by an unnamed strongman in Solo Avengers #2) place Buck at the bar earlier and stay longer than during the Swordsman partnership years. The alcohol use is not yet operationally degrading — his shot is intact — but the *baseline irritability* worsens, and a recurring tell appears for the first time: the slow, deliberate dry-fire pull of an unstrung bow when agitated, performed unconsciously while talking. He does this for the rest of his life.
- The **partnership with Jacques Duquesne dissolves** in this period, but not via rupture — via drift. The Swordsman is a bigger personality, a more flamboyant criminal appetite; Buck's narcissism cannot survive long in the gravitational field of another, larger one. They part, by all accounts, civilly, with the understanding that they will not work the same towns. Buck never speaks of Duquesne with the venom he reserves for Clint, which is its own diagnostic point: the equal who left is forgiven; the inferior who exposed is not.

The interregnum closes when Buck takes his first explicitly criminal contract — a bonded courier-killing in the Texas panhandle, paid in cash by an unrecorded employer, executed at one hundred and twelve yards across an open rail yard at dusk. The shot is clean, the body unidentified for nine days, and the file (such as it is) attributes the kill to "an unknown rifleman" because no investigating officer of the period imagines an arrow. **This is the operational birth of Trick Shot the assassin.** The carnival name is carried over wholesale, which is itself revealing: he does not change handles when he changes professions. The brand is the man; the audience is what shifts.

---

## 6.2 Operational Maturation — The Contract Years

Across the middle decade, Buck assembles the working repertoire of a sole-operator marksman-for-hire. The file can reconstruct it with unusual precision because his methods are signature-bearing and he does not vary them.

**Tooling.** He maintains, throughout this period, three working bows and never more than three:

1. A heavy recurve, draw weight in the 70-lb range, used for distance work and any shot requiring barrier penetration.
2. A faster, lighter recurve for urban work where a draw must be completed in under two seconds from a slung carry.
3. A take-down compound, acquired sometime in the middle of the period (the compound becomes commercially mature in the early 1970s; Buck adopts it later than enthusiasts, earlier than traditionalists — pragmatic, not ideological). The compound is for over-watch positions where he expects to wait hours.

He fletches his own arrows. He does not deviate from this practice once across the entire period. The fletching pattern — three feathers, one cock feather dyed a specific shade of dark red — becomes a recoverable forensic signature in three jurisdictions before he switches to a plain-fletch model after a near-arrest in Mobile in approximately the eighth year of the period. The switch is not contrition; it is craft discipline. He is annoyed at himself for the vanity.

**Pricing.** He does not bid low. He prices himself in the upper quartile of contract specialists for the era and refuses negotiation. Subjects who haggle are subjects he later refuses to work for again, and the refusal is communicated through a single dry-fire dummy arrow delivered by mail. This is theatrical; it is also effective; intermediaries learn not to push him.

**Refusal pattern.** He turns down: contracts on children (consistent across every documented decision point); contracts requiring close-quarters work (he will not work inside fifteen yards if avoidable — a tell of the marksman's preference for the dignified distance, but also of a subject who needs the geometry of the shot to mediate the act); contracts requiring the subject to be tortured or to suffer visibly before death (this is **not** mercy — it is aesthetic. He wants the shot to be the event. Suffering is messy, and mess is a kind of failure).

**Acceptance pattern.** He takes: distance assassinations; demonstration-of-force shootings (a witness left alive to describe the impossibility of the shot); intimidation displays (an arrow through a specific object at a specific distance, witnessed); and, increasingly toward the second half of the period, contracts where the target is himself a skilled operator. The last category is the warning sign. **He begins, somewhere in the middle of the decade, to select for difficulty over money.** When the file flags this shift, the trajectory toward Clint becomes legible in retrospect: he is, well before consciously naming it, training his appetite back toward the only target who would constitute the supreme demonstration.

---

## 6.3 Alliances of Convenience

Buck is not a joiner. The middle period contains no documented attempt at sustained affiliation with any organized criminal enterprise — no Maggia handler, no HYDRA flirtation, no Roxxon retainer. This is consistent with the narcissistic structure: a hierarchy he does not sit atop is a hierarchy he cannot tolerate.

He does, however, accumulate a small network of **recurring confederates**, each managed at arm's length, each treated as instrumentally subordinate, none ever invited into a stable partnership of the kind he briefly had with Duquesne.

- **William Cross / Crossfire** — the most documented of these affiliations. Crossfire's audial-manipulation rackets occasionally require precision elimination work, and Buck takes the contracts repeatedly over a span of several years. The relationship is mutually contemptuous and operationally durable: Crossfire considers Buck a tool; Buck considers Crossfire a paymaster with delusions. Neither is wrong. Importantly, **Crossfire is the conduit through which the first direct contract against Clint is brokered.** Buck does not seek the contract; Crossfire offers it, sensing — correctly — that the personal angle will lower the price. Buck accepts at standard rate, not discounted, because to accept at discount would be to admit the personal angle exists. This is the first time the surveillance record catches him *lying to himself in the act of pricing*.
- A handful of **rural fixers** in the river-town corridor who supply lodging, false identification, and bow-storage. He pays these men on time, in cash, and never asks them their business. They reciprocate. He is, in this narrow operational respect, a model client — a fact that should not be read as virtue. It is the carnival professionalism preserved; the same etiquette that governed the back-lot in his Carson years governs his back-channel logistics now.
- A **woman in Memphis** — unnamed in canon, glimpsed once in a Solo Avengers backgrounder — with whom he maintains an intermittent domestic arrangement of indeterminate duration. She is not a partner; she is a safe house with a kitchen. He is observed (by Clint, briefly, much later) to be courteous to her, even gentle in his sparing way, and to leave without warning whenever a contract or a mood takes him. She does not ask when he is coming back. The relationship's significance to the file is what it confirms: he is **capable** of low-intensity, non-demanding attachment when no performance is required of him and no audience is watching. The capacity exists; it is simply not where he routes his life-force.

---

## 6.4 The Clint Engagements

The middle period contains the long sequence of confrontations with the protégé that defines, more than any other vector, his eventual psychiatric trajectory. The file logs at least four discrete operational engagements during these years (the count varies by retcon; the structural pattern does not).

**Engagement One — the first contracted hunt.** Buck accepts the Crossfire-brokered contract and stalks Clint across three states. He could end it on day two — he has, by his own later admission, a clear shot at one hundred and forty yards on a hotel balcony in Cincinnati and does not take it. He waits. He extends the engagement to seven days. The file reads this, correctly, as not hesitation but **theater**: he wants the confrontation, not the kill. When the resolution comes, it comes in dialogue — Buck announcing himself, Clint recognizing him, an exchange of shots that ends in Buck's withdrawal under conditions he describes to himself as tactical and which were in fact emotional. He has been **out-shot at a critical moment**, and the file flags this as the first documented instance of the pressure point identified in §5: skill-superiority by the protégé produces composure failure. He leaves bleeding, furious, and re-narrating.

**Engagement Two — the punitive return.** Approximately eighteen months later. Not contracted; self-financed. He hunts Clint to West Coast Avengers operations in the desert. This time he wants the kill and is denied it by circumstance — a third-party intervention (the file's reconstructions vary on whether this is Mockingbird, Wonder Man, or an unaffiliated bystander). What matters: Buck retreats again, and this time, in the retreat, he is observed to be **muttering** — a previously undocumented behavior, audible to a single witness who reports it. The muttering is described as one-sided dialogue, conducted in the second person, addressed to an absent Clint. The verbal content is unrecoverable; the structural fact is enormous. He has, by this point, **internalized the protégé as a persecutory object he speaks to**. The relationship is no longer external. He carries Clint with him.

**Engagement Three — the teaching ambush.** Mid-late period. He takes Clint alive, briefly, in an upstate New York warehouse — a feat of preparation that involves three weeks of observation, two false-flag contracts arranged through Crossfire to bait the geography, and a non-lethal trap involving a high-tension line. He has Clint disarmed and bound for somewhere between six and nine hours. He does not torture; he **lectures**. He goes through the technical errors he has observed in Clint's archery over the prior engagements — grip drift, anchor inconsistency, the tell in the left shoulder before a long shot — corrects them verbally, demonstrates with Clint's own bow, and then leaves him alive and unbound at the conclusion. The file flags this as **the most psychiatrically revealing single event in his entire middle period.** It is not mercy. It is not reconciliation. It is the resurrection of the pedagogical economy under conditions where the pupil cannot refuse. He needs Clint to receive the instruction; he needs the instruction to land; and he needs to walk out without acknowledging that needing this is the wound. The blame-externalization machinery hums throughout — at no point does he raise the embezzlement, the beating, the abandonment. In his cognitive map, those events have been so completely re-narrated as Clint's failure that they are not available to consciousness as topics.

**Engagement Four — the equal-footing duel.** Late in the period, public, witnessed, on terms approximating a formal contest. Crowd present (peripheral civilians; the audience matters). Buck loses cleanly, by a margin that cannot be reframed. The file records what happens in his face in the moment of the loss: a flatness, then a tight smile, then immediate withdrawal. He does not retaliate. He does not lash out. He **disappears for approximately fourteen months**, the longest operational silence of his career. When he resurfaces, his shooting is technically unchanged but his contract acceptance pattern has shifted again — he is now selecting almost exclusively for high-difficulty, high-witness work, and his asking prices have climbed by a factor near two. The file reads this as **status repair behavior**: having been beaten in public, he must rebuild the audience-self with louder, costlier demonstrations. He is, in clinical terms, compensating against a narcissistic injury he cannot consciously name.

---

## 6.5 The Quiet Erosions

Across these same years, slower than the engagements but more important to the eventual terminal trajectory, the somatic and behavioral baselines drift.

- **The drinking** consolidates from intermittent heavy use into a daily floor — two to four ounces of bourbon by midday, more in the evening, throttled back hard during operations and resumed immediately after. He never drinks during a contract; he drinks before discussing one and after completing one. The pattern is functional and disguised; it is also progressive.
- **The dry-fire tic** intensifies and migrates. Originally bow-only, by the middle of the period he performs an abbreviated version with empty hands — a slow draw-and-release pantomime, two fingers under an imagined string — when listening to someone he intends to disregard. Confederates learn to read it as a refusal signal before he has spoken.
- **Sleep** worsens. Multiple safe-house keepers note he keeps the light on; one Memphis report places him reading sporting magazines at three in the morning, sober, sitting upright in a chair rather than in the bed. The file infers — without canon's direct testimony — that the protégé-as-persecutory-object has begun to disrupt rest. He does not have the introspective vocabulary to name this, and so he does not pursue remediation.
- **The grooming** sharpens rather than degrades. This is counterintuitive and diagnostic. A man whose internal life is fraying often disorganizes externally; Buck does the inverse. His mustache becomes more precise across the period, the shave closer, the boots more consistently polished. He is **defending the visible surface** because the invisible interior is the problem. The carnival principle holds: be seen to be the master.
- **Reading habits.** He acquires, in the second half of the period, the unlikely habit of reading military history — specifically siege warfare and pre-firearm projectile campaigns. He does not discuss this with anyone. Books are found in his effects. The interest is consonant with the worldview: the great archer-armies, the long siege, the demonstration of impossible range. He is, in his private hours, locating himself in a lineage in which he matters.
- **The audience requirement** narrows and deepens. Early in the period he performs for crowds (county-fair demonstrations, the residual carnival work that subsidized the contract income). Mid-period the crowds fall away as the contracts pay more, and his felt need for audience does not diminish — it **transfers onto a single recipient**, Clint, who must witness, must receive instruction, must be the mirror. By the end of the period the protégé is structurally the only audience that counts. This is the soil from which the late-life deathbed staging will grow. The middle period is where it is planted.

---

## 6.6 Pattern Synthesis for the Period

The defining middle period is the stretch in which Bernard Barton becomes, irreversibly, the man the late canon will find on his deathbed. The operational craft matures; the criminal identity consolidates; the alliances of convenience accrete and stay shallow; the body holds; the drinking and the sleep degrade in slow parallel; and, most importantly, the relationship to the abandoned protégé moves through its full developmental sequence — from absent (interregnum), to contracted (engagement one), to compulsive (engagement two), to pedagogically re-enacted (engagement three), to publicly defeated and silently restructured (engagement four).

The middle period is the answer to a question the early canon does not ask: *how does the harsh mentor of the flashback become the man who summons his protégé to choreograph his own dying?* The answer the file constructs is that he does it by inches, across fifteen years, in safe houses and rail yards and one warehouse in upstate New York, while polishing his boots and fletching his arrows and not, ever, naming aloud the thing that is happening to him. The defense holds; the man it defends erodes underneath it; and the bow, throughout, does the feeling he will not.

— END CHRONOLOGY III —


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

*Subject: Bernard "Buck" Barton, alias Trick Shot. Period under review: approximately the last ten to twelve years of recorded existence, terminating at present-status assessment.*

---

## 4.1 Entry into the recent era: the long quiet, and what broke it

The decade preceding the current file opens with Subject in a state best characterized as **operational dormancy with reputational residue**. After the West Coast contracts (in which he repeatedly took paid work against his former protégé, was repeatedly defeated, and was repeatedly released rather than killed — a forbearance he registered as further humiliation, not mercy), Subject withdrew from the higher-visibility mercenary market. Contributing factors, in order of weight as derived from the behavioral record:

1. **Market displacement.** The high-end marksman niche he had occupied in the 1980s–1990s was eaten from below by augmented operatives (cybernetic targeting, smart-munitions specialists, enhanced-sense actors) and from above by the post-Registration security state's appetite for credentialed contractors. A man whose entire selling proposition was *unenhanced human precision* found his price collapsing precisely as his body began to require that price to rise.

2. **Skeletomuscular attrition.** Surveillance of his physical bearing across this period — gait, draw-arm carriage, the increasing favor of the left shoulder when carrying weight — indicates the early chronic phase of what would later become diagnosable disease. The body was telling him before the doctors did. He responded characteristically: by drilling harder, in greater isolation, and refusing all collateral medical contact that might produce a written finding.

3. **The protégé's escalating public profile.** Through the recent era, Clinton Barton's visibility — Avengers tenure, the Hawkeye street-level run with Bishop, the deafness arc, the eventual semi-retirement to mentor — moved from "famous superhero" to "cultural fixture with a specific narrative of damage." Subject's name began to appear, unprompted, in interview profiles and journalistic backgrounders about that damage. He was, against his will, being **historicized as someone's wound**. The dossier records — through proxies, second-hand quotes from carnival old-timers, one bartender deposition out of a Bowling Green roadhouse — a consistent reaction pattern: a tightening at the jaw, a single dismissive syllable, and a refusal to discuss. The refusal is itself diagnostic. A man indifferent to the narrative would refuse without tightening.

## 4.2 The dormancy: where and how he lived

For roughly the middle stretch of this recent period, Subject occupied what surveillance would classify as a **low-signature itinerant pattern**. No fixed long-term residence longer than nine to fourteen months. Preferred locations:

- **Small-market towns within a day's drive of regional fairground circuits.** Iowa, Missouri, southern Illinois, the Texas panhandle, the Florida panhandle. He gravitated, with a regularity that reads as homing behavior, to the geographic-cultural footprint of the dying American travelling-show economy. He did not rejoin a carnival — his pride forbade it — but he lived adjacent to one, the way some retired clergy live adjacent to seminaries.
- **Rented rooms above businesses rather than apartments proper.** Above feed stores, above bars, once above a gunsmith. Pattern indicates a man who wants a single exit, a single stair, a single set of footsteps to memorize, and no neighbors with whom he might be required to exchange greeting.
- **Cash economy almost exclusively.** Two known bank accounts, both under variations of his legal name, both used for paper-trail purposes (vehicle registration, the occasional mail order of fletching supplies from a Wisconsin specialty shop he has patronized since the late 1970s). The operational money — instruction fees, side contracts, a steady trickle of payment from one or two collectors who buy custom-made trick arrows as curios — moves in envelopes.

Daily structure, reconstructed from the bartender deposition, two motel-clerk interviews, and a tail-surveillance summary from a 72-hour observation conducted by an interested third party (file appended elsewhere):

- **Pre-dawn rising.** 0430–0500. Coffee, black, no food. A consistent observation across every site of residence.
- **Physical maintenance, 0500–0700.** Calisthenics of an obsolete idiom — the floor work of a 1950s carnival strongman crossed with the isometric drills of a Korean-War-era infantry manual. He has never, to the record's knowledge, set foot in a modern gym.
- **Practice, 0700–1100.** This is the immovable core of his day. Wherever he goes, his first task is to find or build a range. Documented improvisations include a stripped tobacco barn in Kentucky, a drained irrigation canal in the Imperial Valley, and — most tellingly — a rented self-storage unit in which he had hung a target on the back wall and shot the length of the unit, twenty-eight feet, ten thousand arrows at twenty-eight feet, because that was what the space allowed and the space was what he could afford.
- **Midday lull, 1100–1500.** Reading (Westerns, military memoirs, a surprising and consistent appetite for accounts of failed polar expeditions — Shackleton, Franklin, Mawson — which warrants its own footnote: he is drawn to narratives of small parties of disciplined men destroyed by an environment indifferent to their skill). Newspapers, never television. He owns no smartphone of his own; he carries, for emergencies, a prepaid flip device replaced every four to six months.
- **Afternoon: instruction or income work, 1500–1800.** During this dormant period he taught — privately, by referral, never advertised. Students were typically the children of carnival or competition-circuit acquaintances, occasionally a wealthy hobbyist who had been routed to him through one of two intermediaries. Lesson fees were high, lessons were brutal, the dropout rate exceeded eighty percent, and the small minority of students who lasted longer than three months were the only humans in this period to whom he gave anything resembling sustained attention.
- **Evening: a bar, 1900–2200.** Always the same bar in any given town. He drank — and this is consistent across the entire dormant period — bourbon, two fingers, with a single ice cube, at a pace of roughly one per hour, rarely exceeding three. He has been observed to nurse the third for ninety minutes. He is not a drunk in any clinical sense. He is a man who uses alcohol as a metronome to mark the end of the day, and who has learned across decades to dose it so that the metronome never overshoots.
- **Lights out by 2230.** Sleeps with the door chain on, the bow case within reach of the dominant hand, and — a habit dating to the carnival years — a single arrow nocked but unsecured beside the case. He has never, to the record's knowledge, drawn it in the night. The ritual is its own reassurance.

## 4.3 The diagnosis

The terminal-cancer finding lands within this period, approximately twenty-six to thirty-two months prior to current status. Reconstructed timeline:

- **Symptom onset:** weight loss across two seasons; persistent cough his bar associates noted before he did; a noticeable tremor in the off-hand which he masked by keeping the off-hand in a pocket or wrapped around a glass.
- **First medical contact:** a county clinic in a town he was about to leave anyway, paid in cash, registered under a partial alias. The clinician routed him to a regional oncology unit; he did not attend the appointment.
