- **Second medical contact, approximately four months later:** an emergency-room admission for a syncopal episode that put him on a gurney in front of strangers — an indignity the file should note he has spoken of, to two separate people, with disproportionate bitterness. The hospital extracted the diagnosis from him in the corridor of his own collapse. He left against medical advice within nineteen hours.
- **Third medical contact, ongoing:** a private oncologist in a small city he has identified as his terminal base, seen approximately every six weeks, paid partly in cash and partly through a thin insurance instrument acquired late and at cost. The oncologist's prognosis, as Subject has paraphrased it to one of his last students, is "less than is comfortable, more than is convenient" — a phrasing too composed to be the doctor's, which indicates Subject has rehearsed it for delivery.

The pathological response to the diagnosis is the central event of the recent era and is consistent with the psychological organization mapped in §3. He did not:

- Seek reconciliation with surviving family of origin (no contact attempted with any party traceable to his pre-carnival history; if such family exists, he has not approached it).
- Seek reconciliation with any past lover, of which the record contains glancing reference to two and rumored reference to a third.
- Withdraw to comfort, contemplation, or affiliative companionship.
- Drink more.
- Drink less.
- Pray, by any observable indicator.

He did:

- Increase practice volume by an estimated thirty to forty percent, despite physical decline, producing in the short term a *measurable improvement* in grouping at maximum effective range — a final, brittle peak before the body's collapse.
- Begin compiling, in a series of cheap composition notebooks, what one student has described as "his book" — handwritten, in pencil, technical: a treatise on the bow as he understands it. The notebooks are not memoir. They contain almost no personal material. They are pedagogy, drill sequences, range estimation tables for various bow weights, and a long, idiosyncratic taxonomy of *failure modes* — every way a shot can be lost, classified by error type, with annotated remedies. The man cannot write his life; he can write the inside of his discipline. This is the only autobiography of him that will exist, and it is in the form of a manual.
- Initiate the search for a successor.

## 4.4 The successor protocol

The search began approximately twenty months ago and has proceeded in two parallel tracks, both characteristically self-deceiving.

**Track A — the ostensible heir.** Subject identified, vetted, and began intensive instruction of a candidate to whom the *Trick Shot* identity could be transferred. The candidate's profile, as reconstructed: late teens to early twenties, raw competition-archery talent, a difficult family background that produced both the hunger and the deference Subject requires of a student, and — critically — *no prior knowledge of Clint Barton*. The last criterion is non-negotiable in Subject's vetting and is, on its face, presented as practical (no contamination of loyalty) but is in fact protective of Subject's narrative (the new student will only ever hear Subject's version of the protégé story, and will only ever hear it on Subject's terms). The training of this heir follows the precise template applied to Clint forty years prior — withholding of praise, relentless physical demand, affection metered as a function of performance — with one observed alteration: the punishments are verbal rather than physical, because Subject's body can no longer reliably back the threats his mouth still issues.

**Track B — the true terminus.** In parallel, and with greater secrecy, Subject has been managing the conditions of a final meeting with Clinton Barton. The instruments of this management include: a sequence of three indirect messages routed through old carnival contacts, each ambiguously phrased so that Subject preserves deniability if Clint does not respond; a calibrated leak to a third party known to be in periodic contact with the Bishop-Barton operational circle, ensuring that Subject's location, illness, and ostensible "search for an heir" became information Clint would receive whether he sought it or not; and the slow consolidation of Subject's effects in a single location — the small-city apartment now functioning as terminal base — so that whoever arrives, arrives at a *prepared room*.

The convergence of Tracks A and B is the entire point. Subject intends — and this can be asserted with confidence from the behavioral pattern, even where intent is unstated — to stage a final tableau in which the protégé he abandoned and the protégé he is grooming are present together, and in which his death is choreographed as a transfer of authority that Clint is forced to witness or to interrupt. There is no version of the staging in which Subject is not the figure on whom all attention converges. The deathbed is the last carnival stage he will build.

## 4.5 Current somatic status

At present-status assessment, Subject's body is in advanced but not yet immediately terminal decline. Specifics, where derivable:

- **Weight loss:** an estimated eighteen to twenty-four percent below his stable adult baseline.
- **Skin:** the dry, papery quality of treatment-side effects; visible jaundice intermittently noted but not constant, suggesting hepatic involvement that fluctuates.
- **Hair:** unchanged in distribution (he never had much to lose), but coarser and whiter than two years ago by photographic comparison.
- **Eyes:** *the eyes remain.* This is the diagnostically critical observation. Visual acuity at distance, by every behavioral indicator, has not meaningfully degraded. He still threads a shot at ranges that most healthy contemporaries cannot. The eyes are the last system to fail, and he is aware that when they fail he is finished, and he intends to be dead before they fail.
- **Hands:** the tremor he masked is now present at rest in the off-hand and intermittent in the draw hand. He has compensated by shortening his drills, increasing rest intervals, and — a small but telling adjustment — switching to a heavier arrow which forgives slight inconsistencies in release.
- **Pain management:** he refuses opioid prescription beyond a minimal threshold, on the explicit ground that he will not shoot impaired. He has accepted a limited regimen of non-sedating analgesics and supplements it with the bourbon-metronome, now perhaps one finger heavier per pour than in the dormant years.
- **Sleep:** poor, fragmented, with the dominant-hand arrow still nocked beside the case.

## 4.6 Current operational and behavioral status

He is, at present, simultaneously:

- **Teaching daily.** Five to six hours of instruction with the heir candidate, on a range he has built behind the rented house in which he now resides. The range is a converted hay-shed with a packed-earth floor; the targets are repainted weekly by the student as part of the disciplinary ritual.
- **Writing nightly.** The notebooks have grown to a count of seven, filling steadily. He has made no provision for their preservation. They will go where his effects go, and what happens to his effects is part of the staging.
- **Monitoring his protégé's life at a distance.** Subscriptions to two newspapers that occasionally carry Avengers-related coverage; a folder of clippings in a drawer; one observed instance of asking a bar associate, with studied casualness, whether "the deaf one is still working." This was the only documented occasion in the recent period on which he acknowledged the existence of Clint Barton in public speech. The studied casualness is the giveaway.
- **Refusing all overtures of repair.** A documented instance approximately seven months ago: an intermediary, having pieced together Subject's circumstances, attempted to convey a message of unspecified content from the Hawkeye party. Subject's response, per the intermediary's debrief, was to listen in silence, finish his drink, set the glass down with exaggerated care, and say one sentence — content not recorded, tone described as "almost amused, like he'd been waiting for the joke to land." He did not reply to the message. He noted it. He factored it into the staging.
- **Awaiting.** This is the most accurate description of his current state. He is not seeking, not pursuing, not closing distance. He has finished his preparations and is now in the period of a hunter at a stand: stillness, patience, conservation of the energy that will be required for the single action at the end.

## 4.7 How he got here: the through-line

The path from the West Coast contracts to the rented hay-shed range is, in retrospect, perfectly continuous. There is no rupture, no conversion, no late mellowing. The man who beat a child for exposing his theft and the man who is now choreographing his own death as a final lesson are the same man at the same work. The work is the management of how he is seen. In youth he managed it by being the best shot in the tent. In middle age he managed it by hunting the protégé who had seen him at less than his best. In the dormant years he managed it by withdrawing from any audience that might catch him in decline. And in the terminal period he is managing it by *constructing the final audience himself* — selecting its members, scripting its arrival, ensuring that the last image of him in the world is the image he has chosen.

The cancer did not change him. It removed the time within which his organization had previously been able to defer its own resolution. He is doing now, under pressure, what he has been doing all along, more visibly because the deadline is real.

## 4.8 Forward projection (six to eighteen months)

Three scenarios, in descending order of probability as derived from the behavioral record:

1. **The staged terminus.** Within twelve months, Subject succeeds in summoning Clint Barton to the rented base, ideally with the heir candidate present. He attempts to compel Clint into a shooting contest, a final-instruction tableau, or — in the most pathological variant — a coup-de-grâce delivered by Clint's hand. The staging is designed so that any outcome (Clint refuses; Clint shoots; Clint weeps; Clint walks out) becomes data the staging itself can absorb as confirmation of Subject's narrative. There is no clean exit from the room he has built. (Probability: high.)
- *Note for operators*: if a Hawkeye-party intervention is contemplated, the operational error to avoid is treating the encounter as a negotiation. There is no offer that defuses the staging because the staging is the man. The only intervention that does not feed the pathology is one in which Subject is denied the audience — i.e., Clint does not come, the heir is removed from access, and Subject is left to die in the empty room he prepared. This is the maximally painful outcome for Subject and arguably the only one in which the wound is not transmitted forward.

2. **The premature collapse.** Subject's body fails before the staging completes. He dies in a hospital bed against his will, or alone in the rented house found by the heir at the next morning's lesson. In this scenario the notebooks survive him; the heir inherits the alias by default rather than by ceremony; the staging miscarries. Subject would consider this the worst outcome. (Probability: moderate.)

3. **The reversion to contract.** A late, financially-motivated return to mercenary work — a final paid kill, taken less for the money than for the audience of having done it. This would require a client willing to commission a visibly dying man, which is not impossible in the current market. (Probability: low but non-trivial; flag for continued monitoring.)

## 4.9 Current status, in one line

A man who has spent his life arranging to be watched is, at present, sitting very still in a small house he has chosen, with a bow within reach and a notebook on the table, waiting for the person he most wronged to walk through a door he has left specifically unlocked.

— END SECTION —


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON (alias TRICK SHOT)

*File Section 2 of 7. Compiled from carnival medical records (Carson Carnival of Travelling Wonders, partial), reconstructed combat injury logs, mercenary-circuit infirmary notes, two oncology consultations, and longitudinal behavioral observation. Where direct record is absent, inferences are flagged and substantiated.*

---

## 2.1 BASELINE SOMATIC ARCHITECTURE

The subject presents, across the full longitudinal record, as a Caucasian male of approximately six feet, lean-mesomorphic build, weight oscillating in a narrow band between 175 and 190 lbs across four decades — a stability indicative of a man whose body is a tool he refuses to permit drift in. No documented enhancements. No serum exposures, no mutagenic incidents, no cybernetic augmentation, no exotic radiation in the file. This is an unenhanced human operating at the ninety-ninth percentile of unenhanced human visual-motor performance, and the cost of that operation is etched into every system in the body.

**Resting heart rate** (carnival medic notation, approximate, mid-career): 48–52 bpm. **Resting respiratory rate**: 12. **Tested visual acuity** (carnival optometry, repeated over years): 20/10 right, 20/12 left, with above-average dynamic acuity and an exceptional vergence/accommodation reserve — the eyes track and re-focus faster than population norm by a measurable margin. This is partly congenital gift (the carnival files note he was "always able to see the wire from the cheap seats"), partly the consequence of forty years of daily aim-point drill. **Handedness**: right. **Ocular dominance**: right, strongly — verified by the consistency of his anchor and the asymmetry of facial musculature observed in late-career photographs (the right orbicularis oculi is slightly more developed, the right brow sits a quarter-centimeter lower from a lifetime of micro-squint at the sighting moment).

**Body composition**, inferred: body fat low (8–11%), muscle mass concentrated in posterior chain, scapular stabilizers (rhomboids, mid- and lower-trapezius), the right latissimus, and the forearm flexor-extensor groups bilaterally. The bow asymmetry — draw side versus bow side — would, in most archers, produce a visible imbalance; in Barton the imbalance is *present but disciplined down*, the bow-side musculature deliberately conditioned to match, which suggests an unusual degree of self-correcting attention to the body as instrument. Vanity in service of function; function in service of identity.

**Skeletal**: dense, slightly enlarged glenohumeral joint on the draw side; calcified entheses at the medial epicondyle, bilaterally, consistent with decades of high-rep tendon loading.

---

## 2.2 THE EYES (PRIMARY ORGAN OF SELFHOOD)

A normal medical history files vision under "screening." For this subject, the eyes warrant their own subsection — they are the seat of his profession, his identity, and ultimately the territory across which his decline will be experienced as personal annihilation.

Early career: documented acuity as above. **Color discrimination**: normal. **Stereopsis**: superior, Randot at 20 seconds of arc or better. **Contrast sensitivity**: elevated across the spatial frequency range, with notable preservation at low-light scotopic conditions — relevant for the carnival shows performed under inconsistent rigging and the later mercenary work taken in non-ideal light.

Mid-career (estimated mid-forties): early presbyopia onset, met not with corrective lenses but with **a systematic recalibration of his shooting mechanic** — bringing the bow closer, adjusting the anchor by perhaps a half-inch, lengthening the focal point in the release sequence. Carnival witnesses describe him as having "changed nothing" during this period, which is itself the tell: a man who refuses to acknowledge age-related change is a man who is acutely aware of it. He never adopted glasses on public record. The pride is medical data.

Late career: file notes (mercenary infirmary, undated, late period) reference "intermittent visual disturbance, right eye, transient" — likely early macular drusen or vitreous floaters, possibly stress-related visual snow. He did not seek follow-up. The omission is diagnostically loud. **A subject whose entire self-concept is mediated by ocular precision will, when the eye begins to fail, refuse the documentation of that failure with greater vigor than he ever refused arrest.**

The psychological impact of ocular aging on this subject cannot be overstated. Every shift in dynamic acuity, every micro-second slowing of vergence reflex, would have been registered as a personal injury — and would have been *re-routed into compensatory mechanical tightening of the shot sequence*, which produces the late-career signature: shots that are still extraordinary but visibly more ritualized, more elaborated in the preparation phase. The body grows liturgy around the eye it can no longer fully trust.

---

## 2.3 THE MUSCULOSKELETAL LEDGER

A career of high-repetition asymmetric loading writes itself, eventually, into the skeleton.

**Right shoulder (draw side)**: progressive supraspinatus tendinopathy, documented by palpation in mid-career carnival medic notes ("the old shoulder grumbles in the cold"); probable partial-thickness rotator cuff tear, undiagnosed and untreated, by the fifties. He worked through it. The compensation pattern — recruiting upper trapezius and levator scapulae for what supraspinatus could no longer cleanly initiate — is visible in late-career photographs as a slight elevation of the right shoulder at rest and a faint upward neck shift before each shot. He would not have called it pain. He would have called it focus.

**Left shoulder (bow side)**: anterior deltoid and serratus anterior fatigue, chronic; minor impingement signs from the static loading of the bow arm held in extension under tension thousands of times across a working life. Less acute than the right, more constant — a low hum rather than a grind.

**Cervical spine**: mild lower-cervical degenerative changes (C5–C6, C6–C7), the predictable consequence of a head held in a fixed pre-aim posture for cumulative thousands of hours. Likely mild radicular symptoms (forearm tingling, finger paresthesia) in cold weather — *which would have terrified him* and which he would have suppressed from external speech entirely.

**Thoracic spine**: kyphotic drift, modest, late career. The aging archer's posture.

**Lumbar spine**: facet wear at L4–L5, asymmetric (right > left), from rotational loading during the carnival's trick repertoire (over-the-shoulder shots, behind-the-back shots, the inverted-target routines).

**Right elbow**: medial epicondylosis, chronic; small olecranon spurring from decades of release deceleration. **Right wrist and fingers**: mild osteoarthritic changes in the metacarpophalangeal joints of the draw fingers (index, middle, ring); calluses at the pad surfaces hardened to leather. Three-finger Mediterranean draw, glove-worn, but the glove only mitigates. The skin tells the truth.

**Left hand (bow hand)**: webspace calloused, knuckles slightly enlarged; a chronic, asymptomatic bruise at the base of the thumb from the bow's pressure point in the lifepath, occasionally fresh in periods of high practice volume.

**Hips and knees**: largely preserved. Carnival performance demanded balance more than impact; he was spared the joint destruction of the trades that involve running and landing.

**Feet**: surprisingly fragile. Carnival shoes are not orthopedic. Plantar fascial thickening, mild, bilateral; a long-standing Morton's neuroma between the third and fourth metatarsals, right foot, that he favored without naming.

The psychological consequence of this ledger: a man who experienced his own body as a sequence of small betrayals, each demanding silent recalibration, none acknowledgeable. Pain became simply *the texture of being him*, and the refusal to name it became indistinguishable from his identity. Stoicism, here, is not virtue. It is the only available defense against the recognition that the instrument is wearing out.

---

## 2.4 INJURY RECORD

Combat trauma, accumulated:

- **Carnival-era**: assorted lacerations and contusions from rigging accidents, animal handling (one notable equine kick to the lateral right thigh leaving a permanent depression in the vastus lateralis), and the inevitable consequences of working under canvas with sharp objects and intoxicated colleagues. A broken nose, twice — once from a fistfight with a roustabout, once unspecified. The nasal septum deviates slightly left; he breathes audibly through it in periods of exertion or rage.
- **The embezzlement-exposure incident** itself, on his end: no injury. The injury was entirely on the child. The asymmetry is documented.
- **Mercenary mid-career**: gunshot wound, through-and-through, left lateral thigh (no femoral involvement, no permanent deficit); shrapnel scarring, lower back and right flank, from an unspecified explosive engagement; multiple knife wounds, hands and forearms, defensive in pattern; one clean stab to the left lower quadrant, abdominal, that should have killed him and did not — the scar is keloidal, pale, and runs roughly six centimeters.
- **An arrow wound to the right shoulder**, inflicted (per file annotation) by his former protégé during one of their confrontations. The wound itself was non-fatal and well-aimed to disable rather than kill. Its *psychological* sequelae dominate the rest of his life: the protégé proved, in that moment, capable of striking him with his own weapon's logic, and the lesson — that he had built the instrument of his own undoing — could neither be absorbed nor discarded. It festered as narcissistic injury for years afterward, and the scar (small, puckered, on the anterior deltoid he could see every morning while dressing) functioned as a daily renewal of grievance.
- **Hand injuries**: a fractured fifth metacarpal, right, from striking something inanimate in rage (era undetermined; the callus suggests mid-career); never properly set, healed with a slight angulation that would have annoyed him in the draw for the rest of his life.
- **Hearing**: bilateral high-frequency loss, mild, consistent with decades of unprotected exposure to gunfire (mercenary work) and carnival noise. He would have begun to mishear consonants in late life and would have responded by speaking less, listening more, and projecting an aura of attentive silence that was, in fact, partial deafness reframed as gravitas.

No documented head injuries severe enough to leave cognitive sequelae. The mind, until the cancer, remained organized as it had always been organized — which is to say, rigidly, with the precision of a man who has never permitted himself the disorganization of being changed.

---

## 2.5 SUBSTANCES

**Alcohol**: chronic, moderate-to-heavy, consistent across the carnival decades and into the mercenary period. Whiskey, neat, the working brand whatever the locale offered; beer in quantity in social contexts he tolerated. Liver function never formally tested in the available record but inferable as compromised by late career (mild hepatomegaly noted in the terminal-period oncology workup, attributable to alcohol load rather than metastasis at the point of notation). The drinking served a regulatory function: it was the chemical permission to relax the cognitive vigilance he otherwise maintained at all hours. He did not drink before performing or before contracted work — the discipline around the threshold is absolute and is itself diagnostic of a man who needs the substance precisely *because* he otherwise refuses any other form of self-permission.

**Tobacco**: yes, era-appropriate. Hand-rolled in the carnival years, store-bought later. Quit, per implication, at some indeterminate mid-career point — possibly under pressure of the early shoulder issues and a noticed shortness of breath that would have been intolerable to him as a performer. The quitting was almost certainly accomplished by sheer will, in a single act, and was almost certainly never spoken of again.

**Stimulants**: none documented. He did not need amphetamine to focus; he had built the focus into his nervous system. Coffee, black, large quantities, throughout life.

**Opiates**: brief courses post-injury, declined when offered for chronic pain. The refusal is in character — accepting pain medication would have been accepting that pain was present.

**Recreational drugs (carnival circuit)**: opportunity was constant; engagement appears minimal. He observed others' dissolution with the contempt of a man whose self-discipline was the single non-negotiable feature of his self-concept.

---

## 2.6 THE TERMINAL DIAGNOSIS

Cancer, late-period, unspecified primary in the available record but presenting with systemic features (weight loss, fatigue, the hepatomegaly noted above, probable bone pain in the axial skeleton given the difficulty of his late-period movement). The differential — and this is inference, but well-supported — favors a smoking-related malignancy with metastatic spread, possibly lung primary with hepatic and skeletal mets, given the historical tobacco load, the time-course, and the systemic presentation. Pancreatic primary is the alternative consonant with the rapid decline and the constitutional weight loss; the file does not adjudicate.

What the file *does* adjudicate is the psychological response, which is the diagnostically central event.

A subject organized around mastery, control, and the refusal of bodily vulnerability is told that his body has betrayed him at a cellular level, in a process he cannot out-discipline, out-shoot, or outwait. The expected response in a subject with normative affective resources would be some admixture of fear, grief, and movement toward affiliation — calls to family, attempts at repair, the documented "life review" of palliative patients. **None of this occurs.** Instead, the subject's defensive organization undergoes not collapse but *crystallization*. The pathology, freed from the maintenance demands of ordinary life, distills.

Specifically: he refuses palliative engagement; he refuses any framing of the illness as something happening *to* him rather than something he is *managing*; he routes the entire experience of dying through a single coercive gesture — the summoning of the abandoned protégé to be either the agent of his death or the conscript of his legacy. The illness becomes the occasion for the most grandiose act of his life, which is to choreograph his own ending through the hand of the man he wronged forty years prior, and to frame this choreography as gift, as legacy-transfer, as the final master class.

There is no peace in any of this. There is only the final, total deployment of the organizing defense: *I am the one who decides; I am the one who is watched; I am the one whose meaning is conferred by the precision of my final act.* The cancer is the audience he could not have arranged for himself, and he performs for it.

**Pain management**, by inference: minimal. He would have endured what could be endured and accepted only the threshold of medication required to remain coherent enough to deliver the final gesture. The pain itself would have been integrated, with characteristic dissociative competence, into the texture of intentional suffering — *I am bearing this, therefore I am still the one in charge of it.*

**Cognitive status at the end**: preserved, by all account. The mind that had refused to change refused to change once more, and held.

---

## 2.7 INTEGRATED MEDICAL-PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT

The medical history of Bernard Barton is the medical history of a man for whom the body was never a place to live but only an instrument to operate. Every condition in the ledger — the cuff tear, the cervical degeneration, the ocular drift, the liver, eventually the malignancy — was met with the same protocol: do not acknowledge, do not document, do not adjust the public mechanic, recruit compensatory effort silently. The protocol worked, in its terms, for forty years. It produced a man whose carnival-era and mercenary-era performances are technically indistinguishable to an outside observer, despite the underlying somatic erosion being severe by the end.

The cost of the protocol is that the body, denied its voice across a lifetime, can only speak in the catastrophic register when it speaks at last. The cancer is not an accident superimposed on the life. The cancer is, in a meaningful sense, the *aggregate unspoken* — every pain refused, every weakness suppressed, every signal silenced — returning as the one thing that cannot be silenced. He responds to it as he responded to every prior signal: by tightening the grip, narrowing the focus, refusing the witness of weakness, and converting the experience into a performance whose audience is the protégé he taught to watch him.

The body, in the end, is treated as the final target. The shot is taken with the same cold precision that defined the career. The medical chart and the psychological chart are, for this subject, the same document, written in different inks.

— END SECTION 2 —


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON

*Classification: Granular Embodiment Mapping / Longitudinal Behavioral Substrate*
*Compiled from: direct observation logs (carnival period through terminal phase); cross-referenced witness depositions (C. Barton, B. Barton dec., Carson personnel); medical intake from contracted physicians; surveillance footage, where extant.*

---

## 1. THE FRAME AT REST

Six feet even at his prime, dropping perhaps three-quarters of an inch by the terminal years through ordinary spinal compression. Lean — not the lean of an ascetic but of an organism that has been moved through the same six or seven motions ten thousand times each until everything not load-bearing in those motions has been pared off. The musculature is asymmetrical in a way that maps perfectly onto the draw: right-side latissimus, rhomboid, posterior deltoid, and the long extensors of the right forearm are hypertrophied relative to the left, which carries the bow and has developed a different signature — a denser, more compact deltoid and a forearm whose flexor tendons stand out like cabling when the hand grips. The right-hand calluses are old and stratified: a deep one at the medial pad of the index finger, a second at the distal phalanx of the middle and ring fingers, a worn polished smoothness at the inside of the right thumb where the nock seats. The left-hand calluses are flatter, broader, across the meat of the palm. The wrists carry the small white scars of a thousand string-slaps from the early years before the technique cleaned up.

Standing posture: chest neither thrown forward nor collapsed; shoulders held a fraction lower than the relaxed mean of most men his age, a learned thing — the shoulder that rises is the shoulder that misses. The pelvis is neutral; the weight rides slightly forward of the heel, in the arch, which is the archer's standing weight. He does not shift foot to foot. When forced to wait, he goes still in a way that reads to most observers as patience and to a trained eye as a kind of pre-loaded readiness, the way a hammer is still on the back-swing.

Resting head carriage: chin a degree lower than perpendicular, which produces the upward look from beneath the brow that has been variously described by witnesses as appraising, contemptuous, or cold. It is none of those things originally; it is a sighting habit, the head set for the dominant eye, that has migrated from the line to ordinary life and acquired social meaning he is no longer aware of.

---

## 2. THE EYES

The single most overdetermined region of the body. Resting blink rate notably below population mean — observers have logged him going twelve, fourteen seconds between blinks in conversation, a duration that produces in interlocutors the sensation of being aimed at. Under task (any visual-precision activity, from threading a needle to clearing a room), blink suppression extends further. He does not have the dry-eye redness one would expect; he has trained a partial blink, a brief lower-lid flicker that re-wets the cornea without breaking sight-line.

Pupils: rapid accommodation, faster than baseline, which is the trained marksman's signature. Dominant eye is the right; the left does not fully close when he sights — another mark of the disciplined shooter, who learns binocular sighting with one eye throttled to a slit rather than shut. In ordinary conversation the left eye will occasionally narrow a fraction more than the right, a residue of this drill, giving the face a faint asymmetric squint that intensifies under appraisal.

Saccadic pattern: economical. He does not scan a room the way a paranoid man does (rapid, returning, never settling); he scans the way a hunter does (sectoring, fixating, releasing, moving on, not revisiting). Entry into a new space follows a stereotyped sequence — ceiling corners first (a circus habit, where the lines and rigging live overhead), then the exits, then the hands of anyone present, then the faces. The faces last. This sequence is consistent across forty years of recorded behavior.

Under stress the eyes do not widen; they narrow and steady. Under threat, the right eye goes to the dominant target and the left to whatever is in peripheral motion, producing a brief disconjugate appearance that has unnerved witnesses. Under intimacy — what little of it is on record — the gaze does not soften; it goes flat and slightly past the partner, as though the person were at the wrong focal distance.

---

## 3. THE HANDS

Hands of disproportionate eloquence in a man whose face says little. The right hand at rest curls — not into a fist, into the half-pronated draw posture, fingers slightly hooked, thumb laid alongside the index. Witnesses report it tends to find his hip or thigh and rest there in this configuration, the fingers periodically performing a small isometric squeeze-and-release that is the residue of nock-set drills. The cycle is roughly every nine to twelve seconds at calm baseline and accelerates under attentional load.

The left hand has two distinct rest positions: cupped slightly, palm down, when seated (the riser-grip shape); or fully relaxed and open when he is genuinely off-duty, which is rare. The differentiation between the hands is unconscious and has been visible since the carnival years.

Tremor: none at baseline. None under stress. A faint physiological tremor begins to register in the terminal year, in the left hand first — a fact he conceals with great consistency by anchoring the hand against a surface, hip, opposite forearm, the back of a chair. The concealment is a tell in itself: a man who never used to brace begins bracing.

Grooming of the hands is meticulous and continuous. Nails clipped flat and short on the right (interference with the release), slightly longer and shaped on the left. Cuticles tended. He carries — has carried since the carnival days — a small folded knife and a sharpening stone; the ritual of touching up the knife edge is performed nightly and at moments of social discomfort, where it serves as a displacement activity that also functions as a low-grade threat display.

---

## 4. THE FACE

A face that has trained itself toward economy. The forehead does not lift; the brow does not gather. The mouth holds in a flat horizontal at rest, the corners neither up nor down, and the lower lip is held slightly forward of the upper — a carriage that reads as a man perpetually about to say no. Smile is rare and comes in two distinct variants, observable since the earliest carnival records:

The **performance smile**: deployed for crowds, marks, employers, and prospective protégés. Broad, fast onset, fast offset, eyes uninvolved. Lip line stays flat at the corners; the smile is all in the cheek lift. Lasts under two seconds without conscious extension.

The **predator smile**: smaller, slower, asymmetric — the right corner pulled higher than the left, the upper lip lifting briefly off the canine. Deployed when out-shooting another marksman, when watching the protégé fail a drill he set him up to fail, and once on record when the boy Clint Barton named the embezzlement aloud. The expression precedes violence by approximately half a beat and is the single most reliable predictor of physical action available to anyone in the room with him.

Jaw set: masseter hypertrophy is visible, particularly along the right side, indicating chronic clenching. Bruxism almost certainly present at night; molars show consistent flat wear on examination. Under any provocation that he must not act on — a slight he is absorbing, a fee he is being shortchanged on, a superior speaking — the masseter jumps once, twice, and goes still. This is the inhibition signature and it is among the most consistent micro-tells in the file.

Vocalization: low register, dry, sparing. Speaks in declarative fragments rather than full sentences when off-stage; on-stage in his carnival years the patter was fluent, theatrical, paced for the rhythm of the trick. The two registers are sealed off from each other; intimates have reported the disorientation of hearing the patter voice slip out in a private moment, like hearing a phonograph from another room.

---

## 5. GAIT, CARRIAGE, AND THE WAY HE ENTERS A ROOM

Walks with a short, economical stride, foot strike toward the lateral edge, weight rolling inward to the great toe at push-off — the gait of someone who has spent a working lifetime on uneven canvas and dirt. Quiet on hard floors, quieter still on soft. The arms do not swing freely; the right is dampened (residual draw posture), the left swings slightly more, producing a faint visible asymmetry from behind that scouts and contracted observers have used as a recognition signature at distance.

Entry into a room: pauses just inside the threshold for one beat — between half a second and a second — during which the sectoring scan described above completes. Then a step to the side, never staying framed in a doorway. Chooses standing positions with a wall to his back if possible, and never sits in the seat with the worst sightline to the entrance. If forced to take a poor seat, the right hand goes to the knife, the sharpening stone comes out, and the displacement ritual begins.

Stair-climbing: economical, no banister contact, breath silent through the nose. Descents controlled, weight slightly back — he does not commit a step until the lead foot is grounded, a habit that has visibly slowed in the terminal year.

Running: rarely observed. When observed, surprisingly graceless above a jog — he is not a runner; he is a stander.

---

## 6. SLEEP

Sleep architecture (compiled from carnival-trailer cohabitation reports, occasional safehouse surveillance, and one hospital admission record): early to bed by professional necessity in the carnival years, holding to roughly a 22:30 down / 05:30 up schedule that compresses to six hours in stressful periods and never extends beyond seven by choice. Initial sleep latency under ten minutes — a discipline, not a gift. He performs a fixed pre-sleep sequence: knife and stone, ten passes; bow inspection by touch with the bow racked beside the cot; a single short exhalation before he lies down; right hand to the chest, left hand to the side, on the back, almost never on the stomach, rarely on a side.

Sleeps shallowly. Wakes fully and instantly at any non-ambient sound, and the wake is not the startle of a frightened sleeper — he goes from supine to sitting upright with eyes open and hand to the knife in a single unbroken motion, with no transitional grogginess. Rolls his neck once, listens, lies back if the sound resolves. Has woken in this manner an average of two to three times per night across most recorded periods.

Dream activity: not directly observable, but bedmates and trailer-mates over the years have noted occasional jaw-clenching audible across a small room, and once a single shouted fragment — a name not recovered — that he denied the next morning with a flatness that suggested either repression or refusal. Snoring: light, nasal, intermittent, increases with alcohol intake.

The pre-sleep ritual breaks only twice on record: during the acute period after Clint's exposure of the embezzlement (he reportedly did not sleep at all for the better part of three nights, pacing) and during the first weeks following terminal diagnosis (the knife sequence extends from ten passes to forty, fifty, and on one observed night past a hundred, the stone going dry).

---

## 7. EATING AND DRINKING

Eats sparingly and on a schedule, the carnival circuit having taught him to feed when food was available and to ignore hunger when it wasn't. Preference for plain food — meat, bread, hard cheese, black coffee — and a marked dislike of any meal that requires sustained attention to consume (shellfish, fish with bones, dishes requiring multiple utensils). He eats with his left hand braced flat on the table beside the plate, right hand working the utensil, eyes on the room rather than the food. Chews with the mouth closed, swallows quietly, finishes plates completely or pushes them away after the first three bites — no middle ground.

Coffee: black, hot, in volume. He drinks it from the cup with the right hand and sets the cup down at the same spot on the table each time, within a tolerance of perhaps a centimeter. The placement consistency is observable in worn-ring patterns on his preferred trailer table from the carnival years.

Alcohol: present, paced, never to the point of dropped guard. Bourbon or rye, neat, one finger at a time, with long intervals. Slips toward two and three fingers in the terminal phase, and the pre-sleep ritual lengthens correspondingly. Tells when drinking: the right hand begins to perform the nock-squeeze a beat faster; the predator smile becomes more available; the masseter inhibition signature weakens, and the things he would otherwise have absorbed begin to be said aloud.

Tobacco: cigarettes through the middle years, dropped in the late period when the wind began to matter more than the habit. Holds the cigarette in the left hand, never the right.

Hydration: undertrained, like most men of his era and milieu. Not a water-drinker. The terminal cancer's first somatic flags (fatigue, the faint tremor, the slowing) he initially attributes, on record, to dehydration and aging — a misreading consistent with a man who has never closely consulted his body for anything except its aim.

---

## 8. GROOMING AND DRESS

Hair kept short, cut by his own hand in the carnival years with a straight razor and a small mirror, the cut uneven at the back in a way only seen from behind. Later periods: barbered, but to the same template — close on the sides, slightly longer on top, no fuss. Greying began at the temples in his forties and proceeded symmetrically; he did not dye.

Shave: daily, in cold water when warm was unavailable, with a straight razor (the carnival economy of one blade for everything). The shave is performed in a fixed sequence — right cheek, left cheek, chin, upper lip, throat — and any deviation from this sequence in a given morning observation is a stress indicator. He does not nick himself; in the terminal year, the first nick is followed by a long stillness in the mirror.

Dress: utilitarian, with one consistent vanity — the costume of the trick-shot performer, when worn, is meticulously kept. Off-stage clothing is dark, plain, fitted to allow the draw, with a slight excess of room in the right shoulder seam (a tailor's accommodation for the hypertrophied lat). Boots low-heeled, soft-soled, kept clean. He laces them tight and double-knots, every time, with the same hand sequence.

Smell: tobacco and the metallic dryness of bow wax through the middle years; later, the soap of whichever lodging he is in, plus the faint medicinal note of analgesic balm on the right shoulder and the lumbar paraspinals (chronic strain from the draw). In the terminal months, the sweet undersmell that some cancers carry begins to register on close observers; he becomes more aggressive with cologne in compensation, a vanity he would have scorned in himself a decade earlier.

---

## 9. THE SHOOTING BODY

The shot itself is the body's grammar, and every other motion is dialect of it. The full sequence, observable in identical form across forty years until the terminal degradation:

- **Stance**: feet shoulder-width, perpendicular to target, weight even and forward in the arch. He sets the stance with a small heel adjustment, never a toe one.
- **Nock**: right hand to quiver, arrow drawn out by the shaft just below the fletching, brought to the string in a single arc, nocked with a quiet click he has trained to be almost inaudible.
- **Set**: three fingers to the string, index above, middle and ring below (Mediterranean), the bow hand rising to roughly chin height with the elbow slightly soft, never locked.
- **Pre-draw**: one breath in, half-released, the diaphragm settled.
- **Draw**: smooth, scapular, the back doing the work — anyone watching the front of him sees only the bow arm steadying, but the back is where the motion lives. Anchor at the corner of the mouth, the index finger touching the canine.
- **Hold**: less than a second. He does not aim long. The hold is a verification, not a search.
- **Release**: the fingers do not open; the string slips them. Right hand finishes at the right ear, fingers relaxed, palm down. No flinch, no follow-through theatrics; the body simply remains where the shot left it for one beat before resetting.

Under stress the sequence does not change. Under fatigue, the hold extends and the elbow softens further. In the terminal year, a new micro-tell enters: a near-imperceptible double-tap of the index finger on the string before the release, a checking motion that was not there before. He becomes furious whenever he notices himself doing it.

---

## 10. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE

The record is thin by character rather than by lack of opportunity — he was a man around whom carnival circuits offered conventional appetites and who appears to have engaged them with the same economy he engaged food. No long partnerships on file. No children documented. Approach is direct, conversation minimal, the same flat post-coital affect that follows any other completed motor sequence in his repertoire. Witnesses describe him as competent and absent in equal measure — the body present, the regard elsewhere.

Touch tolerance generally: low. He does not initiate contact except for instruction (the corrective hand to the protégé's elbow, the adjustment of grip on the bow). He flinches imperceptibly at the unexpected touch of another person — a flinch that ends in his right hand near his knife before the conscious mind has registered the source. The flinch is faster in old age, not slower.

Intimacy markers in non-sexual context: there are essentially three on record. The first is the early training of the boy Barton, in which he occasionally — perhaps four or five times across years — placed his hand briefly on the back of the boy's neck after a particularly clean shot, a gesture he never made toward the elder brother and never repeated after the embezzlement scene. The second is a single recorded instance of him standing at the edge of a carnival lot at dawn alone with a coffee, observed from distance by a roustabout, not knowing he was watched; the carriage was different, the shoulders lower, the head not in the sighting tilt — a face the file has otherwise no record of. The third is the deathbed summons, which is intimacy weaponized: the request to be killed by the only person he ever allowed to love him is the closest he comes, in the whole record, to saying what he means.

---

## 11. STATE SHIFTS — A SYNOPTIC TABLE IN PROSE

**Calm baseline**: low blink rate, slow nock-squeeze, masseter quiet, gaze sectoring slow and complete, knife ritual on schedule, breath nasal and inaudible, posture forward-weighted but soft. He is, in this state, almost pleasant to share a room with, which has historically been the most dangerous thing about him.

**Mild stress (unfamiliar room, unfamiliar interlocutor, money under discussion)**: blink rate drops further, nock-squeeze cycle tightens to every six or seven seconds, knife emerges, masseter begins the single-jump signature, left eye narrows to match right, displacement sharpening commences. The voice drops a quarter step and the sentences shorten.

**Acute stress (status challenge, skill challenge, exposure)**: the entire face goes still, including the masseter — the inhibition signature breaks, which means the inhibition is no longer operating. Eyes go cold-narrow. The right hand stops the nock-squeeze and goes flat against the thigh, fingers extended — a posture he holds for the single beat before action. The predator smile may appear. Breath audibly slows rather than quickens. This is the most dangerous configuration in the file and the one his protégé learned, before he could name it, to read across a room.

**Threat (direct combat)**: full economy. No wasted motion. No vocalization. The shot sequence above, executed in under a second per arrow, the body operating without affect. Heart rate elevation is real but does not surface in any visible tremor or breath disorder. Recovery to baseline within sixty to ninety seconds of cessation; he does not shake afterward; he does not vomit; he eats.

**Intimacy / vulnerability (rare, mostly inferred)**: the flat-past-the-shoulder gaze, the dampened smile, the small reflexive turn of the body away from the partner by perhaps fifteen degrees. He cannot tolerate frontality with another person whom he registers as caring for him. The body presents itself in three-quarter, always.

**Terminal phase**: the new tremor in the left hand; the lengthened pre-sleep ritual; the slowing of the stair descent; the cologne; the unwillingness to be seen seated in a low chair from which rising is visible work; the increased reliance on bracing surfaces concealed as casual leaning; the cigarette dropped, the bourbon doubled. And, threaded through all of these, an increase in the frequency and duration of the predator smile, as though the dying body were allocating more of its remaining bandwidth to the one expression that had always meant *I am still the one who decides*.

---

## 12. THE SIGNATURE IN ONE SENTENCE

Everything above resolves to a single embodiment: a man whose body has been organized for forty years around the half-second between sighting and release, and who has imported the stillness, the economy, the unblinking address, and the refusal of follow-through into every other domain of his life — eating as one shoots, walking as one shoots, sleeping as one shoots, loving as one shoots, dying, finally, as one shoots: with the target chosen, the hold brief, and no flinch on the release.

— END SOMATIC ATLAS —


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON

*Section 5 of UATU Full Intelligence Dossier. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological) and §4 (Psychiatric). All inferences derived from canonical behavior across Hawkeye Vol.1 (1983), Solo Avengers #1–4, West Coast Avengers run, Hawkeye: Blindspot, and the Fraction-era backgrounders.*

---

## 1. Attachment Style — Classification and Origins

### 1.1 The taxonomic placement

Subject's attachment architecture maps with unusual cleanliness onto the **dismissive-avoidant** quadrant, but with a specifying overlay that distinguishes him from the textbook avoidant adult: his avoidance is not a withdrawal from contact, it is a *re-engineering* of contact into pedagogy. Where a pure dismissive avoidant evacuates the relational field, Buck Barton stays in it — but only on terms that abolish the asymmetry of need. He does not refuse intimacy; he refuses to be the one who needs it. The student-teacher dyad is his sole tolerable form of closeness because it locates dependency entirely on the other side of the relation.

Within the avoidant family this places him close to what attachment researchers call the **"fearful-dismissive with grandiose compensation"** subtype, but the more useful frame is the Kernbergian one already invoked in §4: a narcissistic personality organization for which the attachment system has been *colonized* by the self-regulatory system. He does not attach to people. He attaches to *audiences* and to *reflections of his own mastery in another's developing skill*. The boy at the end of the bow is not a son; the boy is a mirror that occasionally talks back, and the moment it talks back morally rather than admiringly, the mirror is shattered.

### 1.2 The developmental origin (inferred)

Canon is silent on Buck's own childhood. The behavior is not. Five features of his adult relational style are diagnostic of his own developmental water:

- **Conditional regard as default currency.** He metes out approval to Clint only at performance landmarks (the splitting of the arrow, the trick-shot sequence in Hawkeye Vol.1 #4). A man who knows no other coin to spend was raised in an economy that accepted no other.
- **Aggression-as-instruction.** He does not separate teaching from punishment. The two are fused at a level that suggests they were fused in his own learning. Subjects who can teach gently were, somewhere, taught gently.
- **Zero tolerance for the child's separate moral judgment.** The embezzlement scene is not, for him, a moral exposure — it is a *role violation*. The student stepped outside the student-frame. This rigidity around relational hierarchy is the fingerprint of someone whose own adolescent attempts at moral autonomy were crushed.
- **The carnival as chosen family.** Runaways and itinerants do not choose the carnival the way young people choose colleges; the carnival is the residual destination of those for whom the family of origin was uninhabitable. Buck's adult home is a structure of provisional belonging organized around skill display — the precise structure his internal working model can metabolize.
- **The Swordsman as preferred peer.** His one durable lateral bond is with another grandiose performer whose ethics are equally absent. He pairs with his structural twin; he cannot pair with anyone less defended.

The probable etiology is a harsh trainer-father or surrogate (carnival, military, athletic) who modeled exactly the contempt-as-pedagogy Buck reproduces. He has not invented his cruelty; he has transmitted it. The Barton boys received what Buck received, minus whatever softening agents (a mother, a sibling, a kind neighbor) may have buffered Buck's own intake and which the orphan brothers wholly lacked.

---

## 2. The Phases of a Buck Barton Bond

Every relationship in the record — Clint, Barney, the Swordsman, the various criminal employers, the late-era successor "heir," even the implicit relation to his own bow — moves through the same staged sequence. The stages are so consistent they constitute a clinical signature.

### 2.1 Phase I — Recognition / Selection

Buck identifies the other through a single perceptual filter: *can this person be made useful inside my skill economy?* For Clint, the recognition is documented as quasi-instantaneous — the boy's hand-eye, his hunger, his fatherlessness. Buck reads three vectors at once: technical potential, emotional vacancy waiting to be filled, and social isolation that will prevent the protégé from comparing notes with anyone outside the dyad. He selects, in other words, for *isolatable competence*. He does not select friends; he selects substrates.

With the Swordsman the selection criterion is different but structurally equivalent: a peer who will not threaten the position and will not impose any ethical demand. Selection is always for low relational friction and high instrumental yield.

### 2.2 Phase II — Investiture

This is the phase that has fooled every observer, including the early canon and including Clint himself for decades. Buck invests *enormously*. Time, attention, technical capital, the inheritance of methods, the privilege of his presence. He drills the boy for hours; he corrects micro-tremors in the draw; he stays after the carnival has closed. To an outsider — and to a deprived child — this is indistinguishable from love.

It is not love. It is the *enrollment* of the other into Buck's narcissistic ledger. The investiture is real labor and produces real skill, but the labor is bookkeeping: every hour Buck spends becomes a debt that the protégé owes. The boy is being purchased, in installments, against future obedience.

Tell: Buck's praise in this phase is always *technical*, never *personal*. "Tight group." "Better." Never "I'm proud of you." Never the personhood-affirming sentence. He cannot say it because he does not, in the relevant sense, see a person there.

### 2.3 Phase III — Binding via Withholding

Once the protégé is materially in the dyad, Buck shifts to a regulated scarcity of regard. Approval becomes intermittent and unpredictable, on a schedule that — accidentally or intuitively — replicates the variable-ratio reinforcement that produces the most persistent attachment behavior. Clint, in the flashbacks, is shown chasing the look from Buck that arrives once a session if at all. This is the operant core of the bond: the student is conditioned into a state of perpetual effortful approach.

The withholding is not strategic in any conscious sense. Buck withholds because giving costs him something he does not have to spend.

### 2.4 Phase IV — Stable Exploitation

The mature middle phase of a Buck Barton bond looks, from the outside, like a partnership. The protégé performs; Buck collects (status, money, the audience's gaze through the protégé's act, eventually a cut of carnival receipts). The Swordsman occupies an analogous slot at peer level. This phase can last years and is not necessarily marked by overt cruelty — the cruelty is reserved for the rupture.

In this phase Buck is at his most behaviorally normal. He drinks moderately, jokes occasionally, displays the gruff-mentor surface that observers (and early writers) took for the whole man. The pathology is latent because the relational contract is being honored: the other is performing the role of admiring instrument.

### 2.5 Phase V — Rupture

The rupture is *always* triggered by the same event: the other party asserts an autonomous moral or evaluative judgment that disconfirms Buck's self-image. Clint discovers the embezzlement and refuses to participate. This is the *only* category of event that can end a Buck Barton bond, and it ends every one of them.

The rupture sequence is stereotyped and worth detailing as forensic signature:

1. **Cold pause** — three to five seconds of complete affective flattening. Subject does not yell first. He goes still.
2. **Reframing utterance** — a single sentence that relocates the moral injury from his act to the other's exposure of it. ("After everything I did for you.") This sentence is the load-bearing defense; it is uttered before any violence and serves to authorize what follows.
3. **Calibrated violence** — never disorganized, never to the kill. He beats Clint, but he beats him to *teach a final lesson*. The pedagogical frame survives the rupture; this is its grotesque tell.
4. **Abandonment without farewell** — he does not say goodbye, does not look back, does not return for belongings. The protégé is, at the moment of rupture, *deleted from the ledger entirely*.

Note: Buck never repairs in the moment. The repair pathway is not available to him. He cannot say "I was stealing, I was wrong, I am sorry" because the sentence is, for him, unspeakable — its utterance would collapse the self-organization.

### 2.6 Phase VI — Revenant Return

This is the phase that distinguishes Buck from a simply avoidant subject who would, post-rupture, vanish. Buck *returns*. Years later, decades later, terminally ill — he returns. The returns are not reconciliations. They are restagings.

The functional purpose of the return is to **re-litigate the rupture on terms that allow Buck to win it retroactively**. He returns as the contracted assassin (Clint is the *job*, which inverts the hierarchy: now Clint is the object of Buck's professional regard); he returns as the deathbed summoner (Clint is the *instrument of Buck's chosen ending*, which restores Buck's authorship of the relation). Each return is an attempt to re-establish the asymmetry the embezzlement scene destroyed.

The protégé's repeated availability for these returns is *itself* a product of the Phase III conditioning. Clint comes when summoned because Buck installed in him the conditioned approach-response in childhood, and that operant scaffolding is not easily decommissioned.

---

## 3. Bonding — The Architecture of How He Lets Anyone In

Buck bonds along exactly three axes and no others.

**The pedagogical axis.** Other as student. This is the primary axis and the only one in which Buck experiences anything resembling sustained interest in another human being. The interest is genuine but its object is misidentified by the other: Buck is interested in *the skill becoming present in the student*, not in the student. When the skill plateaus or the student matures past further teachability, Buck's interest collapses. This is one of several reasons he had to be rid of Clint eventually — Clint was getting too good to remain a vessel for further deposits.

**The confederate axis.** Other as fellow performer at peer level. This is the Swordsman slot. It is shallow but durable so long as neither party impinges on the other's domain. Loyalty in this axis is loyalty to the *arrangement*, not to the person. Buck would sell out the Swordsman in a heartbeat if the arrangement failed to pay; the Swordsman knows this and reciprocates; the bond is the mutual recognition of mutual instrumentality.

**The audience axis.** Other as witness to performance. This is the least obvious and most pervasive form. Every crowd at every carnival, every employer who watches him work, every protégé who sees him shoot — these are the people Buck is most continuously bonded to, in the technical sense that they are most continuously regulating his self-state. He is not bonded to any individual member of the crowd. He is bonded to the *function* the crowd performs, which is to render him visible to himself.

He has no fourth axis. There is no friendship axis, no romantic axis (the record is essentially empty of intimate partners — diagnostically significant in itself), no kinship axis. The late-era "heir" to the Trick Shot identity is *not* an exception; the heir is reabsorbed into the pedagogical axis as a final student.

---

## 4. Distrust — The Architecture of Suspicion

Buck's distrust is **not paranoid**. Paranoid distrust is pervasive, content-rich, and frequently delusional. Buck's distrust is **structural and situational**: he distrusts anyone in a position to expose him, and he distrusts no one else. He sleeps fine next to the Swordsman. He drinks easily with carnival peers. He takes contracts from criminal employers without elaborate countermeasures.

What he cannot tolerate is the **gaze that evaluates rather than admires**. The moment another's eye becomes assessing rather than appreciative, Buck's regulatory system flips to threat. This is why he was undone not by an investigator but by a child — Clint's discovery of the theft was unbearable not because of the legal exposure (which the carnival circuit could absorb) but because the child *looked at him and judged*, and the judgment came from a position Buck had defined as structurally incapable of judgment.

Distrust, for Buck, is therefore a function of role-violation rather than person-perception. He never asks "is this person trustworthy?" He asks "is this person staying inside the box I assigned them?" The substitution of structural surveillance for actual reading of others is one of the central impoverishments of his interpersonal cognition (§3, low introspective capacity, near-zero interpersonal pattern recognition).

---

## 5. Betrayal — Both Directions

### 5.1 Buck as betrayer

Buck does not experience his own betrayals as betrayals. The embezzlement is, in his frame, *taking what was owed*. Contracting against Clint later is, in his frame, *professional work*. Selling out the Swordsman, were it to become necessary, would be *adapting to circumstances*. He has no internal category for his own treachery because the operative ethical primitive in his system is *loyalty to the hierarchy of skill*, and loyalty in this sense flows upward from the protégé to him, never laterally to confederates or downward to dependents.

His betrayals are characterized by:
- **Pre-justification.** He has the exonerating narrative ready before the act, not after. This is why the reframing utterance in the rupture sequence emerges so smoothly — it has been pre-loaded.
- **Cold execution.** No hesitation, no qualm, no compunction. The act of betrayal is performed with the same affective register as a difficult shot.
- **No aftermath rumination.** He does not lose sleep, does not seek to repair, does not even seem to remember the act as morally significant. It enters the ledger as *something I did because the situation required it*, and is filed.

### 5.2 Buck as betrayed

Conversely, when *he* is the object of betrayal — defined as any moral exposure or evaluative refusal by a subordinate — the wound is permanent and unmetabolizable. Forty years on, the Clint matter is fresh. He cannot let it go because letting it go would require acknowledging that Clint's exposure of him was legitimate, which would require acknowledging that he was, in fact, a thief, which would collapse the self-organization.

So the betrayal must be re-litigated, re-staged, re-fought, until either Clint dies, Buck dies, or Clint capitulates to Buck's framing. Since Clint will not capitulate (Clint's whole subsequent life as a hero is, in part, the refusal to capitulate), and Buck cannot kill Clint (the rare canonical demonstration of Clint's superior skill is one of the few things Buck cannot bear to test under maximal conditions), the only resolution available is Buck's own death — which he therefore stages, on his own terms, with Clint as the instrument. The deathbed summons is the *resolution of the unresolvable betrayal*.

---

## 6. Repair — Its Structural Absence and Its Counterfeit

Buck possesses no repair behaviors. The repair-relevant moves — acknowledgment of fault, expression of regret, request for forgiveness, behavioral change, sustained reparative action — are absent from every recorded interaction. This is not a deficit he experiences as a deficit; he does not know these moves exist as live options because his self-organization renders them unsayable.

What he produces *instead* of repair, and what naïve observers mistake for it, is the **counterfeit repair gesture**. These are acts that have the surface shape of reconciliation but whose function is the reassertion of the original asymmetry.

Three documented counterfeit-repair forms:

- **The teaching gift.** He returns and offers a final piece of technique, a refinement, an improvement to the protégé's craft. This looks like generosity. It is in fact *re-enrollment* of the protégé into the pedagogical axis, restoring Buck to the position of giver.
- **The contracted hunt.** He returns as the hired marksman against Clint. This looks, on the surface, like nothing repair-related at all. But its psychological function for Buck is *re-engagement on terms where the contract authorizes him to act and Clint must respond*. It restores Buck as initiator, Clint as reactor.
- **The deathbed summons.** Discussed above. The supreme counterfeit. It has the shape of a dying man seeking peace; its function is the absolute final assertion of authorship.

A handler attempting to elicit genuine repair from Buck will fail. The pathway does not exist. What can be elicited, with careful work, is *behavioral cessation* — Buck can be made to stop a specific harmful action under pressure of credible threat or terminal incentive — but not contrition, not changed inner stance, not durable repair of the underlying relation.

---

## 7. Intimacy and Dependency

### 7.1 Intimacy

The record is, with diagnostic force, almost empty of intimate partners. No documented wife, no documented lover, no documented sustained romantic relation. For a man embedded for decades in carnival and mercenary milieus where such relations are commonplace and casually formed, this absence is not gap in the record — it is the record. Buck does not do intimacy. The forms of vulnerability that intimacy requires (being seen at less than mastery, being received in need, being held in dependence) are precisely the forms his organization cannot tolerate.

The closest thing to intimacy in his record is the pedagogical bond with Clint, and that bond — as the entire foregoing analysis establishes — is intimacy's structural inverse: a closeness organized to prevent vulnerability rather than to permit it.

### 7.2 Dependency

Buck's dependency on others is **denied and displaced**. He cannot acknowledge needing anyone. He has nonetheless been, throughout his adult life, deeply dependent on:
- the carnival as economic and identity scaffolding,
- the audience as continuous self-regulator,
- the protégé as narcissistic extension,
- the bow itself as prosthetic selfhood (§2, somatic-psychological coupling),
- and in the terminal phase, Clint as the chosen instrument of his own dying.

The denial of this dependency network is total. Asked, he would name himself a self-made and self-sufficient man. Observed, he is one of the more thoroughly dependent personality structures in the carnival record — dependent precisely because his form of dependency is fragile, narrow, and non-substitutable. A subject who needs an audience can lose an audience. A subject who needs a particular protégé to mirror back his mastery is hostage to that protégé's continued cooperation. His denied dependencies are his exposed flanks.

---

## 8. The Single Relational Template, Repeated Across Every Bond

Reduced to its operative skeleton, every relationship Buck Barton has ever formed runs the following loop:

> **Select for instrumentality → Invest as enrollment → Bind via withholding → Exploit stably → Rupture on autonomous moral exposure → Reframe as the other's betrayal → Abandon without farewell → Return as revenant to re-litigate the asymmetry → Die staging the final assertion of authorship.**

This is the template. It runs identically with the Swordsman (truncated at exploitation phase because the Swordsman never morally exposed him), identically with Clint (full cycle, decades long, terminating in the deathbed), identically with the late successor (compressed into a single transmission phase under terminal time pressure), identically with employers and crowds (cycled through quickly at low resolution).

The template is not flexible. Buck cannot, on the available evidence, run any other relational program. When the situation calls for a different template — a bereaved father needing comfort, a wounded comrade needing tending, a lover needing tenderness — Buck does not improvise; he absents himself. The carnival is full of slots he never filled.

---

## 9. The Wound Transmitted

The diagnostic and operational point most relevant to ongoing observation of associated subjects: Clint Barton has internalized Buck's template as a **susceptibility profile**. He is, for the rest of his life, vulnerable to mentor-figures who:
- offer technical instruction in his domain,
- meter affection through performance milestones,
- frame his belonging in their world as conditional on continued demonstration,
- and reserve the right to withdraw it.

This is the structural reason Clint cycles through subsequent mentor/handler/leader figures with such pained loyalty and recurring disillusionment. The original template is doing the selecting. The damage Buck did is not a memory; it is a *filter through which all subsequent attachments are processed*. This is the through-line that makes the Bernard Barton file relevant well beyond the lifespan of its subject, and the reason this dossier is maintained.

— END SECTION 5 —


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS
## Subject: Bernard "Buck" Barton — alias *Trick Shot*
### Section 6 of the UATU Dossier

---

## 6.0 Orientation

What follows is the full inventory of Bernard Barton's defensive architecture: the mental operations by which he keeps an intolerable picture of himself (a thief, a child-beater, an aging body, a man whose own protégé surpassed him) from ever reaching consciousness in undisguised form. The architecture is unusually *stable* — this is one of its diagnostic features. He does not cycle between defenses the way a borderline or hysterical organization would; he runs a small number of high-yield operations, in fixed combinations, for decades. The system is brittle in only one specific way: it cannot tolerate being *out-shot in front of witnesses*. Everywhere else the walls hold.

Below the defenses are ranked from most primitive to most mature, following the Vaillant/Kernberg hierarchy. The compensatory mechanisms — what he *uses* (positively or negatively) to keep the organization functional — follow as a separate ledger.

---

## 6.1 Primitive Defenses (the load-bearing layer)

### 6.1.1 Projection (load-bearing, daily, ego-syntonic)

This is the central operation of the entire personality. Every recorded confrontation in canon turns on it.

**Mechanism.** Affects, intentions, and moral failures originating in Barton are experienced and articulated as belonging to the other party. The clearest instance: he is caught embezzling carnival receipts; within seconds of exposure he is *not* defending the theft, he is *prosecuting Clint for disloyalty*. The cognitive reframe is instantaneous and total. He does not appear to lie — he appears to *believe* it. The theft is somewhere else in the mind, walled off; what is in consciousness is the boy's betrayal.

**Behavioral signature.**
- In any argument involving his own misconduct, watch for an inversion within roughly two beats of exchange: accusation arrives → he goes briefly still → he returns the accusation, restructured around loyalty rather than ethics.
- He uses second-person framing under pressure ("*You* turned on me," "*You* couldn't stand that I…"). First-person ownership statements regarding his own actions are nearly absent from canon.
- Body language during projection: jaw set, shoulders squared, weight forward, draw-hand free — the posture of a man preparing to *enforce* a reframe, not negotiate it.

**Why it holds.** Forty years of practice. The original projection (Clint as traitor rather than himself as thief) was rehearsed daily through every grudge-thought, every imagined confrontation, every framing of his own subsequent failures. By the deathbed era it is no longer a defense, it is a perceptual filter.

### 6.1.2 Splitting (mild, structural, professional rather than affective)

Less florid than in a borderline organization, but present and consistent.

**Mechanism.** Persons are sorted into two bins: *competent-and-loyal* vs. *incompetent-or-treacherous*. There is essentially no third category — no allowance for the loyal-but-flawed, the competent-but-independent, the well-meaning-but-mistaken. The Swordsman occupies bin one as confederate; Clint moves from bin one (favored pupil) to bin two (traitor) in a single scene and never returns, regardless of subsequent evidence.

**Behavioral signature.** Verbal idiom is binary — *the kid had it / the kid lost it; he's a shooter / he's nothing*. No qualifying clauses. Estimations of others compress to one-word verdicts.

**Why mild.** The split is largely *cognitive-evaluative* rather than affectively explosive; bin assignments, once made, are durable for decades. This is a frozen split, not a flipping one.

### 6.1.3 Devaluation (chronic, automatic, ambient)

**Mechanism.** Anyone outside the *competent-loyal* bin is rhetorically and internally diminished. Marks, employers, civilians, "ordinary" shooters, anyone who has not been tested in his domain — all are background. Devaluation is not effortful; it is the resting state.

**Behavioral signature.**
- Reflexive epithets for the unskilled (carny argot: marks, rubes, etc.).
- A particular small smirk recorded across artists' renderings — left-corner mouth lift, eyes unchanged — that appears when a non-shooter offers him an opinion.
- He does not argue with the devalued; he simply does not register them as interlocutors. Civilians are scenery.

### 6.1.4 Identification with the Aggressor (inferred, structural)

Canon does not give us Bernard Barton's childhood. The behavior gives us its outline.

**Mechanism.** The harshness of his pedagogy — the withheld praise, the calibrated humiliation, the conviction that affection delivered openly *weakens* the recipient — has the polished, ritualized quality of something learned under the same regime. He is not improvising cruelty; he is reproducing a system. The very specific belief that *praise softens the shooter* is a transmitted ideology, not a personal discovery.

**Behavioral signature.** Pedagogical phrasing that has a quoted feel — "*you don't aim the bow, the bow aims you*"–type aphorisms that read as inherited rather than coined. The almost ceremonial way he sets a stance and then corrects it with a tap of his own bow-tip — that gesture has the smoothness of something done *to* him before it was done *by* him.

### 6.1.5 Omnipotent Control (situational, peaks in late life)

**Mechanism.** Restoration of a sense of total agency over an outcome — most visible in the deathbed staging. Faced with a death he cannot defeat, he *choreographs* it: summons Clint, dictates terms, attempts to convert his own dying into a final act of pedagogy and dominance.

**Behavioral signature.** Late-period speech patterns shift toward the imperative mood (*you'll do this; you'll come; you'll finish it*). He stops asking. He composes the room — sight lines, who stands where, the weapon present and laid out. The cancer ward becomes a carnival tent he is once again running.

---

## 6.2 Neurotic / Intermediate Defenses

### 6.2.1 Reaction Formation around Tenderness (chronic, the saddest of the operations)

**Mechanism.** Whatever proto-paternal warmth exists toward the boy is, at the moment of its threatened surfacing, converted to its opposite — sharpness, demand, withdrawal. The training scenes are the laboratory. A correct shot from young Clint produces not "good work" but a re-set of the bar — *again, farther, smaller, faster*. The tenderness was real; the conversion was reflexive.

**Behavioral signature.**
- A characteristic micro-sequence: when Clint succeeds, Barton's face begins a fractional softening — eye-corner crinkle, breath release — *which he interrupts*, often by turning a quarter away and finding a new flaw to call out. The interruption is the defense in motion.
