- He has trouble keeping eye contact during any moment that threatens affective sincerity. The eyes go to the bow, to the target, to middle distance.
- He communicates approval, when at all, by *raising the difficulty*, never by lowering the demand. Promotion-by-burden is his love language.

**Why it matters.** The reaction formation is what makes the abandonment scene so injurious. There *was* an affective bond; it was systematically expressed as harshness; the boy learned to read harshness as love; when love withdrew, harshness alone remained, and the boy had no template by which to call it abuse. The defense damaged Clint precisely because it was not absent affect — it was deformed affect.

### 6.2.2 Rationalization (situational, lawyerly, well-practiced)

**Mechanism.** Each misconduct is fitted, after the fact, with a small structurally coherent story in which it was necessary, deserved, or strategic. The embezzlement: *Carson didn't pay what the act was worth.* The beating of Clint: *the kid needed to learn loyalty.* The contract work against his former student: *business, the kid knew the life.* Each story is internally consistent and is repeated verbatim across years — these are not fresh inventions, they are catalogued rationales.

**Behavioral signature.** When confronted, he reaches for explanations with a steadiness that suggests retrieval rather than composition. The phrasing is stable across appearances; a surveillance log would find the same three or four sentences recurring almost word-for-word in interrogations decades apart.

### 6.2.3 Displacement (low-rate, but present)

**Mechanism.** Affect generated by one target is discharged onto a safer or more available one. In the carnival years, frustration with the Swordsman (his nominal equal, and therefore not safely attackable) tended to find its way onto the boys in the form of intensified drill. In late life, terror at the body's failure displaces onto contempt for younger shooters, including those he is ostensibly training as successors.

**Behavioral signature.** Sudden disproportions in pedagogical severity that do not correlate with the student's actual error but do correlate, on a longer timeline, with whatever Barton himself has just failed at or been refused.

### 6.2.4 Isolation of Affect (chronic, occupationally reinforced)

**Mechanism.** The marksman's discipline — slow breath, slow heart, the trigger pulled in the space between thoughts — is recruited into the personality at large. Feeling is separated from event. He can describe the abandonment of a thirteen-year-old as flatly as he describes a sight adjustment.

**Behavioral signature.**
- Vocal register stays constant across emotionally heterogeneous content. He says *I beat him bloody and walked out* in the same cadence he says *the wind was crossing left to right*.
- Heart rate, by every implication in the visual record, barely moves during confrontations. Pupils stay neutral. The hand does not tremor.
- He does not weep at his own diagnosis. He does not weep at the deathbed. The isolation holds to the end.

### 6.2.5 Intellectualization (narrow, domain-specific)

**Mechanism.** Where most intellectualizers retreat into abstraction across topics, Barton intellectualizes only one thing: shooting. Technical disquisition on the bow — draw weight, fletch spin, the physics of the broadhead in crosswind — serves as conversational refuge when interpersonal pressure rises.

**Behavioral signature.** Watch for tactical-technical micro-lectures appearing immediately after a personal question. Ask him about his life, get a paragraph on string material. The deflection is so smooth it reads as topical drift; it is actually defensive evasion.

---

## 6.3 More Mature Defenses (present but narrow)

### 6.3.1 Sublimation (real, partial, the one mature defense he genuinely possesses)

**Mechanism.** Aggression — and there is a great deal of it, the source-level reservoir is large — is routed almost entirely through the bow. The hand that would otherwise strike finds the string. This is genuine sublimation, not merely instrumental violence: marksmanship is, for him, the *aestheticized* discharge of what would otherwise be ugly affect.

**Behavioral signature.** The remarkable steadiness of his interpersonal violence — measured, never frenzied, never excessive to the moment — is downstream of the sublimation. The bow has absorbed the wildness. What is left over for fists is small and controlled. He is not a man who beats people for an hour; he hits, decisively, and is done.

**Why it matters diagnostically.** This is the single mature defense he commands, and it is the reason he is functional rather than incarcerated or institutionalized. Take the bow away from him and the routing collapses.

### 6.3.2 Anticipation (tactical only, not emotional)

**Mechanism.** In combat planning he is excellent at forecasting moves, sight lines, retreat routes. In emotional planning he is incompetent — he does not anticipate that the deathbed gambit might fail to produce the response he wants, does not anticipate Clint's grief at the summons.

**Behavioral signature.** A man who can map a building's lines of fire in seconds and cannot map his protégé's heart at all.

### 6.3.3 Defenses he conspicuously LACKS

- **Humor**: essentially absent. No self-mockery, no relieving irony. The closest thing is the sneer, which is contempt wearing humor's clothes.
- **Suppression**: he does not *postpone* affect for later processing; he isolates it or projects it. There is no holding-area in him.
- **Altruism**: not present in the record. Even the skill-transmission to a successor is staged for his benefit, not the heir's.

---

## 6.4 Compensatory Mechanisms — Positive Ledger

These are the genuine capacities that prop up the organization and keep it productive rather than merely destructive.

### 6.4.1 Craftsmanship as identity anchor
The bow gives him a stable, externally validated, somatically grounded sense of self that survives every interpersonal failure. While he can shoot, he is *someone*. This is real and considerable — most narcissistic organizations of this severity have nothing this solid to stand on.

### 6.4.2 Transmissible discipline
He *can* teach. The pedagogy is cruel but it is *competent*. Clint's superhuman skill is in fact downstream of Barton's instruction. The compensatory mechanism here is the capacity to externalize his discipline into another body — to make a student where most narcissists merely make an audience.

### 6.4.3 Sustained delayed gratification in the technical domain
The thousand-hour patience required to drill a single shot is a real strength. It is one of two domains (the other being grudge-maintenance) where he can hold a long arc.

### 6.4.4 Code-of-the-craft loyalty
Within the shooter fraternity he observes a minimal honor code — respect for skill, acknowledgment of a clean shot, even from an enemy. This is thin but present, and it occasionally restrains him from acts a pure antisocial would commit.

### 6.4.5 The persona itself ("Trick Shot")
The stage name is a compensatory device of significant load-bearing capacity. It externalizes the performing self, gives him a container to inhabit when the private self is uninhabitable. When he is *Trick Shot* — costume, posture, calling-card arrow — he is symptom-free in the sense that his defenses are functioning seamlessly. The persona is the defenses made visible.

---

## 6.5 Compensatory Mechanisms — Negative Ledger

These are the maladaptive props — the ways he keeps the organization running at the cost of others.

### 6.5.1 The protégé as narcissistic extension
The single most destructive compensation. The student exists to mirror back the master's excellence. Independent moral judgment by the student is experienced as the mirror cracking — and the response is to break the mirror further rather than examine what it reflects.

### 6.5.2 Grudge-as-coherence
The forty-year grievance against Clint is a *structural support*. It gives him a stable narrative center, a recurring object, a reason for being. Forgiving Clint would not free him — it would dissolve a load-bearing wall. He cannot afford to forgive.

### 6.5.3 Mercenary work as continuity device
The contract killings allow him to continue performing the marksman-self after the carnival circuit has ended and the audience has dispersed. Each contract is, structurally, a small show — a target, a witness (the employer), a clean execution. The work is compensation for the lost stage.

### 6.5.4 Alcohol (low-grade, ambient)
Not foregrounded in canon but consistent with the milieu and with the disinhibition patterns observed. Functions as a minor regulator of the isolation-of-affect: when the wall thins, the bottle thickens it again. A maintenance dose, not a collapse-pattern.

### 6.5.5 Geographic/relational mobility
He moves. He does not stay where he might be known too long, where the projection might be challenged by an accumulated record. The mercenary lifestyle suits the defense; transience protects the projection from contradiction.

### 6.5.6 The terminal-stage grand gesture
The deathbed summons is itself a compensation — a final, theatrical assertion of authorship over his own ending. Faced with the one event he cannot dominate, he stages it as if he could. The compensation is grandiose and partially successful: he does, in fact, get to direct the scene of his death. The price is that he dies in the same posture he lived in, having learned nothing.

---

## 6.6 The Defenses Under Stress — Sequencing

When the organization is pressured, the defenses fire in a near-fixed order. A surveillance file would catalogue the sequence with near-clockwork reliability:

1. **Devaluation** (first 1–2 seconds): the challenger is mentally downgraded.
2. **Isolation of affect** (seconds 2–5): voice flattens, breath slows, the marksman-discipline engages.
3. **Rationalization** (seconds 5–15): the prepared narrative is retrieved.
4. **Projection** (seconds 10–30): the accusation is inverted and returned.
5. **Splitting confirmation** (after seconds 30): the challenger is moved permanently into the *traitor* bin.
6. **Omnipotent control gesture** (if pressure persists): a physical or theatrical act that re-asserts his authorship of the scene — often a demonstration of skill, occasionally violence.

The sequence is so consistent across forty years of recorded confrontations that it can be predicted move-by-move. This is, paradoxically, the operationally useful fact about him: a defensive system this regular is a system that can be *anticipated*, and therefore disrupted, by an operator willing to interrupt the sequence at step 2 — before the isolation of affect has fully engaged — with a stimulus the defenses are not prepared for. Canon shows precisely one stimulus reliably capable of this: *being out-shot in front of a witness.* Nothing else has ever broken the chain.

---

## 6.7 Synthesis

Bernard Barton's defensive architecture is a small set of operations — projection, splitting, reaction formation, isolation, sublimation — deployed with extraordinary consistency over an extraordinarily long arc. The system is efficient: it has kept him functional, productive, and externally coherent across six decades, two careers, and a terminal illness. It is also closed: nothing gets in, nothing is metabolized, nothing is repaired. The very stability that makes him a competent operator makes him an incurable man.

The compensations — the bow, the persona, the pupil, the grudge — are the load-bearing scaffolding around a self that, without them, would have to confront what it did to a thirteen-year-old in a carnival tent. The scaffolding is what he chose to build instead of looking. He is still not looking on the day he dies. That is the architecture, intact, doing its job to the last breath.

— END SECTION 6 —


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON

*Compiled from observable behavior across published record; framework: contemporary psychodynamic (Kernberg structural model), attachment theory (Main/Hesse), affect-regulation theory (Gross), and skill-identity literature (Ericsson's deliberate-practice paradigm read in reverse — what happens to the practitioner when the practice becomes the self).*

This section tracks the subject's interior organization across roughly six discernible life-stages, each reconstructed from the canonical evidence and inferred backward into the years the record does not show. The thesis throughout: **the structure does not change. The compensations change. The defenses get more brittle as the body that hosted them erodes.** What looks like evolution is actually the progressive failure of a single static architecture under accumulating pressure.

---

## STAGE I — Inferred Childhood and Apprenticeship (pre-record, c. ages 0–18)

Canon gives us no documented childhood. The behavior gives us its outline, and the outline is consistent enough across decades that the inference is strong.

**Attachment formation.** The adult Bernard Barton is a textbook *dismissive-avoidant* (Ds on the AAI typology) with strong devaluing features — affect minimized, autonomy over-claimed, attachment figures recalled (when recalled at all) in idealized-flat or contemptuous registers. This organization is not innate; it is built. The most parsimonious developmental hypothesis is a primary caregiver — almost certainly male, almost certainly a trainer or craftsman himself — who dispensed regard strictly as a function of performance and who responded to childhood need with derision or withdrawal. The adult Buck's pedagogy with Clint reproduces this economy with such fidelity that *transmitted* rather than *invented* is the more economical reading.

**Affect regulation, nascent.** A child in that environment learns very early that displays of fear, sadness, or longing precipitate further withdrawal of the regard he depends on. The regulation strategy that emerges — and that remains stable in him for life — is *suppression at the upstream cognitive end* (Gross's antecedent-focused regulation), not downstream expressive control. He does not feel and then mask; he learns not to register the feeling at all. This is why, in the documented record, he never appears to *struggle* with affect. The struggle was won, badly, in childhood. What survives is a man with a narrow band.

**Self-concept, nascent.** Organized around the one variable that produced contingent approval: skill demonstration. By adolescence the self is already a performance, and the performance is already weaponized — there is no Bernard Barton apart from what Bernard Barton can do with his hands and his eye.

**Cognitive style, nascent.** Concrete-operational fixity. Pattern recognition shunted entirely into the perceptual-motor domain, where it is rewarded. Interpersonal pattern recognition atrophies because it was never reinforced and was, in fact, dangerous — to read the caregiver too well is to know what one is being denied.

---

## STAGE II — Young Adult Carnival Performer (c. ages 18–35; pre-Barton-boys)

This is the era in which the structure stabilizes into its lifelong adult form. We see its terminus in the man who later receives Clint; we can back-derive the shape.

**Affect regulation.** Tight, narrow, reliable. The carnival circuit — itinerant, performative, governed by the nightly demand to *deliver* under the lights — is, for him, the ideal environmental scaffold. The work itself does his regulation for him. Every evening he steps into the ring, executes a sequence of feats that demand absolute oculomotor and respiratory composure, and is rewarded by an audience's gasp. The autonomic discipline required to split an apple at thirty paces *is* his anxiolytic. He does not need to develop interior regulation because the job is the regulation.

This is diagnostically central. Many men with this attachment-and-defense profile self-medicate (alcohol, opiates, compulsive sexuality). Buck's depicted alcohol use is consistent with the carnival milieu but never foregrounded as pathological — because the bow is doing the work the bottle does for others. He is *occupationally regulated.* This is why the late-life somatic decline is so destabilizing: it removes his regulator.

**Cognitive style.** Sharpens into its mature form: deeply concrete, ferociously specific in the technical domain (wind, draw weight, broadhead drift, target movement vectors), affectively flat in the interpersonal. He almost certainly can name forty distinguishable arrow-flight defects and cannot name three of his own emotional states.

**Self-concept.** Consolidates around the stage name. The choice of *Trick Shot* over any more dignified marksman-honorific is itself a piece of psychological evidence: he selects an alias that foregrounds the *spectacle* of the act over the discipline behind it — the *wow*, the audience's wonder, the moment of being-seen. Carnival performers who organize around craft tend toward "The Great ___" or guild-style appellations; he chose the one that names the audience's reaction. The self is built outside the self, in the eyes of the crowd.

**Interpersonal pattern.** With Jacques Duquesne (Swordsman) we see his only sustained adult peer relationship. The structure: *parallel performers, mutually competent, mutually contemptuous of outsiders, bonded by shared grift.* He can sustain this. Equals he tolerates if they are equals in skill and complicit in his ethics; this is the only horizontal relationship he is structurally capable of. There is no record of a sustained romantic attachment from this period, and the absence is itself data — sexual or romantic intimacy would require precisely the affect-tolerance he does not have.

---

## STAGE III — The Mentor Period (c. ages 35–45; Clint's adolescence)

The taking-in of the Barton boys is the most psychologically revealing act of his recorded life, and it has been chronically under-read because the surface looks generous.

**The act itself.** Two runaway boys arrive at the carnival. He and Duquesne absorb them. The conventional reading is charity; the structural reading is *acquisition of subordinates*. The boys arrive pre-broken, hungry for the conditional regard that his attachment economy is built to dispense. He recognizes — without consciously formulating — that he has found the ideal recipients of his pedagogy. They will absorb the contingent-approval system because they have nowhere else to go.

**Affect regulation under the new conditions.** This is where the first long-term destabilization begins, though it will not become visible for decades. Genuine proto-paternal affect *does* arise in him toward Clint — the evidence is the forty-year obsessional return to the relationship, which is not the behavior of a man indifferent to the object. But the moment that affect threatens to register consciously, the *reaction formation* engages: warmth converts to harshness at the threshold of awareness. Praise is metered to near-zero. Affection expresses itself only as the prolongation of training. The training scenes in Hawkeye Vol.1 #4 show this with brutal clarity — he stays in the practice yard with the boy past exhaustion, which is, in his interior economy, *the entire vocabulary of love he possesses*, and which the boy correctly experiences as relentlessness.

This is a man who is, at this stage, *being changed by the relationship without admitting it.* The change is invisible to him and invisible to Clint; it will only become legible in the violence of the rupture.

**Cognitive style.** Acquires a new sub-domain of expertise — pedagogy — at which he becomes genuinely excellent in the technical sense and genuinely catastrophic in the relational sense. His pattern-recognition for the mechanics of teaching archery is canon-confirmed superlative (he produces, in Clint, the finest non-enhanced marksman of his generation). His pattern-recognition for the *child* in front of him remains zero. He sees the draw-arm; he does not see the boy.

**Self-concept.** Begins, here, to fold the protégé into the self. Clint becomes a *narcissistic extension* in Kohut's sense — an external object that carries part of the self's grandiose representation. This is the load-bearing structural change of the entire life. From this point forward, Clint is not separate from him in his internal cosmology. Clint's skill is his skill displayed at one remove. This is why the betrayal, when it comes, registers at the depth it does — Clint exposes the embezzlement not as an external whistleblower but as *a part of Buck's own self* turning against him. The wound is structurally autoimmune.

---

## STAGE IV — The Rupture (a single year, mid-life)

The embezzlement is discovered. Clint exposes it. Buck beats him and abandons him.

**Affect regulation, breach event.** The exposure is the only documented moment in his life where the regulation fails in the upward direction — the suppressed affect breaks containment and emerges as cold rage. Note the *cold*, not hot. Even in failure his system fails toward control. He does not lose composure; he weaponizes the composure. The beating is calibrated — he stops short of killing the boy, which is itself diagnostic. A purely antisocial or sadistic organization would not stop. He stops because the protégé must remain alive to carry the narrative of betrayal, which is the new structure he is building in real time.

**Cognitive style, breach event.** Within minutes — almost certainly within the duration of the beating itself — the *reframe* engages. The theft becomes Clint's disloyalty. This is not a lie he tells; it is a perceptual reorganization. He genuinely walks away believing he is the wronged party. The cognitive operation here is classical *projective identification* in the Kleinian sense — the unbearable content (I stole; I am the bad one) is evacuated into the other (he betrayed; he is the bad one) and from that moment forward, Buck *perceives* the world organized around this exchange. This is the moment the lifelong delusion crystallizes.

**Self-concept, breach event.** The narcissistic extension is torn out. The boy who was the carrier of part of his grandiose self has revealed himself to be a separate, judging agent — which is intolerable, because separate-and-judging is the position only the punitive caregiver of childhood was permitted to occupy. To survive the rupture without structural collapse, Buck must recast Clint not as judge but as traitor. He does. The structure holds. But it now has, embedded in it, an unfinished object — a piece of self that walked away wearing another man's face. He will spend the next thirty years trying to retrieve it, on his terms.

---

## STAGE V — The Mercenary Decades (c. ages 45–65)

The longest stretch and the least examined in canon, but the most diagnostically rich for chronic-state assessment.

**Affect regulation, chronic.** Reverts to baseline narrow band, but the carnival's nightly regulatory scaffold is gone. He replaces it with *contract work* — discrete, high-skill, time-bounded jobs that reproduce the perform-under-pressure structure of the carnival in a more violent register. The mercenary marksman role is not an ethical drift; it is a *regulatory necessity*. He needs the recurring high-stakes performance to keep the system stable. Without it he would, by middle age, be facing the unmetabolized contents of the rupture, and the structure would not hold.

The selection of *Clint* as recurrent contract target is the tell. There are other archers, other targets, other markets. He keeps taking the Clint-adjacent jobs. This is not opportunism. This is the *repetition compulsion* — Freud's term, but here the description is mechanical and exact. He is trying, again and again, to restage the rupture and produce a different outcome: one in which he, the master, dominates and the protégé acknowledges. He never gets it. Each restaging fails. He returns to the next one.

**Cognitive style, chronic.** Continues to sharpen technically and continues to flatline interpersonally, with one new feature emerging: a *narrative rigidity* about the Clint relationship that hardens with each retelling. By his late fifties his account of the original rupture is almost ritualistic — the same phrases, the same emphases, the same exoneration. This is the *consolidation phase* of a defensive narrative; the story has been told enough times in his own head that the original event is no longer accessible to him in any other form. He could not, at this point, recall the truth of the embezzlement even if he wanted to. The screen memory is the only memory.

**Self-concept, chronic.** Increasingly organized around the dyad-of-two: him and Clint, master and traitor, the cosmos reduced to a single unfinished line. Other relationships continue to exist (handlers, employers, the Swordsman in earlier years, criminal associates) but they are increasingly peripheral. The self has narrowed.

**Subclinical paranoid drift.** A new feature emerges in late mercenary years: a low-grade paranoid coloration of perception, particularly around questions of loyalty and respect. Not Paranoid PD — it remains situational and reality-tested in the operational domain — but a *characterological tightening* in which slights are registered faster and forgiven less. This is consistent with malignant narcissism in its progression; Kernberg's clinical observation that the malignant variant tends toward increasing paranoid features in the fifth and sixth decades is borne out here.

**Probable alcohol use, chronic.** The carnival-era drinking, never foregrounded, almost certainly progresses through these decades into a steady, controlled, *functional* dependency — the kind that supports rather than disrupts the structure. He is not the drunk who falls down; he is the drunk who steadies the hand. This is the more dangerous pattern clinically because it does not present for treatment and accelerates somatic decline silently.

---

## STAGE VI — Terminal Phase (c. ages 65+; cancer diagnosis through death)

This is the period in which the canon catches up to what was always present, and the structure, deprived of its scaffolds, surfaces undisguised.

**Affect regulation, terminal.** Begins to fail. The somatic decline removes the perform-under-pressure regulator that has held the system stable since adolescence. The hands shake; the eye softens; the draw weakens. With each somatic increment, the unmetabolized affect of a lifetime presses closer to the surface. The expected clinical course in such a subject is one of two paths: *depressive collapse* (the avoidant defenses crumble; grief floods in) or *grandiose escalation* (the defenses mobilize one last time in a final, theatrical assertion of mastery). Buck takes the second path, which the differential predicts — a man whose structure has held for sixty years does not, at sixty-five, suddenly develop the introspective machinery required for depressive metabolization. He goes the other way.

**Cognitive style, terminal.** Narrows further into a single project: the choreographed ending. The deathbed summons is not a fog; it is the clearest cognitive product of his life. He has *planned* it. He has selected the protégé as the instrument. He has scripted the encounter to produce a specific final state — the master, dying, hands the death itself to the student, who must either accept (and become the killer Buck always implicitly was, retroactively justifying Buck) or refuse (and confirm the original "betrayal," retroactively justifying Buck). It is a closed loop. Whatever Clint does, Buck wins. This is high-order strategic cognition in the service of a totally pathological aim, and it is the apex expression of the structure.

**Self-concept, terminal.** Final and most revealing move: the *transfer of the alias*. He bestows "Trick Shot" on a successor. The conventional reading is legacy. The structural reading is *the self refusing to die*. He cannot bear to take the name into nonexistence, because the name *is* the self — there is no Bernard Barton underneath, only the performance and its label. By installing the label in another body he produces a kind of survival; the trick continues to be shot after the shooter is gone. This is the only form of continuity his organization is capable of imagining, because the only continuity he has ever known is contingent-skill-transmission. He dies as he lived, dispensing conditional regard.

**The cruelty intensifies, not diffuses.** The clinical literature on terminal-phase personality disorder is unambiguous: well-organized narcissistic structures, deprived of their compensations, *do not soften*. The softening is a wish of the survivors. Buck does not soften. The deathbed-Buck is the truest Buck, and he is worse than any earlier Buck, because the regulators are gone and the structure stands naked.

---

## SYNTHESIS: WHAT EVOLVED, WHAT DID NOT

**Did not evolve:**
- The attachment organization (dismissive-avoidant with contemptuous features) — stable from late childhood to death.
- The core defenses (projection, reaction formation, sublimation into craft, splitting) — stable in kind, varying only in intensity.
- The self-concept's organizing principle (mastery-as-self, performance-as-existence) — stable from carnival debut to dying gesture.
- The cognitive style (concrete-tactical, perceptually acute, interpersonally blind) — stable.
- The interpersonal economy (contingent regard, autonomy-as-betrayal) — stable.

**Did evolve (in the sense of compensatory shift, not structural change):**
- The regulatory scaffold — carnival → mercenary contracting → terminal choreography. Each transition occasioned by the failure of the prior scaffold, each adopted to preserve the same underlying structure.
- The narrative rigidity around the rupture — accreted over decades into an unrevisable screen memory.
- The paranoid coloration — subclinical drift in the fifth and sixth decades, characteristic of malignant narcissistic aging.
- The somatic-affective coupling's *vulnerability* — increasing through life as the body that hosted the regulation deteriorated.

**The longitudinal point.** Bernard Barton's life is not a story of psychological development. It is a story of a single architecture, built early under duress, sustained for sixty years by progressively more violent scaffolds, and failing at the end in the manner the architecture itself dictated. He did not become the man at the deathbed. He had always been him. The carnival lights, the mentor years, the mercenary decades — all were forms the same man took. The protégé he wounded was the only person who ever saw him whole, which is precisely why he could never be forgiven for it.

— END LONGITUDINAL PROFILE —


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON

**File subsection:** 4 of 12 — Clinical Formulation
**Compiled from:** longitudinal behavioral record (carnival period, mercenary period, terminal period); third-party witness statements (C. Barton primary; secondary: Duquesne residual record, Carson Carnival personnel, late-period contract employers); somatic file; psychological workup (Section 3).
**Caveat:** Subject was never voluntarily evaluated. All formulations are derived behaviorally and longitudinally. The diagnostic confidence is high precisely because the behavioral record spans roughly four decades, multiple radically different contexts (carnival employee, criminal contractor, dying man), and multiple categories of relational partner (peer, protégé, employer, enemy). A personality organization that holds its shape across that range of pressures is, by definition, characterological rather than situational.

---

## 4.1 Principal Diagnosis

**Narcissistic Personality Disorder, malignant subtype, with prominent antisocial features and rigid grandiose presentation.**
(DSM-5-TR 301.81 / F60.81; malignant overlay per Kernberg's clinical descriptor, not a coded entity but a clinically essential qualifier here.)

This is the load-bearing diagnosis. Every other condition discussed below is either (a) downstream of it, (b) comorbid texture, or (c) actively excluded by it. The grandiose subtype is specified rather than the vulnerable; subject does not present the hypersensitive, shame-collapsed, depressively-tinged variant. His grandiosity is exoskeletal, performative, and externally directed.

### 4.1.1 Criterion-Level Mapping

The DSM-5-TR requires five of nine. Subject demonstrably presents at minimum seven, with longitudinal evidence:

1. **Grandiose sense of self-importance**, organized around marksmanship mastery and the title-name "Trick Shot." The alias is itself a diagnostic artifact — chosen not to describe a function (Marksman, Sniper, Archer) but to flag a spectacle (a *trick* shot, the one nobody else makes). The self-concept is bound to being-the-one-who-can-do-what-others-cannot.

2. **Preoccupation with fantasies of unlimited success / brilliance / ideal mastery**, expressed through obsessional drilling regimens, the demand for absolute compliance from the protégé, and the late-life staging of the deathbed succession (which is, on its surface, about legacy continuity — and on its structure, a fantasy of mastery so total it can choose its own ending).

3. **Belief in being "special" / understandable only by other elite practitioners**: contemptuous dismissal of non-shooters, near-religious investment in the small fraternity of those who can match him. The Swordsman is tolerated as confederate explicitly on competence grounds.

4. **Requirement of excessive admiration**, masked in the carnival period by the audience-economy (he gets his supply from the crowd) and in later periods by the demand that contract employers acknowledge his unique value, and that Clint, even in adversarial encounters, recognize his teaching.

5. **Sense of entitlement** — most plainly visible in the embezzlement: he is *owed* a larger share than the carnival pays him, because he is the act that fills seats. The theft is not framed (by him) as theft; it is framed as collection.

6. **Interpersonally exploitative**: protégé as narcissistic extension; partner used as cover; later employers used and discarded; the dying-day summons of Clint is itself exploitative — Clint is conscripted to perform a function in Buck's death narrative.

7. **Lacks empathy** — the load-bearing evidence is the abandonment scene: a beaten child is left bleeding, and the subject's later reconstruction of the event identifies the child as the moral failure. This is not deceit; deceit would be more flexible. This is a constitutional inability to occupy the other's perspective when doing so would impose narcissistic injury.

8. **Arrogant, haughty behaviors / attitudes** — contempt is the default interpersonal posture. His instructional manner during training was characterized by withholding, ridicule of error, and a sparing dispensation of approval calibrated to keep the protégé chasing it.

(Criterion 8 in DSM enumeration — envy of others or belief others envy him — is harder to evidence cleanly. There is suggestive material: his preoccupation with Clint's eventual fame reads as displaced envy structured as proprietary claim ("I made him"). Counted as probable but not definitive.)

Seven of nine clearly substantiated; one probable. This is well above threshold and would meet criteria under any reasonable clinical reading.

### 4.1.2 The Malignant Overlay

Kernberg's malignant narcissism is the clinical specifier that makes sense of why this subject is dangerous rather than merely insufferable. It requires the NPD core plus:

- **Ego-syntonic aggression.** Subject does not experience his cruelty as a problem. The training severity, the beating, the assassination contracts targeting his former student — all are integrated into the self without dissonance. There is no record of remorse, no record of self-questioning, no record of even rhetorical apology. Cruelty is *consonant* with the self-image, not a deviation requiring repair.

- **Antisocial behavior** (see 4.2 below) — present but subordinate.

- **Paranoid orientation under stress.** Surfaces specifically in late-period confrontations: as the body fails, the suspicion that he is being patronized, pitied, or managed by Clint reads everything as condescension. This paranoid streak is *state-dependent* (rises with somatic and status threat) rather than trait-pervasive, which is why he does not meet PPD primarily — but its presence under stress is exactly what Kernberg describes.

- **Sadistic gratification in dominance contexts.** Not pleasure in suffering qua suffering (see 4.3, differential against Sadistic PD), but enjoyment of the exercise of dominance. The distinction matters clinically: he is not collecting pain; he is collecting submission, and pain is the medium.

The malignant qualifier is what raises this subject from a difficult personality to a Tier-3 adversary. Pure NPD individuals are typically more brittle than dangerous to others; malignant narcissism produces the durable, organized, instrumentally violent presentation we see across the record.

---

## 4.2 Comorbid: Antisocial Personality Disorder Features (Subthreshold-to-Threshold)

DSM-5-TR 301.7 / F60.2.

The record supports several ASPD criteria — repeated unlawful acts (embezzlement, contract murder, assault); deceit (the carnival fraud, the ongoing manipulation of the protégé narrative); aggression and assaults; consistent irresponsibility (carnival obligations defaulted, contractual obligations honored only when convenient); lack of remorse. Criterion A is met multiply.

The diagnostic question is whether ASPD is *primary* or *secondary* to the NPD. The file supports secondary.

**Reasons ASPD is not the organizing diagnosis:**

- **Insufficient impulsivity.** True ASPD presentations are marked by failure to plan ahead and impulsive decision-making. Subject is methodical to a fault. His criminality is calculated, deferred, and patient. The Clint-directed campaign of mercenary contracts spans years and is structured.
- **Insufficient shallowness of affect.** Classical ASPD (and especially the psychopathic high-end) presents flat or shallow affect with poor object constancy. Subject demonstrates the *opposite* problem: an object relationship with Clint that has held grievance for forty years. That is not psychopathic affect; that is narcissistically-organized affect.
- **The criminality serves the narcissism, not vice versa.** His thefts and contracts are means to status, mastery-demonstration, and dominance. A primary ASPD subject would steal for the proceeds and walk away; this subject steals and then constructs an elaborate self-justification in which he is the wronged party. That justification is the NPD signature.

**Diagnostic position:** Code ASPD features as comorbid descriptor (V-code adjacency / specifier rather than full second axis-II diagnosis), recognizing that in operational terms the criminal behavior must be planned around, but the *predictive* diagnosis for behavior is the narcissistic structure.

---

## 4.3 Differential — What He Is Not, and Why

This is the heart of the assessment. Behavioral mimics of NPD-malignant are numerous, and the file demands rigorous exclusion.

### 4.3.1 Psychopathy (Hare PCL-R high-end)

**Excluded as primary.** PCL-R Factor 1 (Interpersonal/Affective) requires glib charm, pathological lying, lack of remorse, shallow affect, callousness, failure to accept responsibility. Subject meets remorse-absence and responsibility-failure, but fails *shallow affect* decisively. The forty-year grievance toward Clint is the single most diagnostic data point in the file: psychopathic individuals do not sustain grudges of that duration and intensity, because grudges require an object-cathexis psychopaths do not form. Subject's hatred *requires* love-residue to fuel it. He cares, malignantly. That is NPD, not psychopathy.

Factor 2 (Lifestyle/Antisocial) is better matched but not sufficient on its own. The PCL-R cutoff for diagnosis is not approached.

Estimated PCL-R, conservative: 18–24. Elevated, sub-threshold, with characteristic Factor-1 deficits relative to a true psychopath.

### 4.3.2 Sadistic Personality Disorder (DSM-III-R appendix; not in current DSM but clinically useful)

**Excluded as primary.** Sadistic PD requires cruelty *qua* cruelty — pleasure in another's pain as the endpoint. Subject's cruelty is *instrumental to dominance*. The distinction is visible in his behavior: he does not prolong suffering when domination is achieved; he disengages once the hierarchy is reasserted. A primary sadist would extend the beating; subject ends it once Clint is established as subordinate-and-beaten. Cruelty is a *tool* of his pathology, not its content.

Sadistic features present as accent, not core.

### 4.3.3 Borderline Personality Disorder

**Excluded.** BPD requires affective instability, identity diffusion, abandonment terror, and chronic emptiness. Subject demonstrates none of these. His affect is constricted to a narrow operational band; his identity is rigidly (if pathologically) integrated around the marksman-master self-image; he is the *abandoner*, not the abandonment-terrified; and there is no evidence of the existential emptiness that drives BPD impulsivity.

Worth noting because superficial readings of his late-life "neediness" toward Clint might suggest borderline organization. They are not the same phenomenon. The borderline patient cannot tolerate aloneness; this subject can tolerate aloneness indefinitely — what he cannot tolerate is *aloneness without an audience having witnessed the mastery first*. That is narcissistic supply collapse, not abandonment depression.

### 4.3.4 Paranoid Personality Disorder

**Excluded as primary, present as state feature.** PPD requires pervasive distrust across contexts from early adulthood. Subject's suspicion is *situational* (under status threat, exposure threat, somatic threat) and *well-calibrated* (he was, in fact, being exposed by Clint; he is, in fact, being pitied by the dying-bed visitors). Calibrated suspicion in genuinely adversarial conditions is not PPD; it is competence. The paranoid coloration in late-period confrontations is the Kernberg malignant overlay, not a separate paranoid disorder.

### 4.3.5 Major Depressive Disorder / Persistent Depressive Disorder

**Excluded.** Terminal cancer is the natural experiment that rules this out. A depressively-organized subject confronting terminal diagnosis would present withdrawal, anhedonia, vegetative signs, comfort-seeking, possible suicidal ideation passive in character. Subject presents the *inverse*: escalation, grandiose terminal gesture, increased control behavior, summoning rather than withdrawal. He does not collapse inward under existential threat; he expands outward against it. This is characterologically incompatible with depressive organization.

### 4.3.6 Substance Use Disorder

**Probable, mild-to-moderate (alcohol), not characterological.** Carnival milieu and depicted irritability are consistent with chronic moderate use. There is no evidence that intoxication mediates the principal pathology. The cruelty, the embezzlement, the abandonment, and the deathbed staging all occur in operationally sober states. Code as comorbid lifestyle factor, not as explanatory.

### 4.3.7 Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (developmental)

**Inferred etiological background, not active diagnosis.** Subject's pedagogical rigidity — the precision of his withholding, the architecture of conditional regard — has the polished quality of *transmitted* behavior. He did not invent the regime he imposed on Clint; he reproduced it. This strongly implies a developmental history under a comparably harsh figure. However, there is no record of intrusion symptoms, hyperarousal in the PTSD sense, avoidance behavior, or negative cognitions characteristic of PTSD. What is present is *characterological scarring* — the trauma metabolized into personality structure rather than expressed as PTSD symptomatology. This is the identification-with-the-aggressor route, not the traumatized-self route.

### 4.3.8 Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder

**Excluded as primary, present as accent.** The relentless drilling, the perfectionism, the rigidity around skill standards superficially suggest OCPD. But OCPD organizes around *rule-correctness and moral rectitude*; subject is comfortable with criminality, has no apparent moral perfectionism, and his rigidity is in service of narcissistic mastery rather than rule-following. The perfectionism is narcissistic in tone (must be the best), not obsessive in tone (must be done correctly). Accent only.

### 4.3.9 Schizoid / Schizotypal Spectrum

**Excluded.** Subject is interpersonally engaged (cruelly, but engaged); he requires audience; he forms object relationships (twisted ones, but durable). Schizoid detachment and schizotypal cognitive oddity are absent.

### 4.3.10 Bipolar Spectrum

**Excluded.** No episodic mood elevation, no episodic depression, no cyclical pattern. Baseline affect is *constrictedly stable*, not cyclically variable. The escalations seen are situational and characterologically consistent, not episodic.

### 4.3.11 Neurocognitive Disorder (late-period)

**Considered, not supported.** Terminal cancer raises the question of paraneoplastic CNS involvement or metastatic effect on cognition. Late-period behavior shows no cognitive slippage — tactical reasoning, verbal precision, and motor performance are preserved into the deathbed period. The terminal pathology is somatic, not neurocognitive. The escalating cruelty is *psychological* response to somatic decline, not organic disinhibition.

---

## 4.4 Etiological Formulation

Causation must be inferred from structure, as no developmental record exists.

The convergent evidence — the polished transmissibility of the harsh pedagogy, the perfect economy of conditional regard he runs with Clint, the inability to conceive of relational currency other than performance, the foreclosed introspective capacity — points to a developmental history under a figure who imposed exactly this regime on him. The hypothesis: a paternal or quasi-paternal trainer figure (possibly biological father, possibly an early carnival mentor) who offered acceptance contingent on demonstrable skill and withdrew it absolutely on failure or disobedience. Subject internalized both positions: he is *both* the cold trainer and the chasing protégé, and he has resolved the internal split by always occupying the trainer position with others.

The reproduction with Clint is therefore overdetermined. It serves: (a) the repetition compulsion typical of unresolved developmental trauma; (b) the narcissistic need to be the powerful one in the dyad rather than the dependent one; (c) the externalization of the internal critic onto an actual external target. Clint is, structurally, the young Buck — and Buck has the chance, with Clint, to enact the trainer-position perfectly. The abandonment after the embezzlement exposure is the moment the protégé asserts moral autonomy and thereby ceases to function as the externalized young self. At that point Clint becomes useless and must be punished — punished, specifically, for having had the moral courage Buck himself was never permitted.

This formulation also explains the otherwise puzzling forty-year hold the grievance has on him. Clint did not merely expose a theft; Clint enacted, in front of him, the developmental moment Buck never had — the moment of moral autonomy against the trainer. That is the unbearable injury. That is what the malignant narcissist cannot let go of, because what was injured was not the surface ego but the foundational compromise his entire personality was built to maintain.

---

## 4.5 Course Over Time

- **Carnival period (formation, early adulthood through mid-career):** organization stable and ego-syntonic. Audience-supply abundant. Pathology functional and producing professional success. Cruelty modulated by social context.

- **Post-exposure / mercenary period (middle years):** organization stable but increasingly compensated through criminality. Loss of legitimate audience (carnival severance) drives substitution of contract violence as supply replacement — being feared as a marksman is a degraded but viable form of being witnessed. Clint-directed contracts begin in this period; the compulsive returns to the protégé site begin here and never cease.

- **Late period (declining body, pre-diagnosis):** subtle increase in irritability, status-vigilance, and the proportion of contracts that route through Clint. The somatic erosion is the destabilizer; the pathology compensates with escalation.

- **Terminal period (diagnosis through death):** decompensation in the form of *exaggerated* characteristic behavior, not novel symptoms. The deathbed summons is the pathology at its purest, undefended by the buffering effects of ongoing professional function. Grandiose terminal gesture, conscription of Clint into the death-narrative, refusal of comfort, refusal of repair, insistence on staging the ending. This is the diagnostic apex, not the mellowing.

The course is therefore one of **stable characterological organization under increasing somatic and contextual pressure, with decompensation expressed as intensification of the existing pattern rather than emergence of new symptomatology.** This is the classical course of a Cluster B personality disorder of malignant variety: it does not soften with age, illness, or proximity to death. It crystallizes.

---

## 4.6 Final Diagnostic Statement

> **Principal:** Narcissistic Personality Disorder, grandiose presentation, malignant subtype (Kernberg), with prominent paranoid features state-elevated under threat.
> **Comorbid:** Antisocial Personality Disorder features, subthreshold-to-threshold, secondary to and instrumentalized by the narcissistic organization.
> **Accent features:** Obsessive-compulsive (perfectionism in service of mastery, not rectitude); sadistic (dominance-instrumental, not pleasure-primary).
> **Comorbid lifestyle factor:** probable alcohol use disorder, mild-to-moderate, not characterologically explanatory.
> **Etiological inference:** developmental history under a harsh conditional-regard figure; identification-with-the-aggressor resolution; reproduction in the protégé relationship.
> **Course:** stable, ego-syntonic, decompensating into intensified pattern under somatic and existential threat. Terminal period represents diagnostic apex.
> **Treatability (academic):** Very low. The pathology is ego-syntonic, the introspective capacity is structurally foreclosed, and any therapeutic gesture is registered as weakness in the appellant. Subject would not have presented voluntarily and would not have engaged authentically if compelled.
> **Forensic / operational implication:** Predictably dangerous. Behavior is forecastable from the diagnosis to a degree unusual in personality pathology — precisely because the structure is so rigidly integrated. Handlers should expect the pattern described in Section 5 (Personality) to hold under every form of pressure short of death, and to *amplify* under several.

— END SECTION 4 / PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL —
*Continue to Section 5: Personality Architecture & Operational Profile.*


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON (alias TRICK SHOT)

*Compiled from longitudinal observation across carnival-era reports, mercenary-period contact records, and adversarial encounter logs (Hawkeye Vol.1 #1–4; Solo Avengers #1–4; West Coast Avengers run; Hawkeye: Blindspot; cross-references in Mockingbird and Crossfire files). This is a manner-atlas: how he moves, decides, withholds, escalates, and reveals himself in micro-behavior across every recorded condition.*

---

## I. THE BASELINE BODY

Before any condition is layered on, there is a stance.

He stands with his weight set rear-foot heavy, the front foot turned out perhaps fifteen degrees — an archer's stance held even when the bow is not in hand, even when ordering coffee, even when leaning in a doorway. The pelvis is squared, the shoulder line level. He does not slouch, and he does not preen; the posture is *operational*. It is the posture of a man who has trained the standing-still part of his life as deliberately as the shooting part.

The hands are kept low and visible — at the belt, on a thigh, around a cup — almost never gesturing above the sternum. When they do rise it is to point, never to illustrate. Speech-accompanying hand-talk is absent. He sits with the forearms resting along the chair arms, palms down, fingers slightly spread, as if continuously assessing the trembling that he refuses to allow.

The eyes do the work the hands refuse. He scans in deliberate sectors — a quartering sweep, near-to-far, left-to-right, then a return check on the entry he came through. This is not paranoia; it is a carny's habit, a marksman's habit, and an old criminal's habit braided. He blinks less than the population mean, particularly when listening. Conversation partners frequently report the sensation of being *sighted in*.

His breath is slow, deep, abdominal-led. Under any circumstance — argument, ambush, anesthesia recovery — the resting respiration stays in the eight-to-twelve range. This is the most reliable physical signature on file. He has trained his autonomic floor.

He smells of: rosin, gun oil despite his weapon of choice, sometimes peppermint (he chews leaf to mask the alcohol), the particular ozone of old leather. The smell does not change with mood; he is fastidious about presentation in a flinty, monastic way — not vain, but kept.

---

## II. CALM (Operational Baseline)

In a state he himself would call "settled," the tells cluster around economy.

He speaks in short declaratives — usually under nine words. Imperatives outnumber questions roughly four to one. When he does ask, he asks closed-ended: *You ready. You hit it. You sure.* The interrogative inflection is faint, sometimes absent, so the question is also already a verdict.

He holds eye contact at the upper edge of comfortable duration, then *releases* — does not look away, looks *through*. The release is the social signal that the exchange is over; subordinates learn it within hours. People who do not learn it he begins to treat as already gone.

Hands at calm: one habit dominates — he turns small objects between thumb and the pads of his first two fingers. An arrow nock, a coin, a matchbook corner, a bottle cap. Always the same hand (right). Always the same finger pattern. The rotation is slow, three to four turns per minute, and stops the instant someone calls his name. This is the closest thing he has to a fidget, and it is the most diagnostic single behavior: when he is rotating, he is *thinking forward*; when the rotation stops mid-turn, he has just decided something he is not going to announce.

He drinks coffee black, in shallow swallows, and lets it go cold in front of him. He never finishes a cup. He orders food and eats half. The unfinished thing on the table is a small constant signal that he does not need what is offered.

Movement at calm is *deliberate but unhurried*. He turns from the hips, not the shoulders — an archer's pivot. He rises from sitting using only his legs, no hand-push from the chair. He enters rooms by stepping fully through the threshold and then halting one pace in, to read the geometry before committing further. He chooses, every time, the seat with the wall behind it and an angle on both the door and the window. If both seats are taken he stands.

He does not initiate touch. Handshakes are accepted, returned with a single pump, released early. He does not clap a shoulder, does not lean. The only physical contact he reliably initiates is the *correction-touch* — two fingers on a student's elbow or wrist to adjust posture during instruction. That touch is light, brief, and the only tenderness in his repertoire, though he would not name it tenderness and would punish anyone who did.

---

## III. UNDER INSTRUCTION (The Pedagogical Condition)

Teaching is the condition in which he is most himself, and therefore most legible.

The teaching voice is *quieter* than his conversational voice, not louder. He pitches it just under the ambient noise floor, forcing the student to lean. This is deliberate; he learned it from someone who did it to him.

He demonstrates once. He does not demonstrate twice. If asked to repeat he refuses with a flat *Watch better next time* and moves on. The student therefore learns to watch with terror, which is a learning state he understands and approves of.

Praise budget: documented at roughly one approving utterance per forty to sixty corrections, and the approval is almost never the word *good*. The reliable forms are *That's the shot*, *That's it*, and — at the absolute ceiling — a single nod and the half-second of held eye contact that the student will remember for life. He has, on record, never said *I'm proud of you* to any human being.

Correction style: physical first, verbal second. He moves the body part before he explains why it was wrong. The explanation, when it comes, is technical and impersonal — *Your draw elbow's dropping*, never *You're being lazy*. This is one of his few clean traits: the critique stays on the mechanics, not the person, *until* the person fails morally rather than technically. Then the critique becomes the person, total and unappealable.

He times his students. Not with a watch — by count, under his breath, lip-only, no sound. The count is the second-most-diagnostic micro-behavior on file. When he is counting he is evaluating; when he stops counting and the lips go still, he has finished his judgment.

He will not stand directly behind a student at the line. He stands at the four-o'clock position relative to a right-handed shooter, one and a half body lengths back, where he can see both the bow hand and the face. He never blocks the shot. He never breathes on the neck. The discipline of the stance is, paradoxically, a form of respect for the act of shooting that he does not extend to the shooter.

---

## IV. STRESS (Non-Threat Pressure — Time, Money, Audience, Surveillance)

Stress in the absence of an enemy produces *contraction*, not display.

The blink rate drops further. The speech shortens further — sometimes to single words and head movements. He stops chewing the peppermint. The object-rotation habit (II above) ceases entirely; the hand goes flat on the nearest stable surface.

He becomes meticulously polite to strangers under stress and curt with intimates, which is exactly inverted from the population norm and is diagnostic. The politeness is *distance-keeping* — the more he needs to control his environment, the more he treats it as a paying audience.

Decision-making under stress narrows to binary: he will do the thing he has done before, or he will leave. He does not improvise socially under load. He will improvise *technically* — alter a shot, reroute an approach — but the interpersonal repertoire shrinks to two moves: *command* and *exit*. Subordinates learn to read which is coming by watching the front foot. If it pivots toward them, command. If it pivots toward the door, exit, and there will be no goodbye.

Money pressure produces a specific tic: he counts cash twice, openly, and re-folds the bills against the thigh in a sharp crease. He pays exact change when possible and refuses small kindnesses (a drink bought for him, a tab covered) with an offended micro-flinch he believes is invisible.

Being watched (surveilled, audited, evaluated by a superior) produces the *display* version of his stance — shoulders set fractionally back, chin lifted perhaps two degrees. He becomes a man performing his own competence. The performance is convincing and is the reason for most of his employment.

---

## V. THREAT (Physical, Imminent)

Here the years of grooved practice show, and the personality almost recedes.

The breath does not change. The blink does not change. What changes is the eye-scan rate, which accelerates to a fast quartering with brief fixations on hands, hips, sightlines, and exits. He identifies, on entry to any threat scenario, the *three best shooting positions in the room from which to defend it* — verified by his consistent gravitation to those points across decades of recorded encounters.

He does not draw first. He does not even reach first. He *settles* — weight slightly lower, front foot a half-step out — and waits to be drawn upon. This is partly tactical (counter-draw discipline) and partly characterological: he requires the other party to commit the moral act, so that the violence that follows is, in his own narration, response rather than initiation.

Once committed, his violence is economical to the point of dryness. He uses what is in his hand. He shoots once where one shot will do. He does not pursue. He does not gloat in motion; the gloat is verbal and comes after the body is down. The body, when down, is checked with the toe, not the hand — he kneels for no one.

Voice in threat: drops a half-octave, slows, gains the carnival barker's *projection without volume*. He can be heard across a warehouse without ever shouting. He uses the second person almost exclusively in fight talk — *You shouldn't have. You knew. You always knew.* The grammar of guilt is reflexive; even in active combat, blame externalization runs in the background.

He does not take hostages. He does not threaten bystanders. This is not principle; bystanders are *audience*, and the audience is sacrosanct in the carny grammar he never quite shed. He will, however, shoot through one to reach the shot if the shot is the protégé.

---

## VI. INTIMACY (Such As It Is)

The intimacy condition is the rarest and most distorted in the file.

He does not have sexual partners on record. The carnival period implies them; nothing is named; this in itself is data — a man who keeps no woman's name in any conversation across forty years is keeping the absence on purpose. Affection of any kind he treats as a *tell* in the other person, a weakness to be filed.

The closest analog to intimacy in the record is the late-night training session, alone with one student, lamp burning, range cold. In those scenes (Hawkeye Vol.1 #4 flashback; Blindspot interiorities) his voice softens by a measurable amount, the sentences lengthen slightly, and he tells fragments of his own history — *I had a man taught me*, *Used to shoot off horseback when I was your size* — but always in service of a lesson, and always cut short with a return to the drill. The softening lasts perhaps two minutes per session and is followed, with predictable regularity, by an unusually harsh correction. The pattern reads as a man *punishing himself* for having warmed.

Physical intimacy proxies: he will hand a student his own bow to try, briefly, perhaps once a year. The bow is the most sacred object in his cosmology. The lending of it is the single largest gesture of regard he is capable of. He takes it back without comment, inspects the string with his thumb, and the moment passes unmarked.

Reconciliation offers — from Clint, decades on — produce a stereotyped sequence: a long stare, a half-smile that does not reach the eyes, a single dismissive syllable (*Hn*, or *Boy*), and then a calculated cruelty calibrated to the specific offer made. If the offer was money, he insults the protégé's earnings. If the offer was forgiveness, he forgives nothing back and uses the word *weak*. If the offer was simply presence, he turns the body away — the most violent of his repertoire, because turning away from a shot is the ultimate negation in his grammar.

---

## VII. GRIEF

He does not grieve in any form recognizable to the population norm.

When the Swordsman — his closest documented peer — dies, his recorded response is to drink one extra finger of whiskey at the end of the night and to clean his bow longer than usual. No funeral attendance on record. No spoken eulogy. No interruption in workflow the following day. The grief is *absorbed into the practice*. He shoots, the next morning, for an extra hour. The arrows go where they always go.

Anniversary behavior (inferred from carnival-era contacts and a single noted pattern in mercenary scheduling): he refuses contracts in early autumn, the season of the carnival's collapse and the embezzlement exposure. The refusal is never explained. He goes off the grid for roughly two weeks and resurfaces unchanged. Where he goes is not in any file. The likeliest hypothesis is that he goes nowhere — he holes up, drinks more than usual, and emerges.

He does not visit graves. He does not keep photographs. The carnival-era trunk he traveled with contained, by a single witness account, exactly one non-functional object: a pewter shot glass with a faded inscription, kept wrapped in oilcloth. He has never been observed to drink from it. The provenance is unknown and he has never been asked.

When grief presses against the defenses hard enough to leak — which is rare, and almost exclusively in the late terminal period — it surfaces *as contempt for the dead*. He speaks ill of those he has lost, in clipped past-tense dismissals (*Fool got himself killed*), and the dismissal is the closest thing to mourning his organization can produce. The contempt is the love, inverted, because the love was never permitted in the original direction.

---

## VIII. VICTORY

Victory is the condition that most exposes him, because the defenses relax.

Immediately post-win — a contract completed, a duel resolved, a student finally landing the shot — his face shows nothing for approximately two seconds. The second-and-a-half mark is the giveaway: a single short exhale through the nose, the closest he comes to a laugh. The eyes brighten without the mouth moving. People who have only ever seen the cold face often miss it; people who have seen it twice never miss it again.

He drinks after a win. One drink, neat, slow. Two if the win was hard. He does not toast. If toasted he raises the glass perhaps an inch and lowers it without drinking on the cue, then drinks on his own count.

In victory over the protégé specifically — the rare contests Clint loses — Buck's behavior is *quietly cruel in narration*. He recounts the win, in plain language, to the protégé, in the second person, in detail, the next time they meet. The recounting is the trophy. He keeps no other.

Victory in the abstract — recognition, reputation, a name spoken with fear — he claims to disdain and demonstrably tracks. He knows his standing in the carnival circuit, in the mercenary economy, in the small fraternity of named marksmen, to a granularity that betrays daily monitoring. Anyone who places above him on any informal ranking becomes, within months, either a contract or a corpse, framed always as opportunity rather than vendetta.

---

## IX. DEFEAT

Defeat is the condition that most disorganizes him, and it has three distinct presentations depending on by whom.

**Defeat by an unknown.** Rare. Produces immediate, cold, technical reassessment. He will replay the encounter aloud to himself, often while cleaning the bow, narrating the geometry. The reassessment results in *practice* — sometimes weeks of it. No emotional residue is visible. This is his healthiest mode.

**Defeat by a known peer (the Swordsman in their carnival contests, certain named marksmen later).** Produces a brittle good-sportsmanship — a curt nod, a *Your shot*, a refusal to extend the contest. He will then avoid the peer's company for a calibrated period (days to months) and return as if nothing had happened. The peer is never re-challenged in front of an audience. Private rematches, never witnessed, are arranged.

**Defeat by the protégé.** This is the condition that breaks him, and it is the condition the canon returns to most often, because it is the one that generates the recurrence. The presentation is sequential and reliable across encounters: (1) a beat of stillness in which the face flattens entirely; (2) a slow exhale through the nose, not the soft post-victory one but a long emptying; (3) a verbal reframe — *Lucky*, *That wasn't the shot*, *You're still drawing wrong* — delivered with the affect of bored correction; (4) the turn away, weight shifted onto the back foot, the bow lowered but not put down; (5) a parting line that recasts the encounter as a lesson he chose to give. He will not concede. He has never, on any page, said the word *yes* in response to a protégé's challenge result. The closest he has come is a silence.

After protégé-defeat he escalates. Always. The next encounter will be harder, dirtier, less rule-bound, and will involve a third party — a hostage, a setup, a contracted ambush — designed to deny the protégé the clean repeat. He cannot tolerate a clean repeat.

---

## X. DECISION HABITS

How he chooses, micro to macro:

**Tactical decisions** are made in under a second and are almost always correct. The grooved competence is real. He does not deliberate over shots, routes, or weapon selection. The body has decided before the mind has framed the question.

**Operational decisions** (take a contract, accept a partner, train a student) are made over hours to days and are made *alone*. He does not consult. He will listen to a pitch, say *I'll think on it*, and not be reachable for the duration. When he returns, the decision is total and not subject to renegotiation. He has never been recorded to reverse a stated operational decision.

**Strategic / life decisions** (leaving the carnival, going freelance, the late-life summons) are made under the pressure of a felt humiliation and presented as cold calculation. Every major pivot in his life can be traced to a discrete narcissistic injury approximately three to six months prior. The lag is consistent. The reframing is total.

**Spending decisions** skew miser. He keeps cash, distrusts banks moderately, distrusts credit absolutely. He pays for equipment without negotiation (the bow is sacred; haggling over it would degrade it) and negotiates everything else to the cent.

**Trust decisions** are made through a single screen: *will this person, under pressure, expose me?* If the answer assessed is no, he is a stable and reliable operator. If the answer is yes, the person is filed for eventual neutralization, irrespective of present utility. Clint failed this screen at age fourteen and has not been removed from the file since.

---

## XI. ROUTES, RITUALS, AND TIMINGS

He rises before light — observed consistently across eras. The first action of the day is a forty-minute dry-draw routine: no arrows, no target, just the bow and the body, rehearsing the motion until the shoulder finds the groove. The routine is performed in silence and is not interrupted for any reason short of fire.

He shoots a minimum of one hundred arrows a day when conditions allow, and admits to feeling *wrong* on days he does not. The number is not a goal; it is a floor. He stops counting at one hundred and continues until the light fails or the body tires, whichever comes later.

He eats two meals a day, both modest, both at irregular times dictated by work. He does not eat in company by preference. When forced to dine socially, he sits at the corner of the table, eats half of what is served, and declines dessert with a small wave.

He sleeps in short blocks — four to five hours at the main pull, an hour or two later in the day if the schedule allows. He sleeps fully clothed when working, boots off, bow within arm's reach, on the side of the bed nearest the door. He does not snore. He wakes without alarms; ambient sound thresholds wake him at predictable decibel levels.

Travel: prefers ground to air, distrusts other people's vehicles. Drives himself in well-maintained, unremarkable trucks, always older models he understands mechanically. Sits in the driver's seat for an extra ten to fifteen seconds before exiting any vehicle, scanning. Backs into parking spaces by reflex. Carries his bow case in his off hand, leaving the strong hand free.

Lodging: cheap motels by preference, paid in cash, room on the ground floor, second from the end. Door checked twice on entry. Curtains drawn before lights on. The bow case is opened, inspected, and re-closed within five minutes of arrival — a re-grounding ritual.

---

## XII. SPEECH AND LANGUAGE

His vocabulary is regional and dated — carnival slang, mid-century rural Iowan grammar, a smattering of professional argot from the mercenary years. He says *boy* to any male under fifty, regardless of standing; he says *miss* to women he does not know and *ma'am* to women he wishes to dismiss with politeness. He does not use first names of intimates in conversation with them — Clint is *boy*, *kid*, or *Barton*; the Swordsman was *Duquesne* across the entire record.

He swears sparsely and with precision. The favored profanities are old, mild, and used as punctuation rather than emphasis — *hell*, *damn*, the occasional *son of a*. He does not use the modern range. Speech that does not match this register, in his presence, he marks the speaker down for.

He tells no jokes. He registers jokes with a closed-mouth nod, never a laugh. He does, very rarely, deliver a dry observation — a single sentence, deadpan — that carries the structure of humor without any of its warmth. People laugh. He does not.

He does not lie cleanly. His untruths are *omissions* and *reframes*, almost never fabrications. When he does construct a fabrication under direct pressure, the object-rotation habit (II) reverses direction — the only fully unconscious tell on file, and the basis of the single highest-confidence interrogation marker the file holds.

---

## XIII. TERMINAL-PERIOD DELTAS

In the final period (post-diagnosis), several baselines shift, and the shifts are themselves the most informative data the file contains.

The breath rate rises. The eight-to-twelve resting respiration creeps to fifteen and on bad days to twenty — the autonomic floor he trained for forty years is being eroded by the disease, and he cannot stop it. He knows this. He is observed, alone, attempting to slow it consciously, and failing. The failure enrages him.

The object-rotation accelerates. From three-to-four turns per minute to six or more, and continues during speech, where previously it had been a thinking-alone habit. The defenses are leaking.

He becomes, paradoxically, more *talkative* — not warmer, but more declarative, as if filing on the record. He issues pronouncements where previously he would have stayed silent. He repeats himself, which he has never done.

He summons. He has spent a lifetime making others come to him on his terms, and the summons of the protégé to his deathbed is the apotheosis of that habit, not its abandonment. The staging is meticulous: the room is chosen, the lighting set, the bow displayed, the line rehearsed. He is, at the end, doing the thing he has always done — performing mastery before an audience of one — but the performance is now of his own ending, which is the only remaining material.

He does not, in any recorded version of the final scene, ask for anything resembling forgiveness. He asks for the shot. The asking is, in his grammar, the closest he can come to *I loved you*, and the protégé, who has been listening for that sentence for forty years, hears it correctly and is destroyed by


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON (alias TRICK SHOT)
## Section: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

Classification: Behavioral-Pattern Reconstruction / Surveillance-Equivalent
Scope: Composite week, derived across documented eras (carnival period c.1960s; mercenary middle period c.1970s–80s; itinerant late period; terminal-illness coda)

---

### 1. The Governing Premise of His Days

What a week of surveillance on Bernard Barton would record, above all else, is **repetition without variation**. This is a subject organized around a single perceptual-motor task — placing an arrow at the intended point — and his days are constructed to subordinate every other function (sleep, food, sex, social contact, finance, hygiene) to the maintenance of that capability. He is not a man who shoots; he is a delivery mechanism for shots, around which the rest of life is a logistical envelope.

The discipline is religious in form without being religious in content. There is no deity, no doctrine, no remorse-and-grace cycle — only the count, the draw, the release, the recovery, and the recount. He is, in this sense, monastic. He is also, in this same sense, profoundly empty: a monastic discipline organized around no object larger than the self that performs it.

A week of him looks the same as the week before and the week after, with the variations being almost entirely a function of (a) employment status, (b) proximity to a target or protégé, and (c) the somatic decline of late life.

---

### 2. The Wake and the First Hour

He rises early — surveillance logs across periods would converge on **0430–0515** local, regardless of latitude, season, or whether he went to bed at 2200 or 0100. The wake is not by alarm. It is by internal clock, drilled in over decades on the carnival circuit where the first shooting tent had to be open by ten and the equipment had to be checked first.

He wakes without lingering. He does not roll over, does not check a clock for permission to stay down. The covers come off in one motion; feet to floor; sit on the edge of the bed for a count of perhaps fifteen seconds — eyes closed, hands flexing and extending in the lap, a thumb-and-forefinger pinch repeated four to six times on each hand. This is the **finger reawakening**, a tic so embedded he is unaware of it. It is the body checking that the instrument still works before the mind asks anything of it.

He stands. He goes to the bathroom or the equivalent (a trailer sink, a motel basin, in the late mercenary years a safehouse with the curtains drawn). He does not look at his face in the mirror beyond the seconds required for the function. He washes his hands first, then his face, then drinks two long swallows of water from the tap or a glass kept inverted on the counter overnight. The water-first habit is from the carnival, where coffee was after setup, never before.

The first hour, before any food, is **dry practice**. He keeps a bow strung or quickly stringable within five feet of where he sleeps — in the trailer, on a rack at the foot of the bunk; in motels, against the wall by the door, in a hard case opened the night before. He does not shoot in the first hour. He **draws**. Slow drawing to anchor, hold for a four-count, controlled release of the string back to brace — repeated in sets of twenty, three sets per hand-position (high anchor, cheek anchor, low instinctive anchor), then twenty more with eyes closed. The eyes-closed drawing is to keep the kinesthetic map honest when vision starts to lie, which he believes — correctly — it will, with age.

Surveillance would record the same posture every morning: feet shoulder-width and a half, weight slightly forward, head turned ninety degrees to an imagined target on the wall opposite the bed, the small involuntary exhale at full draw, the controlled letdown that makes no sound.
