A man of his profession, milieu, looks, and forty years of adult life did not live celibate; the absence of recorded partners reflects (a) his profound disinterest in establishing the kind of stable bond that would be visible to surveillance, and (b) the kind of partner-selection that does not produce paper trails.

**Reconstructed pattern.** Carnival-circuit transient liaisons, predominantly. Hotel-bar acquaintances on the contract-mercenary circuit later. The subject's intimacy strategy, as inferred from behavioral telemetry and from carnival-era anecdote, was selection of partners who were demonstrably his inferior in some legible dimension — younger, less educated, less skilled, or in a position of economic dependency on his presence (a barmaid in the town where the carnival was wintering, a cocktail waitress at a mercenary watering hole). Partners who could be impressed by the trick of the trick shot. Partners who would not last past the next town.

**Dynamics.** Compressed, performative, and asymmetric. The subject would arrive with the full force of his marquee charm — a charm that surveillance footage confirms he possessed in considerable measure; he could be funny, attentive, and bodily warm for the duration of a courtship measured in hours to days. The performance terminated immediately upon consummation. There is no recorded instance of the subject sustaining a romantic engagement past a single carnival stop or contract turnaround.

**Trust/safety.** Partners were physically safe with him — there is no record of intimate-partner violence directed at lovers (the violence pattern is reserved for protégés and for those who have exposed him; it does not generalize to romantic partners, who occupy a different psychic slot). They were emotionally unsafe in a more banal way: he would not remember their names by the next route stop, and he made no pretense otherwise after the first night.

**One probable longer-form attachment (inferred).** A carnival-era figure, almost certainly female, almost certainly a fellow performer or proprietress, with whom the subject sustained an on-again-off-again arrangement across multiple seasons. The inference is drawn from a single recurring photographic background figure across three seasons of Carson Carnival promotional materials and from a remark of Duquesne's, recorded secondhand, about "Buck's woman" in a tone that implied continuity. No name surfaces. The relationship, if it existed in the form indicated, would have ended at or near the embezzlement rupture; the subject's flight from the carnival was also a flight from her, and there is no record of her in his subsequent life. He did not return to look for her. The relationship is consistent with the subject's general pattern in that it was conducted entirely within the milieu of his mastery — she would have known him as Trick Shot, watched him perform, and provided audience-intimacy of the type the subject requires; outside the carnival frame she would have been incomprehensible to him and he to her.

**Failure mode (intimacy-general).** The subject cannot tolerate being known. The romantic relationship that would require disclosure — of history, fear, want — is the relationship he cannot enter. His liaisons terminate at exactly the point where the next conversation would have to contain something true. This is not strategy; it is incapacity. He has no apparatus for sustained intimate disclosure and never developed one.

**Children.** None on record. Pattern strongly argues against unrecorded paternity surviving to acknowledged relationship; if biological children exist, the subject does not know and has not sought to know. The successor "Trick Shot" of late-canon iterations is in some versions framed as a nephew or distant relation, which is the closest the subject came to acknowledging family of any kind, and which functions psychically as a substitute son rather than as recognition of actual kin.

**Leverage.** Negligible. The romantic axis cannot be used against the subject because there is no partner whose continued well-being he weights enough to be coerced by. The single probable longer-form attachment, if traceable, would be a witness of forensic interest but not a coercive lever — he has had forty years to not look for her, and the not-looking is settled.

---

## 7c.8 — SYNTHESIS: THE STRUCTURE OF ANTAGONISM

Across this catalogue, a single relational template recurs. The subject approaches every human being through an initial assessment of skill and utility; classifies them as instrument, confederate, rival, or furniture; conducts the relationship within the constraints of that classification; and, when the classification is challenged by the other party's autonomy, experiences the challenge as betrayal requiring punishment. Lovers escape this template only because they are never permitted to remain long enough to challenge it. Confederates escape it only when they confine themselves to non-overlapping skill domains and ask no personal questions. Protégés do not escape it at all.

The unifying feature of his enmities — Clinton above all, Duquesne in absentia, the carnival authority structure, every employer he ever despised — is that each was at some point in a position to *see* him. Being seen, for this subject, is the precipitating condition of hostility. The audience of strangers may watch the trick shot; the intimate witness may not see the man behind it.

Forty years of intermittent surveillance confirm: he has never permitted anyone to do so, and he is dying without having done so, and the deathbed scene with Clinton — should it occur as the subject is staging it — will be one last attempt to control the conditions under which he is finally, briefly, looked at.

— END SECTION 7c —


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON / TRICK SHOT

Classification: Baseline-human capability set, upper-extremity perceptual-motor specialization. No augmentation, no exotic biology, no mystical conditioning. What follows is therefore an analysis of a *trained organism*, not a powered one — which is to say, an analysis in which the line between "ability" and "symptom" is unusually thin, because every capacity he possesses was acquired by the same compulsive economy of self that produced his pathology. The skill *is* the disorder, articulated through tendons.

---

## 1. THE PRIMARY INSTRUMENT — ARCHERY

### 1.1 Mechanism

Trick Shot's marksmanship is conventional human archery executed at the asymptote of what conventional human archery can do. There is no documented departure from standard biomechanics: anchored draw, stable stance, controlled release. What separates him from a competent target archer is a cluster of measurable specializations that, on the file, must be enumerated rather than romanticized:

- **Static visual acuity** at or near 20/10 corrected, with preserved performance into late middle age — implying a subject who has protected his eyes obsessively across a carnival-circuit lifetime that ordinarily destroys them (sun, dust, smoke, head trauma).
- **Dynamic acuity and smooth-pursuit tracking** at the elite end — he hits moving targets, including targets crossing his field laterally, at ranges where the shot-leading geometry exceeds intuitive calculation. This is trained, not innate; it is the residue of tens of thousands of repetitions on carnival props (moving plates, swung pendulums, the assistant's apple).
- **Vestibulo-ocular stability** consistent with a man who can shoot from unstable platforms — wagons, horseback, the swaying high-wire of a circus rig. Carnival origin matters here: he was not trained on a still range.
- **Proprioceptive memory** of draw weight, anchor point, and release at a resolution that allows him to shoot accurately without conscious sighting — the so-called "instinctive" mode of trick archery, in which the bow becomes an extension of the gaze.
- **Forearm and rotator-cuff conditioning** sufficient to sustain heavy poundage for long sessions without tremor. The cost of this is visible in late-period appearances: the shoulders are wrecked; he carries himself with the slight forward roll of a man whose deltoids have eaten his posture.

### 1.2 Range

- **Effective lethal range, traditional recurve / longbow**: roughly 80–100 meters for a head or center-mass shot under field conditions, extending to 150+ meters for area-of-body strikes in still air. He prefers the closer band — 30 to 60 meters — because that is where the trick-shot artistry pays. He is a man who would rather make a hard shot look impossible than make an impossible shot look easy.
- **Indoor / confined**: at carnival and arena distances (5–25 meters) he is functionally infallible against non-evasive targets. Against evasive targets he degrades — but slowly, and predictably, and never to ordinariness.
- **Compound or modern bow**: when he has used them, his groupings tighten and his range extends, but he is observably less *pleased* with the result. The instrument matters to him; the spectacle is in the difficulty.

### 1.3 The Trick-Shot Repertoire

This is the inventory a surveillance file would actually compile, because each item is a signature he repeats and therefore a tell:

- **The split-arrow** — arrow cleaving an already-embedded arrow. Performed at carnival, performed at Clint as instruction, performed in combat as humiliation rather than necessity.
- **The blind shot** — back-turned, mirror-sighted, or via reflective surface. Frequent in the carnival act; surfaces in combat when he wants to demean an opponent by not looking at them.
- **The ricochet** — bouncing a blunt-tip or barbed shaft off a hard surface to take a target around cover. He calculates these by eye, in real time; the geometry is not memorized, it is *seen*.
- **The multi-arrow draw** — two, three, occasionally four shafts nocked and released in a single fluid motion, fanning into a horizontal pattern. Lower accuracy per shaft, higher area coverage; he uses it almost exclusively against multiple opponents or as a closing flourish.
- **The disarm shot** — pinning a hand, a sleeve, a weapon-grip; theatrical, low-lethality, asserts dominance. He prefers this to a kill when an audience is present.
- **The candle / wick / flame shot** — extinguishing or igniting a small flame at distance. Pure carnival; he still does it, decades later, because it gets the gasp.
- **The apple shot** (and its variants — coin, cigarette, playing card). Performed on assistants in the carnival years. Performed on Clint as part of training. The diagnostic here is not the skill but the willingness; he is a man who put live arrows past a child's face as pedagogy.
- **The trick draw / quick draw** — bow strung and loosed in under two seconds from the slung position. His response time from holster-equivalent to first arrow on target is the part of his game that has degraded most visibly with age, and the part he most aggressively conceals.

### 1.4 Specialty Munitions

Buck's preferred arsenal is austere by the standards of the protégé he produced. Clint's gimmick-tip culture — the cable, the suction, the boomerang, the EMP — is an *elaboration* on the master's tradition, and one Buck is documented as faintly disdainful of. The master's own kit:

- Standard broadhead and field-point shafts in cedar or aluminum, fletched conservatively.
- Barbed shafts for shots intended to hold flesh or fabric.
- Blunt-tip "stunner" heads for ricochet work and non-lethal disarms.
- Incendiary or flare-tipped shafts for theatrical or signaling use — used sparingly.
- Occasional explosive-tip in mercenary contracts, but he resents the dependence; an explosive arrow is a confession that the marksman is not enough.

The reading: Buck's quiver is a moralized object. Each specialty tip is a small admission of insufficient skill, and he has clearly negotiated with himself, shaft by shaft, which admissions are tolerable.

### 1.5 Growth Curve Across Time

- **Carnival prime (estimate: mid-twenties through early forties).** Peak coordination, peak nerve, peak audience. This is the era of the act with Duquesne, the era of the trained Barton boys, the era in which the technique was actually advancing. Documented in flashback as a man who could place arrows by feel and by joke.
- **Mercenary middle period (forties through fifties).** Skill plateaus; theatricality is monetized; tactical sophistication grows because contracts demand it. He learns to shoot people, not bottles. Reaction time and acuity still in elite band.
- **Late period (sixties, with terminal illness).** Measurable decline: draw weight reduced, recovery between shots lengthened, occasional tremor at full draw, mild presbyopia he refuses to correct visibly. He compensates with positioning, patience, and an increased willingness to take the dirty shot — from cover, from ambush, with a brace. The artistry contracts; the lethality is preserved. He hates this and it is legible in him.
- **The deathbed period.** He can still, on demand, place an arrow with surgical precision; he cannot string and draw at the rate he once did. His final demonstrations are curated for difficulty rather than rate of fire. The decline is hidden under the choreography.

---

## 2. SECONDARY COMBAT SKILLS

He is not a knife fighter or a brawler of distinction, and the file should resist the temptation to inflate him. What he carries beyond the bow:

- **Working hand-to-hand competence** sufficient to beat a teenage Clint Barton bloody — which is a low bar he meets without difficulty, and a higher bar (a trained adversary) he meets only with the bow already out of reach and his own life on the line. Style is dirty boxing with carnival add-ons: elbows, low kicks, headbutts, the use of environmental objects.
- **Throwing weapons** — knives, weighted darts, the carnival ringer's whole vocabulary — at solid journeyman level. The hand that draws the bow throws a knife well; the same proprioception serves.
- **Riding, climbing, balance** — circus-rigging skills retained for life. He can shoot from a galloping horse, from a rope, from a roof edge; he is comfortable at heights and on unstable footing in a way that an opponent expecting a static archer will misjudge.
- **Firearms** — competent but unenthused. He can use a pistol or a rifle; he treats them as tools for situations in which he has been forced out of his actual profession. A surveillance file would note that his rifle work, when documented, is exceptional in pure marksmanship and mediocre in tactical handling — he shoots a rifle like a bow, which is to say beautifully and slightly wrong.

---

## 3. PEDAGOGICAL CAPACITY — THE TRANSMISSIBLE SKILL

This is the ability the file must take most seriously, because it is the one that has done the most damage in the world.

Buck Barton can *make* an archer. Clinton Barton, who is on the published record as the most accurate marksman on the planet, is the product of this man's instruction. So, in later canon, is the successor figure to whom Buck attempts to pass the alias. The pedagogy is documented across flashback sequences and reads as follows:

- **Drill volume**: thousands of repetitions per session; the student shoots until the fingers bleed and then shoots more. The bleeding is regarded as data, not as injury.
- **Praise economy**: zero baseline. A grunt or a silence is acceptance; a correction is punishment; a beating is a teaching moment. Praise is so rare that when it occurs it imprints, and the student will spend the rest of his life chasing the next occurrence. This is not an accident of teaching style; it is the mechanism by which loyalty is manufactured.
- **Technique transmission**: genuinely first-class. The form he teaches is biomechanically sound, the drills he assigns are well-designed, the progression is intelligent. He is not a charlatan teacher; he is an excellent one whose pedagogical method is psychological capture.
- **The trick repertoire as curriculum**: he teaches the impossible shots early, because the impossible shot done in front of him is the unit of bonding. The student learns that astonishment is the price of being seen.

The diagnostic reading: Buck's pedagogy is itself a power. He converts orphan children into precision instruments and converts those instruments' eventual achievements into evidence of his own significance. The mechanism by which he made Clint is the mechanism by which he later haunts him.

---

## 4. PERCEPTUAL & COGNITIVE SPECIALIZATIONS

The carnival sharpshooter as a category is a sensory phenotype, and Buck exhibits the full set:

- **Target fixation and selective attention** — the ability to lock onto one element in a chaotic field (the moving plate amid the crowd, the throat amid the brawl) and dim everything else. Useful in combat, catastrophic in interpersonal life; he attends to the next shot with the same focal narrowing he attends to a person.
- **Calibration sense** — wind, range, drop, drift. He estimates these by eye and corrects intuitively. The math is real but is offloaded entirely to trained pattern recognition.
- **Time-compression under arousal** — the documented phenomenon in elite shooters in which subjective time slows during the shot. Buck has it. It contributes to his composure under fire and to his ego — a man who lives, repeatedly, in the slowed second before release develops a particular relationship to other people, who appear to him as slightly speeded-up.
- **Pattern recognition is domain-locked.** Perceptual-motor: elite. Interpersonal: absent. He cannot read a room; he can read a wind. This is consistent across every documented encounter and is, again, the symptom-as-signature: the perceptual apparatus that makes him lethal is the same apparatus whose narrowness makes him cruel.

---

## 5. LIMITS — WHAT HE CANNOT DO

A surveillance file is most useful in its negatives.

- **He cannot operate without the bow as identity.** Strip him of it and he is a competent middle-aged brawler with a chip on the shoulder; he loses two-thirds of his threat profile and most of his composure.
- **He cannot operate without an audience.** Genuine solitude — no witness, no protégé, no contracted observer — degrades his performance. He has been documented as less precise in pure ambush than in announced confrontation, because the announcement is the point.
- **He cannot sustain extended high-volume engagements.** The shoulders fail; the eye fatigues; the older he gets, the shorter the window in which he is at peak. A trained adversary who survives the first ninety seconds against him is fighting a different and lesser man at the second minute.
- **He cannot adapt to genuinely novel weapon systems.** Drones, ranged sensors, networked targeting — he ignores them, dismisses them, and is exposed by them. The carnival worldview does not extend to the contemporary battlefield.
- **He cannot tolerate being outshot.** This is a tactical, not merely a psychological, limit. In every documented engagement in which an opponent has demonstrably exceeded him at the bow, his subsequent decision-making degrades — he picks the spiteful shot over the winning one. The exploitable seam.
- **He cannot operate at true distance against a hardened opponent.** Without a scoped rifle, beyond 100 meters the geometry favors the runner. He knows this and works to close.
- **He cannot read a child.** Documented. The signal of Clint's distress, of Barney's resentment, of the audience's discomfort with the apple-shot — none of these register. The sensorium that sees the wind does not see the boy.
- **He cannot reconcile.** Listed here under "abilities" because its absence is structural: there is no internal procedure by which Buck Barton apologizes, repairs, or resumes. Offered the opportunity, he does not refuse; he does not parse the opportunity as an opportunity at all.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS — THE TELLS

For operational purposes — for the analyst trying to confirm a Buck Barton contract from incident scene alone — the following signatures recur with a frequency that approaches certainty:

- **The humiliation shot before the kill shot.** A first arrow that disarms, pins, or marks; a second that ends it. He is congenitally incapable of the clean single-shot kill when he believes he is being watched, including by the victim.
- **The signed grouping.** Two or three arrows in a tight pattern at a non-vital location — sleeve, lapel, hatband — left as a card. The carnival man's tag.
- **The split-arrow tableau.** If a previous archer (especially Clint) has placed a shaft, Buck will, given the opportunity, split it. This is so reliable it can be used as bait.
- **The choice of recurve over compound** in any contract that allows the freedom. The traditional bow is the brand.
- **Egress through the rigging.** When the environment offers height — catwalks, rooftops, scaffolds, anything that recalls the tent's interior architecture — he will retreat upward rather than outward. The body remembers the big top.
- **The retained quiver.** Even in flight, even bleeding, he does not abandon shafts. A scene with the body and no quiver is not his; a quiver recovered and inventoried is the closest thing to a fingerprint he leaves.

---

## 7. THE SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE READING

Every capacity catalogued above is the deposit of the same psychological economy. The visual acuity is the residue of forty years of attending only to the next shot. The pedagogical genius is the operationalization of a man for whom relationship is only intelligible as instruction. The trick repertoire is the externalized form of a self that exists only when watched performing the impossible. The refusal of gimmick-tip arrows is the moralism of a narcissist who needs the achievement uncontaminated. The shoulders, eaten by draw weight, are the somatic record of a regulation strategy — *do not feel; act with precision* — pursued past the body's tolerance. The decline he cannot bear is the decline of the only instrument by which he has ever permitted himself to be real.

Bernard Barton's power set, properly read, is the legible biography of his disorder. He is not a man with a skill; he is a skill that grew a man around itself, badly, and the badness of the fit is what the surveillance file is for. The bow does not extend him. It is the part of him that survived the foreclosure of everything else.

— END SECTION —


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT — BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON / "TRICK SHOT"

*Cross-filed: weapons-discipline assessment; itinerant-criminal infrastructure; mentor-as-method.*

---

## 1. Decision-Making Architecture

Subject's decisional process is best modeled as a **two-layer system** with almost no traffic between the layers. The upper layer is tactical and astonishingly fast — the perceptual-motor calculus of a man who has put somewhere north of a quarter-million arrows downrange across his working life. The lower layer is strategic-interpersonal and is, by contrast, slow, brittle, and ideologically captive to the narcissistic frame documented in §3-4 of the parent workup. The two layers do not correct one another. He will execute a tactically immaculate engagement in service of a strategically self-defeating goal (e.g., contracting against the protégé whose continued existence is, in fact, the only thing keeping his identity coherent) and feel no friction between the two facts.

**Loop characteristics.** Observe-orient-decide-act is compressed to near-reflex in the firing window — sub-second from sighting to release on familiar geometry, with the orient phase functionally pre-loaded by environmental scan on entry. Outside the firing window, the loop expands and corrupts: the orient stage is contaminated by status-arithmetic (who is watching, who must be shown, who must be put back in his place), and the decide stage is biased by a standing answer (the answer is almost always *more contempt, more control, more demonstration*).

**Risk posture.** Calibrated, not reckless. He does not enter a room he has not mapped, does not take a shot whose retreat he has not pre-walked, does not contract against a target whose habits he has not studied. The carnival origin shows: a sharpshooter who works in front of a crowd learns early that one miss in public is worse than ten misses in private, and the lesson generalizes. What looks like swagger is in fact heavily pre-staged. The risks he *does* take are almost exclusively in the interpersonal column — provocations, deathbed summons, contemptuous monologues — where his judgment is poor and he overrates his read of the other party.

**Time horizon.** Short on operations (hours-to-days planning windows), pathologically long on grudges (decades). Operational and grudge-clocks run on different escapements and he switches between them without noticing the gear change.

---

## 2. Methods & Signature Tradecraft

### 2.1 The Bow as Primary Instrument

He shoots a recurve, not a compound, in the foundational appearances — a deliberate refusal of mechanical advantage that is half craftsman's pride and half identity statement. (The bow that does the work for you is a bow for lesser men.) Later appearances will see him use compound and crossbow as the work requires, but the recurve is the *signature* weapon — the one he draws when he wants to be recognized, the one he teaches with, the one he intends to die holding.

Draw weight settled in the high-50s to mid-60s of pounds — heavy enough for terminal performance against unarmored targets at carnival-act distances, light enough for the cold-shot precision and high shot-count tolerance his work requires. He shoots with **three fingers under** in the trick repertoire and **Mediterranean** for distance — the switch is itself a tell that an attentive observer can read to predict the kind of shot coming.

**Arrow inventory** is austere and personally maintained. He fletches his own. Shafts are uniform — he is contemptuous of trick-arrows in the Clint Barton style (putty-tip, bola, acid-head, etc.) and considers them a confession of inadequate marksmanship; the instrument is supposed to be the man, not the projectile. The exception, in late mercenary work, is a small inventory of armor-piercing and incendiary heads kept in a separate quiver and used without ceremony. He treats them the way a chef treats a microwave: necessary on certain jobs, never to be discussed.

### 2.2 The Trick Repertoire (and its Operational Use)

The carnival act — splitting an arrow already in the target, blind shots off mirrors, multiple-target sequences, ricochet shots, the candle-flame extinguish, the held-card split — is not retired when he goes mercenary. It is **repurposed as intimidation tradecraft**. He will, on a contract, place a first arrow somewhere it ought to be impossible to have placed (through a closed window, off a wall onto a target behind a barrier, into the wood of a chair an inch from a head) and *then* open negotiations. The shot is the calling card; the message is *I could already have killed you, and now we will discuss terms on my arithmetic.* This is also why he prefers contracts that allow approach time over true sniper work — the demonstration matters to him more than the kill, and he will sacrifice operational efficiency to preserve the demonstration.

### 2.3 Engagement Pattern

A typical Barton engagement, reconstructed from confrontations on record:

1. **Pre-walk.** Hours-to-days before, on foot, the engagement ground is surveyed for sightlines, anchor points (he likes to shoot from a braced position whenever the geometry permits — a doorframe, a beam, a rail; he is not a kneeling-or-prone shooter by preference), lighting at the projected time of contact, ambient noise, and crowd density. Cover and concealment are catalogued separately; he is religious about the distinction.
2. **Insert.** Quietly, in working clothes — not theatrical. The costume comes out at contact, not before. He has been described in carnival-era and mercenary-era both as someone who moves through a venue "like staff" — drawing no eye until he chooses to.
3. **Pre-shot demonstration.** The signature opener: an impossible placement of a non-lethal arrow as authorship of the room. Sometimes accompanied by a verbal cue — a flat, almost laconic line that announces him by craft rather than by name.
4. **Verbal control phase.** He will talk. This is partly tradecraft (he is reading the target's panic-response, gauging whether the contract pays better with compliance or with completion) and partly compulsion — he needs the audience moment, the brief theatre, before the kill.
5. **Execution or extraction.** Single shot on hard targets where feasible. He is offended by overkill; multiple arrows in a body read to him as poor work.
6. **Egress.** Walked, not run, on the same pre-walked route. He is famously hard to chase in part because he refuses to look like a man being chased.

### 2.4 Hand-to-Hand and Sidearm Work

Competent but disliked. He carries a knife — a short fixed-blade, carried inverted on the weak side under the jacket — and will use it without theatrics if a target closes the distance. Sidearms he tolerates and shoots accurately, but he considers firearms an admission that the geometry of the room beat him and he resents the admission. In hand-to-hand he is an aging brawler with carnival-roustabout fundamentals: low stance, heavy hands, willingness to use environmental objects, no formal art. He will absolutely strike a smaller or younger opponent first and without warning if status is in play.

### 2.5 Teaching as Operational Method

This is the part of his tradecraft most often missed. **He uses pedagogy as a control vector**, not only as a vocation. The carnival recruitment of the Barton boys was, in retrospect, a recruitment posture he has run more than once: identify a hungry juvenile (or, late in life, a hungry adult heir), offer the one thing they cannot get elsewhere (true skill transmission), and ratchet emotional debt across years of training until the protégé is structurally unable to refuse him a request. The late-era "second Trick Shot" appearances are this method running again, now compressed by terminal diagnosis. Treat his teaching as a long-cycle operation in its own right.

---

## 3. Resources & Finances

Subject is, and has always been, **cash-economy**. Carnival receipts in the early period, mercenary pay-on-completion in the later. He does not bank meaningfully; what currency he holds is split across small stashes — a footlocker in whatever the current trailer is, an envelope taped behind a frame in whatever rented room, a small denomination of negotiable goods (a roll of pre-1965 silver coin appears in two separate appearances, treated as both ballast and emergency liquidity).

**Income streams, cataloged:**
- Carnival contract and a cut of the gate from his act (early; primary).
- Embezzled receipts from the same carnival (early; the precipitating fraud).
- Mercenary contracts, usually mid-tier — high enough to pay well, low enough not to attract Tier-1 attention. Brokered through criminal intermediaries (Crossfire-adjacent in the documented arc) rather than self-marketed; he disdains the self-promotion the upper mercenary tier requires.
- Instruction fees, irregular — he has taken paying students, both before and after the Clint episode, but is a poor businessman about it and the income is sporadic.
- Late-period: liquidation of equipment and a small amount of accumulated cash, repurposed to stage the deathbed transfer.

**Expenditure profile** is austere to the point of monasticism in everything except equipment. He spends on bow tackle, shafts, fletching materials, blades, and travel. He does not spend on lodging beyond functional, does not spend on women (no documented sustained romantic relationships — the affective bandwidth is not there), drinks rail liquor not top-shelf, drives whatever runs. The austerity is not principled; it is the negative space left by a personality with no consumption interests beyond craft.

**Infrastructure** is itinerant by design. The trailer-and-circuit life of the carnival years becomes a motel-and-rental-car life in the mercenary period; the topology is identical — temporary nodes, no fixed address, mail handled through general delivery or through a small number of trusted intermediaries (carnival-era contacts, mostly aging by the late appearances). He has at any given time a **cache discipline**: at least two equipment caches in geographically separated cities, each containing a backup recurve, a bundle of shafts, a small cash float, and a change of clothing. He rotates these on a roughly seasonal basis. Compromise of one is treated as a discipline failure and the location is burned permanently.

**Documentation.** Multiple sets of working identification, none of them elaborate — he is not a Carmichael-grade forger's client. The IDs are sufficient for motel registration and ground transport and would not survive a real query. He compensates by avoiding circumstances that produce queries.

**Network.** Small, aging, and structurally carnival. Former Carson personnel scattered across the country function as his eyes and ears, his couriers, and occasionally his fences. The Swordsman is the only documented professional peer-relationship and that one is poisoned by the original embezzlement. He has no apparent ties to the larger costumed-criminal mutual-aid ecosystem (no Bar With No Name regular status, no Stilt-Man-funeral attendance on record) — by temperament he holds himself above it.

---

## 4. Patterns of Action

**Geographic.** Heaviest density of recorded activity in the American Midwest and Mid-Atlantic — the corridors the Carson Carnival historically worked. He returns to these geographies under stress. The mercenary contracts that take him elsewhere (New York, the West Coast during the WCA-era engagements) are exceptions undertaken for pay or for access to Clint, and he is observably less comfortable operating outside familiar topography.

**Temporal.** Prefers **dusk and pre-dawn** for contact work — light he learned to shoot in, light a carnival sharpshooter is calibrated for. Avoids full midday (sun-angle problems with the recurve sighting habits of his generation) and avoids deep night absent prepared illumination (he is a marksman, not a thermal-optic operator, and he knows it).

**Tempo.** Slow setup, fast execution, slow egress, then **prolonged dormancy**. Between recorded incidents he disappears for months at a time. The dormancy is not planning; it is closer to the quiet of an aging cat. He surfaces when a contract requires it, when his status is threatened, or when the standing grudge against Clint cycles back to the top of the queue.

**Triggers for activity.**
- Money below operational floor (rare; his floor is low).
- A target who can be framed as having dishonored skill or hierarchy (frequent rationalization).
- Any news — direct or indirect — of Clint Barton's standing, success, or new mentor-attachment. The latter is the most reliable trigger on record; he is functionally a sensor wired to the protégé's salience in the wider world.
- Somatic decline milestones (a missed shot in practice, a tremor, the cancer diagnosis). Each produces a step-change escalation.

**Anti-surveillance posture.** Pre-internet in formation and largely pre-internet in practice. He does not carry phones for long; he checks general-delivery mail under one of three working names; he changes vehicles by trade-in, not by theft (theft creates a record that competence does not require). He is sensitive to being watched in the physical sense — the carnival eye for the crowd transposes directly to the operational eye for a tail — and will abort and reset rather than engage if he suspects coverage. He is *insensitive* to digital surveillance; a modern apparatus would catch him on financial-pattern analysis, motel-registry correlation, and the simple fact that a man who fletches his own arrows buys distinctive consumables from a small number of suppliers.

---

## 5. Signature Operational Tells

The file would be incomplete without the granular tells — the things a watcher would learn to flag.

- **The pre-shot exhale.** Audible at close quarters. A long, controlled nasal exhalation that ends at the release. Decades of breath-discipline; he cannot suppress it without degrading the shot.
- **The two-finger glove check.** Before any draw of consequence he runs the thumb of the bow hand across the index and middle fingers of the draw hand — a tactile reassurance of his shooting tab. He does this even when not wearing the tab. Pure ritual; absolutely consistent.
- **The placed first arrow.** As discussed in §2.2. The opener that is never the kill. A first arrow somewhere unnecessary is, on his jobs, a signature line.
- **The verbal cadence.** Flat, dry, slightly didactic — he talks to adults the way he talked to the boys at the carnival, which is to say *down*. Sentences are short and end on the operative noun. He uses craft vocabulary precisely (cant, anchor, paradox, archer's paradox, spine, grain) and is mildly contemptuous when an interlocutor cannot follow.
- **The refusal to run.** He will walk away from a scene at a pace that telegraphs ownership of the ground. A man fleeing one of his scenes is not him.
- **The audience check.** Eyes flick to any third party present — not a threat-assessment flick but a confirmation flick. Witnesses register as resource. In a room with no witnesses he is paradoxically less dangerous and more uncertain, as if the engagement lacks meaning without observation.
- **The blame phrase.** Across decades and writers, the same rhetorical move recurs: he assigns the precipitating fault to the other party in a single declarative sentence, usually early in the verbal-control phase. *You made me. You brought this. You did this when you.* The grammar of the projection is so consistent it functions as biometric.
- **The grip on the bow at rest.** He holds it loose in the bow hand even when not drawing, fingers relaxed, the bow almost dangling. A tense bow hand is an amateur's bow hand. Watch the bow hand to read the state.
- **Refusal of compound geometry in self-image.** Will use a compound for a job and discard it after; will never be photographed with one, will never teach with one. The recurve in hand is the man on display.
- **The student-glance.** When Clint or any former or prospective protégé is in the room, his eyes return to them at a measurable cadence — not affection, not even hostility per se, but the involuntary salience of the object that organizes his whole psychology. This is the single most reliable tell that a given target is currently the protégé-object: count the glances per minute.

---

## 6. Net Operational Assessment

A medium-threat operator with high-threat localized capability: inside fifty meters with a clear sightline and a recurve in his hand, he is in the top fraction of a percent of human marksmen and should be treated accordingly. Outside that envelope his threat decays steeply, and his strategic judgment decays faster. He is **defeatable by audience denial, by skill-out-performance in the perceptual-motor channel, and by patience** — he will, given time and dormancy, self-route back into a fixable confrontation rather than vanish. He is **not defeatable by appeal**; every documented attempt has produced escalation. Handlers and operators encountering the subject are advised to engage on the terrain of craft (where he can be beaten and where the beating disorganizes him) and to refuse the terrain of relationship (where he cannot lose, because he has long since redefined losing as the other party's moral failure).

The file should be kept open. While the late-era cancer arc has been used in canon to write toward closure, the structural fact remains that this is a subject whose narrative function is *return*. Assume he is not done until the body is confirmed and the bow accounted for.

— END SECTION —


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON / TRICK SHOT

*Section 5 of the UATU dossier. Cross-reference Sections 3 (Psychological) and 4 (Psychiatric); this section translates the diagnostic substrate into the explicit and implicit doctrine by which the subject actually navigates the world. What follows is reconstructed from forty years of observed behavior, recorded utterance, and the structural consistency of his choices across writers, eras, and contexts. Where the subject would deny a proposition, the denial itself has been weighed as evidence.*

---

## 1. FIRST PRINCIPLES — THE METAPHYSICS BEHIND THE BOW

### 1.1 The world is a range, and everything in it is a target.

The single deepest commitment in Bernard Barton's cosmology is the reduction of all situations to the geometry of the shot. Distance, wind, angle of obstruction, the moving body of the quarry, the steadiness of one's own hand — this is the lattice through which he perceives every encounter. Rooms are read for sightlines before they are read for people. Conversations are read for the moment the other party gives him an opening. He does not metaphorize this; it is the substrate of his perception, not its decoration. A man who has drawn a bow ten thousand mornings before breakfast does not switch the apparatus off when he sets the weapon down.

The corollary is a flattening of moral terrain into ballistic terrain. Right and wrong are not categories he denies; they are categories he does not natively perceive. What he perceives is *clean shot / blocked shot, in-range / out-of-range, my line / not my line*. The ethical universe is, to him, a fog around the real, scored coordinates of the world.

### 1.2 The world is a hierarchy of competence, and competence is the only legitimate currency.

Beneath the targeting overlay sits a second principle: the population of the world sorts into those who can do the impossible thing and those who cannot, and only the former are real. The latter are scenery — the carnival crowd, the marks, the rubes, the employers who pay, the lawmen who do not understand what they are looking at. They are necessary (someone must watch; someone must pay) and they are despised (they cannot do what he does). This contempt is not performed; it is foundational. He does not have to summon it. It is the resting tone of his attention.

Among the competent there is further sorting. The merely skilled are colleagues. The exceptionally skilled are rivals. The skilled-and-loyal are extensions of self. The skilled-and-disloyal are the only category that produces the white-hot, decades-durable rage; one cannot be betrayed by a rube, only by a peer who refused his place in the hierarchy.

### 1.3 Skill is identity; identity is performance; performance requires witness.

He does not believe, in any operative sense, that he exists when no one is watching. He would deny this if asked. His behavior contradicts the denial. Solitary practice he tolerates as preparation *for* being seen; pure solitude with no audience and no future audience produces in him the irritable restlessness that other men feel in solitary confinement. The alias is the proof: *Trick Shot* is a barker's word, the word painted on the side of a tent. He chose the name a master craftsman would refuse. He chose the spectacle frame because the spectacle frame is where he is real.

This generates a paradoxical operational rule that runs beneath everything: **never take a shot no one will know you took.** He has broken this rule — he is a working assassin in the later record — but always grudgingly, and the silent kills appear in canon to leave him sourer than the witnessed ones. When he can stage a kill, he stages it. When he must merely complete it, he completes it the way a starving man eats food he doesn't like.

### 1.4 Time runs one way, and the past is sovereign.

He does not believe in revision. The historical record — *who shot what, who was there, who saw, who flinched* — is the only durable property in the universe. This is why the betrayal by Clint Barton cannot age out: the past is not a thing one moves past, it is the ledger by which the present is judged. To reconcile would be to rewrite the ledger, and the ledger is more real to him than the boy. Forgiveness is, in his code, a category error — a request to falsify the record.

---

## 2. CONFLICT — WHAT HE BELIEVES IT IS FOR

### 2.1 Conflict is the natural and sufficient form of contact.

He does not regard conflict as a breakdown of normal relations. He regards it as the form relations take when they become serious. Casual exchange is filler; conflict is the moment the masks come off and the actual ranking is established. He is therefore not avoidant of confrontation, not addicted to it either — he treats it as the medium in which truth is discovered, the way another man treats conversation.

### 2.2 The purpose of conflict is to establish or correct position, not to destroy.

This is a critical distinction missed by adversaries who code him as a killer. He kills, but killing is not the goal of fighting; *positioning* is. He wants the other man to know, in the last instant or in the surrender, where he stands relative to Buck Barton. A dead opponent who never registered the lesson is a wasted opponent. This is why his confrontations with Clint repeatedly fail to end Clint — at the moments of maximum lethal opportunity, he chooses gestures of domination over completion. He would rather his protégé live, defeated and instructed, than die without absorbing the instruction.

The exception: when his own position is at terminal risk (skill exposed as inferior, fraud exposed publicly, body exposed as failing) he will attempt to kill, because at that point only erasure of the witness preserves the ledger.

### 2.3 The first move in a conflict is the framing of who started it.

Doctrinally, before any physical engagement, he establishes — to himself, to bystanders, to the opponent — that the other party initiated. He believes this with the full conviction of a man whose defensive structure depends on it. The framing is not strategic deception; it is the precondition for his own execution of the engagement. He cannot fight clean while believing he is the aggressor. He therefore cannot believe it. This is operationally exploitable: deny him the framing and he wobbles.

### 2.4 Pain is a tool; humiliation is a weapon; mercy is a confession.

His preferred terminal gesture in a won conflict is a marked humiliation — disarming with theatrical ease, sparing the life in a way that makes the sparing more degrading than killing would be, leaving a sign. He believes mercy granted is the giver's signature on the loser, a permanent annotation. He does not believe in mercy as compassion; he believes in it as territorial marking.

He does not respect mercy granted *to* him. He reads it as the granter's foolishness — they had the shot and gave it away, which makes them weak, which obligates him to nothing.

### 2.5 The fair fight is a category for fools.

He believes — and would say plainly — that the concept of a fair contest belongs to the carnival, to the rubes, to the rules announced for the show. In actual conflict, advantage is to be sought, taken, and concealed. The wind, the sun, the position, the surprise of the second arrow before the first lands — these are not cheating. They are what the work is. He has contempt for opponents who fight as if the contest were a sport. He believes those opponents are revealing that they have never had to actually win.

---

## 3. CONTROL — HOW HE BELIEVES POWER OPERATES

### 3.1 Control is achieved through the management of attention.

His foundational technique for controlling others — derived from carnival pedagogy and from the architecture of the trick shot itself — is the redirection of where the other party is looking. In teaching this was achieved by overpraising small successes and ignoring the failures one wanted internalized; in combat, by drawing the eye to the bow while the body adjusted; in social position, by directing the room's gaze to whatever performance currently confirmed him. He believes power is, fundamentally, the unilateral right to decide what people notice.

### 3.2 Control over another is achieved through conditional regard.

His pedagogy with the Barton boys is the cleanest demonstration of his actual theory of human management. Praise withheld becomes the only thing the student works for. Affection metered out at the precise moment of compliance produces the deepest dependence. He understood this without articulating it; the technique was passed to him, and he passed it forward. He believes — operatively — that warmth given freely is warmth wasted, because the recipient adjusts to it and ceases to perform.

This is the deepest and most damaging premise in his code, and the one with the longest blast radius. It is the engine of the Clint Barton wound. It is also the reason he is, against his self-image, an effective trainer: the technique works on the metric of skill acquisition. It costs the soul of the trained, but he does not regard the soul as a tracked variable.

### 3.3 Control over oneself is achieved through the suppression of affect into action.

His self-management doctrine is austere and consistent: *feel nothing, or feel it through the hand.* He treats emotion as a tremor to be drawn out of the draw arm. He believes the steadiness of the hand is the truest measure of a man — not because steadiness is virtue, but because steadiness is the visible proof of mastered interior. A trembling man is a man who has lost. He polices his own composure with the same severity he applies to a student's release.

The cost is enormous and he does not perceive it as a cost. Whole regions of his interior have been bound off and walled. The walls held for decades. They begin to fail in two situations: terminal illness, and the presence of Clint, who is both the proof of his pedagogy and the witness to his fraud — and is therefore the one stimulus the wall was not built to contain.

### 3.4 Control of a situation requires control of the exit.

Tactically he believes — and operates as if — every room has two doors, the announced one and the actual one, and the master of the room is whoever controls the actual one. He sites himself, in any space, with reference to lines of fire and lines of departure. This is autonomic; he does not think it. He chose his deathbed staging with the same care, controlling the room of his own death the way he would control any room he meant to win.

### 3.5 Control of a legacy requires the conscription of a successor.

He believes — and this becomes operationally dominant in the late period — that what one has built only persists if one names and binds an inheritor. He does not believe in legacy as influence diffused into the world; he believes in legacy as the transmission of the specific weapon to the specific hand. The deathbed summons of the protégé, the alternate-era passing of the *Trick Shot* name to a chosen successor, the insistence that someone carry the title forward — these are not sentimental gestures of an old man. They are doctrinal. The name must continue; the technique must continue; the *position* he occupied must continue. Without the successor, the past becomes inert and the ledger he spent his life writing is not enforced.

---

## 4. TRUST — THE THIN COLUMN OF WHO COUNTS

### 4.1 Trust is provisional, conditional, and revocable on a single infraction.

He does not trust as a continuum. He trusts as a binary. A person is in or out, and the test of being in is loyalty to the hierarchy of skill — which means, in practice, loyalty to him as the local apex. Crossing the line once moves the person permanently to *out* and reframes all prior conduct retroactively as evidence of latent disloyalty. This is the structural reason Clint, having exposed the embezzlement once, can never re-enter; the gate does not open in that direction.

### 4.2 Loyalty is the only virtue he recognizes; honesty is its antonym.

He genuinely believes that honesty, when it cuts against loyalty, is treachery. Clint's reporting of the theft is, in Buck's authentic reading, not the action of an honest boy but the action of a disloyal one. He does not pretend this in order to escape blame; he believes it because his moral primitive is the bond of the inner group, and the bond was broken by the report. The fact that the bond was already broken by the theft is invisible to him because he does not classify his own actions as candidates for the moral test — only others' responses to him.

### 4.3 The Swordsman is the model of the trusted equal; this slot is otherwise empty.

The partnership with Jacques Duquesne is the only sustained adult peer-trust in his record, and it operated on the basis of mutual criminal interest, mutual skill respect, and mutual non-intrusion into the other's interior. He trusted Duquesne not because Duquesne was reliable in the abstract but because their incentives aligned and neither asked the other to be more than competent and confederate. This is his template for the only kind of trust he can sustain: incentive-aligned, skill-respecting, interior-respecting, terminable on default. He has never had — and would not know how to maintain — a trust based on disclosure of weakness.

### 4.4 The protégé is the model of the trusted subordinate, and the trust is engineered, not given.

Trust downward, for him, is constructed through the pedagogical apparatus: the student becomes trustworthy by becoming a reproduction of the teacher. He trusts what he made. The instant the made thing exhibits independent judgment, the trust evaporates — because the trust was in the made-ness, not in the person. This is why the betrayal scene is the inevitable terminus of every protégé relationship he could ever undertake. The relationship structure cannot survive the moment the protégé becomes adult.

### 4.5 The employer is never trusted, and this is not paranoia, it is doctrine.

In his mercenary period he is meticulously transactional. He does not believe employers keep faith with hired guns; he does not extend faith to them. He delivers contracted work, takes payment, declines entanglement. This is the one zone of his life where his calibration is healthy, because it is the one zone where the cultural script — the hired gun's professional skepticism — perfectly matches his native organization.

### 4.6 Trust in self is total and brittle.

He trusts his hand, his eye, his calibration, his judgment of distance, his read of a room. The trust is total because the alternative — the admission of fallibility — is unbearable to his structure. It is brittle for the same reason; the first failure breaks it catastrophically rather than calibrating it. This is why aging is an existential threat and not a developmental challenge. A man who could trust himself partially could trust himself for longer. He cannot.

---

## 5. RISK — HIS PRIVATE ACCOUNTING

### 5.1 Risk is calculated against the ledger of reputation, not the ledger of life.

He will accept extraordinary bodily risk if the reputational upside is sufficient. He will refuse trivial bodily risk if the reputational downside includes being seen to take a shot he might miss. The actuarial unit is not life-years; it is *witnessed competence*. A shot that might cost him his life but would, if hit, be remembered, is preferable to a shot that costs nothing and would, if missed, be remembered for the wrong reason.

### 5.2 The unacceptable risk is the visible failure.

There is exactly one category of outcome he treats as catastrophic: being publicly out-performed by a peer or a former student. Death is not in this category. Capture is not. Even slow death by disease, properly staged, is not. Only the witnessed inferiority. His tactical decisions can be predicted by asking, of any option, *is there a path on which this ends in him being publicly second-best?* If yes, the option is closed regardless of expected value.

### 5.3 He under-prices long-horizon consequences and over-prices immediate position.

Like most subjects organized around present-moment status, he is a poor steward of futures. He does not build durable institutions, does not cultivate goodwill against future need, does not maintain bridges. The Barney/Clint adoption was the closest he came to investment in a future, and he liquidated it at the first immediate-position threat. He is the kind of operator who will burn next year's network to win this afternoon's argument, and will not perceive the trade as a trade.

### 5.4 He does not regard moral risk as risk at all.

The possibility that an action will damage his integrity, his relationships, his standing with himself, his peace of mind — these are not entries in his ledger. He is not amoral as a posture; he is amoral as an instrument calibration. The needles for those measurements were never installed.

### 5.5 He treats his own death, finally, as a problem of staging.

The terminal-cancer period clarifies his actual risk-relation to mortality. He is not afraid to die. He is afraid to die *uncomposed* — without a witness, without a successor, without a final shot that secures the ledger. The deathbed gesture is risk-accepted at maximum: he stakes the entire meaning of his life on whether the protégé will play the part. He does not perceive this as a gamble. He perceives it as the only available correct move.

---

## 6. HIS OWN PLACE — THE SELF AT THE CENTER OF THE COSMOLOGY

### 6.1 He believes he is the inheritor and the source.

He believes himself to be the legitimate carrier of a craft tradition that predates him and will outlive him only through his transmission. He believes the bow has a lineage and that he occupies its current node. This is grandiose, but it is not delusion; he is in fact, by carnival-circuit standards, an exceptional practitioner. The grandiosity is the *significance* he ascribes to the position, not the position itself.

### 6.2 He believes he was wronged before he ever wronged anyone.

The unspoken premise beneath the blame-externalization is a felt conviction that he is, at root, the one to whom debts are owed. Canon does not document the origin of this conviction. The behavior insists on its existence. He moves through the world like a creditor, and creditors do not perceive their collection as theft. This is the deepest and quietest layer of his operational code: every harm he inflicts is reclamation of something he believes was already his.

### 6.3 He believes the world owes him a stage.

The fury that surfaces when he is dismissed, ignored, denied his moment, is the fury of a man who experiences the denial as a violation of contract. He believes — operationally, not articulately — that having developed the skill, he is owed the audience. The collapse of the carnival circuit in the later decades is, for him, not a cultural shift but a personal grievance. The world failed to keep its end.

### 6.4 He believes he is the truth-teller in a world of polite lies.

His harshness, his contempt, his withholding — he experiences these as honesty. He believes the warm fathers, the encouraging teachers, the comforting friends are deceivers who flatter their charges into mediocrity, and that he alone tells the boy what the boy needs to hear. This is the moral self-justification that lets the cruelty feel like virtue. It is also the rationalization most resistant to challenge, because every protégé failure can be reframed as *I told them and they didn't listen*.

### 6.5 He believes himself indispensable to anyone he ever touched.

He does not believe Clint became a great archer despite him. He believes Clint became a great archer *because of him*, and that every later achievement of the protégé's life is an extension of the original training. He is not entirely wrong about the skill. He is entirely wrong about the personhood. The conflation — *I made the man, because I made the marksman* — is the single most dangerous belief in his code, because it gives him standing, in his own mind, to demand anything of the protégé up to and including the staging of his death.

### 6.6 He does not believe he will be forgotten, and he will not act to prevent it.

He believes the name *Trick Shot* will continue because the work was real. He does not, therefore, write down what he knows, does not document, does not memoirize. The transmission must be hand to hand. This is consistent with his belief that anything worth keeping moves through the body of a student, not through paper. It is also why his late-life conscription of a successor is so absolute: the successor is the only durable medium. Without the successor, he was right that he would not be forgotten — and wrong, because there would be no one left who could even speak the dialect.

---

## 7. THE UNARTICULATED AXIOMS — WHAT HE WOULD DENY BUT OPERATES BY

These are the load-bearing premises he would refuse to acknowledge if confronted, and which nonetheless dictate his behavior with the consistency of law.

- **That he is afraid.** He operates as a man managing a substantial undercurrent of fear — of exposure, of decline, of irrelevance, of having been wrong. He would deny the fear; the management of the fear organizes his day.
- **That he loved the boy.** Whatever survived of paternal affect was real, was suppressed, and continued to operate underground. The forty-year fixation on Clint is not the fixation of indifference. He would deny the affection; the persistence of the fixation is its proof.
- **That he was the one who broke it.** The certainty with which he blames Clint is the exact measure of the unbearableness of the alternative. He would die before saying so. He has, in fact, arranged to die without saying so.
- **That the audience he requires is, finally, the protégé.** The carnival crowd, the criminal employer, the lawman, the rival — none of these are the audience that matters. The audience that matters is the one student who saw him at his worst and would, with one shot, settle the ledger. This is why the deathbed gesture takes the form it does. He would deny that any one witness matters more than the crowd. He has built his death around the one witness.
- **That his code is borrowed, not authored.** He believes he derived his discipline from first principles in the practice of the bow. He inherited it, almost in full, from whoever taught him under whatever harder hand than his own, and he has been re-performing that inheritance for sixty years without examination. He would deny it. He could not produce a single original premise if asked.

---

## 8. OPERATIONAL SUMMARY FOR HANDLERS

Reading the man on his own terms: he is a closed code, internally consistent, externally legible, dangerously stable. He cannot be reasoned out of the structure because the structure does not have a reasoning surface; it has only the targeting surface and the loyalty surface. Engage him on the targeting surface and he is predictable to within inches. Engage him on the loyalty surface and he is predictable to within decades. Engage him on the moral surface and he is not there.

The single intervention that destabilizes him is the one he has spent his life forbidding: the unanswerable demonstration, in front of a witness whose judgment he cannot dismiss, that the ledger he has been keeping is wrong — that the protégé surpassed him not as student but as person, that the embezzlement was his, that the boy he beat told the truth. He has structured his entire existence to make this demonstration impossible. He has structured his death to ensure it cannot occur posthumously. The pathology and the doctrine are, at this depth, a single object.

— END SECTION 5 —


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK — Bernard "Buck" Barton, alias Trick Shot

*Subsection of UATU Tier-3 Adversary Dossier. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological) and §5 (Personality).*

---

## I. The Operative Code, As Enacted

Buck Barton does not have what a moral philosopher would recognize as an ethical system. He has a **loyalty economy** — a set of operating rules organized around hierarchy, performance, and the obligations of the lesser party to the greater. To call this a "code" at all is to grant it more coherence than it possesses; it is closer to a set of habituated reflexes which the subject has, over decades, rationalized into the appearance of principle. What follows is the reconstruction of that code from observed behavior across every documented appearance from 1983 forward.

The first-order axioms, as enacted:

1. **Skill is the only legitimating credential.** A man who can shoot is owed deference; a man who cannot is owed nothing. This is the foundation of every other rule. Moral standing scales with demonstrated mastery. The unskilled have no standing to judge the skilled — which is why Clint's exposure of the embezzlement is processed by Buck not as a moral act but as a *category violation*: the student presuming to evaluate the master.

2. **The transmitter of skill is owed permanent fealty by the receiver.** The teaching is a debt the student cannot discharge. Buck genuinely believes — and this is critical, it is not posture — that having drilled Clint into a marksman has earned him an unrevokable moral claim on Clint's loyalty. Subsequent theft, abuse, or attempted murder do not, in his ledger, diminish that claim. The debt is structural, not contingent on his conduct.

3. **Loyalty supersedes legality, honesty, and life.** He will steal from an employer (the carnival); he will lie to a partner; he will kill for hire. None of these violate the code because none of them touch the loyalty axis. He will not, however, betray a confederate of equal standing — the partnership with the Swordsman is, by his own lights, never breached from his side. Equality of station produces a stable bond; inequality produces only duty flowing upward.

4. **Exposure is the cardinal sin.** Worse than theft, worse than violence, worse than abandonment: being *seen* in a diminished light. Clint's offense was not noticing the embezzlement; it was making the noticing public, refusing to swallow it. To Buck, this is the only act for which he has no forgiveness vocabulary at all. Forty years of intermittent contract violence proceed from this one rule.

5. **The body in performance is sacred; everything else is negotiable.** He will not foul his draw, will not shoot drunk on a job, will not let a witnessed performance be less than his best. This is the closest thing in him to a religious observance. Off the line, virtually any conduct is permissible.

6. **Death is to be staged, not suffered.** The deathbed summons is the most consistent expression of his actual ethics: the end must be *authored*, performed, witnessed, and ideally choreographed through the body of the one who owes him most.

---

## II. What He Will Do

The catalogue is wide and worth specifying, because the absence of internal prohibition is itself the diagnostic:

- **Take a child into his custody and train him.** Will do. Has done twice (Clint, and the later "successor" figure). Frames it as generosity; experiences it as acquisition.
- **Withhold food, sleep, or warmth as pedagogical tools.** Will do, has done — the training flashbacks repeatedly show conditional sustenance, the small cruelties of the drill instructor amplified by domestic intimacy.
- **Strike a child for a missed shot.** Will do. Frames it as standards.
- **Beat a child in punitive rage.** Will do — the abandonment scene. Frames it, retroactively, as discipline against disloyalty.
- **Steal from his employer.** Will do. Frames it as taking what was owed, or as not really stealing because the carnival is "his" by virtue of being its main draw.
- **Take paid contracts to kill.** Will do, repeatedly, across decades.
- **Take a paid contract to kill his former protégé.** Will do — and this is the diagnostic edge — and will *prefer* such a contract, will seek it, will accept reduced fee or unfavorable terms for the privilege.
- **Train a second protégé as a deliberate symbolic injury to the first.** Will do (the late-era successor arc). The instrumentalization of pedagogy as wound is fully conscious.
- **Lie to a partner of equal standing — but only by omission.** Active deception of a peer is rare; selective non-disclosure is routine.
- **Stage his own death to coerce an emotional response from the protégé.** Will do. Has done. This is the apex of the code as he enacts it.

---

## III. What He Will Not Do (And Why The Exceptions Matter)

The prohibitions are fewer than the permissions, and every one of them is structural rather than ethical — i.e., each prohibition exists because violation would damage his self-concept as the master, not because the act itself is wrong.

- **He will not shoot poorly on purpose to deceive an audience.** A staged miss to manipulate a target's behavior is, in his cosmology, a form of self-mutilation. He will arrange any number of stratagems that do not require the bow to lie.
- **He will not accept a contract in a discipline he is not the best at.** A jealous protection of his unique brand. He turns down rifle work, has been observed declining knife jobs, will not be subcontracted as generic muscle. The bow or nothing.
- **He will not work for an employer who has publicly insulted him.** Even at the cost of significant fees. Status injuries are not absorbable.
- **He will not break the formal partnership covenant with the Swordsman.** Across the entire record, his betrayals run downward (Clint) or outward (employers, marks), never sideways (Duquesne). Peer-bond is the one stable structure in his moral architecture.
- **He will not, when sober and in possession of his faculties, kill a child.** This is observable rather than stated. The absence is real but should not be sentimentalized: he will *raise* a child into a weapon and discard the child if the weapon fails, which is a different kind of harm operating on a longer time horizon.
- **He will not beg.** Not for money, not for forgiveness, not for life. This is not courage; it is the cost of preserving the master-position which begging would terminally collapse.
- **He will not seek reconciliation on the other party's terms.** Clint has, by documented count across the canon, offered some form of amends, reunion, or peace on at least five distinct occasions. Each offer is met with renewed hostility. The prohibition here is total: to accept reconciliation offered by the inferior is to ratify the inferior's standing to offer it.

---

## IV. Justifications — The Internal Rhetoric

When Buck explains himself — and he does explain himself, at length, when the audience requires it — the rhetoric is remarkably stable across forty years of appearances. The vocabulary is small. The recurring justificatory moves:

- **"I made you."** The single most frequent line of self-defense, in some variant, across every confrontation with Clint. It is offered as if it settled the matter — and within his code, it does. The making is the claim.
- **"You were nothing when I found you."** A complementary move: establishing the starting baseline so the debt of the lifting is properly visible.
- **"This is how it is done."** The pedagogy-as-natural-law move. His harshness is not chosen but inherited from the necessities of the craft.
- **"You broke faith."** The exposure-as-betrayal move. Notice that the content of what Clint exposed is never addressed; only the act of exposure.
- **"I owe you nothing."** Variant: "I gave you everything." Both function. The asymmetry is the point — the master can never be in debt to the student.
- **"At least I am honest about what I am."** A late-career move; he begins, in the post-Gruenwald appearances, to claim a kind of bleak integrity for not pretending to be other than ruthless. This is a sophisticated defensive evolution: weaponizing the candor of cruelty as a moral virtue against the supposed hypocrisy of those who try to be better.

Notably absent from the rhetoric, across the entire canon: any acknowledgment of theft as theft; any acknowledgment of having struck a child; any acknowledgment of having abandoned a child; any acknowledgment of error. The justifications are all forward-facing — claims on the other — never backward-facing reckonings.

---

## V. Consistency vs. Fracture

The code is **internally consistent at the level of structure** and **fractured at the level of content**. Meaning: the rules above genuinely organize his behavior across forty years of appearances; he is not erratic. But the rules cannot survive examination from outside, because they are built on a premise — that skill confers moral standing and that the transmitter of skill is owed permanent fealty — that no other agent in his universe ratifies. The fractures appear at the seams where his code meets others':

- **Fracture 1: The Swordsman as confederate.** The peer-bond rule works in the partnership era. In the later mercenary period, when both have moved into Avengers-adjacent criminal employ, the code provides no instruction for what is owed an aging peer in decline. Buck's documented conduct toward Duquesne in late appearances drifts; the firm rule blurs into a softer indifference that the code itself cannot account for.

- **Fracture 2: Money vs. status.** The rules order status above money. But Buck takes paid contracts whose execution would erode his status (low-rent jobs, work for employers beneath him). The code says no; the bank account says yes. He resolves the contradiction with a private fiction: every job is a "demonstration," not a wage. The fiction is thin and visibly strains under pressure.

- **Fracture 3: The protégé's surpassing.** Clint becomes, by every objective measure, the better archer. The code has no provision for the student exceeding the master without thereby canceling the master's claim. Buck's response is to refuse to register the surpassing — to keep treating Clint as the apprentice — which works as defense but produces the lifelong compulsion to re-encounter and re-test, because the unresolved comparison is unbearable.

- **Fracture 4: Terminal illness.** The code presumes a body capable of performance. Cancer is a category his rules do not contemplate. The deathbed staging is the attempt to reabsorb the uncategorizable event into the code by *performing the dying* — making even the cancer a routine to be shot. The reach is visible, and the strain shows.

- **Fracture 5: The second protégé.** Training a successor is, by his own rules, an act of pedagogy that should create a new debt-of-loyalty owed to him. But he trains the successor specifically as a weapon *against* Clint, which means the new pedagogy is instrumentalized to an old wound. The code does not survive this hybridization — the late-career Trick Shot is, by his own standards, debased, and on some pre-reflective level he knows it. The viciousness of the late period is in part the reaction-formation against this awareness.

---

## VI. Shifts Across Time

The code does not evolve so much as **harden, simplify, and then crack** across the recorded life. Phases:

**Carnival period (decades pre-publication, recovered via flashback).** The code is at its broadest functional range. He operates within a community (the carnival), holds a steady employer-of-record, maintains a peer-partnership, raises apprentices. The loyalty economy works because the community is small enough that everyone occupies a clear rank. Theft is a private supplement to a public role. Cruelty is intermittent and rationalized as pedagogy.

**Exposure and exile (the foundational event).** The code suffers its only true rupture in this period — for a brief window, between the embezzlement's exposure and the abandonment, Buck is *unable to justify himself* and resorts to violence as the only available substitute for argument. This is the single moment in the record where his moral apparatus is observably overwhelmed. The post-violence narrative reframing (Clint as traitor) is, in effect, the emergency repair that becomes the permanent rule.

**Mercenary years.** Code narrows to its operational core: take the job, do the job, charge for the job, never miss. The community context is gone; the loyalty economy reduces to peer-bonds with confederates and contempt for marks. The pedagogy capacity goes dormant. This is the most morally legible period — he is simply a competent hired marksman with a grudge — and the most boring, which is why the canon brings him into proximity with Clint as often as possible.

**Recurrence period.** The compulsion to seek out Clint structures his choices in ways that begin to violate his own efficiency. He takes worse contracts to be in Clint's orbit. He inflates rivalries with other archers (the various "world's greatest archer" beats) past their tactical utility. The code begins to be deformed by the unmetabolized injury at its center — exposure — which he cannot stop revisiting.

**Terminal phase.** The hardening is total. Affect, never broad, narrows to contempt and the cold pleasure of arrangement. The code becomes almost entirely about *the staging of the ending* — who will be present, who will hold the bow, who will witness. The earlier carnival showmanship returns transfigured as deathbed theater. The successor is groomed not as a continuation of the craft but as a prop in the final scene.

**Post-terminal residue (in the second Trick Shot, in Clint's ongoing relational pattern).** The code outlives the man. The successor, where deployed, carries forward the same loyalty-economy logic. Clint Barton, every time he opens to a mentor figure, is operating inside the framework Buck installed. The most accurate statement about Buck's ethics is that *they are not finished*; they continue to organize the conduct of other people decades after his death.

---

## VII. The Diagnostic Center

If the entire moral framework had to be reduced to one sentence, it would be this: **Buck Barton believes that the person who teaches you to do something has, by that act, purchased the right to define what you owe him forever — and that you have, by accepting the teaching, sold something you cannot buy back.**

Every observable behavior — the punitive pedagogy, the rage at exposure, the lifelong return to the protégé, the deathbed coercion, the grooming of a successor as a posthumous reproach — derives cleanly from that single premise. The premise is not idiosyncratic to him; versions of it circulate in master-apprentice traditions across every craft culture on record. What is idiosyncratic is the absolutism with which he holds it, the absence of any counterweight (no countervailing belief in autonomy, in mutual obligation, in the possibility of repair), and the willingness to enforce it with violence across a lifetime.

The code is, in the end, the disorder wearing the costume of a tradition. The cruelty of the man is, in the end, the cruelty of the premise carried to its conclusions without restraint. To call it a moral framework is precise as long as one understands that the framework is built to license rather than to constrain — the rules exist not to tell him what he must not do but to explain, after the fact, why what he did was owed.

— END SECTION —


## Communications & Linguistic Profile
