# 6. COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON

*Cross-reference: Section 3 (Psychological), Section 5 (Personality). All verbal data sourced from Hawkeye Vol.1 #1–4 (Gruenwald, 1983); Solo Avengers #1–4; West Coast Avengers appearances; Hawkeye: Blindspot; assorted backgrounder material. Linguistic inferences are extrapolations from documented dialogue and behavioral context.*

---

## 6.1 Baseline Register

The subject operates from a single dominant register — a clipped, mid-Western American carnival vernacular, masculine-coded, late-Depression-cohort, with the residual cadence of a man who learned to project his voice across a midway tent before he learned to modulate it for a room. The voice is built for the bark, not the conversation. He does not whisper well; under stress he reverts to projection regardless of whether the room requires it. Volume is one of his tells: when he wants to seem most controlled, he becomes slightly *louder* than the conversational baseline, because his idea of authority is a stage-voice.

Sentence architecture is short, declarative, and end-stopped. He favors the imperative and the indicative; he avoids the subjunctive almost entirely. He does not hypothesize aloud. "If" clauses appear chiefly as threats ("If you'd kept your mouth shut—") rather than as exploratory thinking. The conditional, in his mouth, is always retrospective and accusatory.

Lexicon is small, concrete, kinetic. Verbs of striking, hitting, drawing, putting (a shot, a man, a thing) down. Nouns drawn from the body, the weapon, the trade. Abstractions are rare and, when they appear, are stock — *loyalty*, *honor*, *guts*, *nerve*, *backbone* — never examined, never disassembled. He uses these words the way he uses arrows: as fixed implements with known properties.

He is functionally monolingual in English but salts speech with carnival cant and showman's argot: *mark*, *rube*, *roust*, *flash*, *grift*, *the lot*, *the tip* (for the gathered crowd), *blow the show*. These are not affectations; they are the dialect of the only world that ever conferred status on him, and his persistent use of them into mercenary and deathbed contexts is a clinging — verbal evidence that he never psychologically left the midway.

---

## 6.2 Diction & Word-Choice Tells

**Pronoun economy.** Heavy first-person, sparing second-person, the third-person reserved for contempt. He addresses Clint directly in confrontation but talks *about* him in the third person when others are in the room — even when Clint is present — a status maneuver that converts the protégé into an object of discussion. ("Kid's got the hands. Always did. Wasted on him.") The shift from *you* to *he* in the presence of an audience is a reliable indicator that the subject has moved into performance mode and that the temperature has risen.

**Diminutives as control.** He almost never uses Clint's given name in their early relationship. *Kid*, *boy*, *son* (rare, weaponized), and later — when distance is being asserted — *Hawkeye*, said with a faint downward inflection that turns the codename into a mild sneer. Use of "Clint" by the subject is statistically anomalous and signals one of three states: (a) genuine, fleeting affect breakthrough (extremely rare, mostly inferred from late-era panels); (b) calculated softening preceding a manipulation; (c) terminal-context address, where he uses the name to bind the listener into the deathbed scene.

**The honor-vocabulary cluster.** Words he reaches for under any pressure to justify himself: *square*, *straight*, *clean*, *fair*, *honest*, *true*. The frequency is diagnostic — a man who uses *honest* this often in self-description is managing an internal accusation. Note especially the construction "I always played you straight," variants of which appear across decades. The word "always" in his mouth is a perjury marker; it appears almost exclusively in statements that are demonstrably false at the moment of utterance.

**Skill-vocabulary as moral vocabulary.** The categories *good*, *sloppy*, *clean*, *tight*, *loose*, *off* — borrowed from shot assessment — bleed into his evaluation of persons. People are *tight* or *loose*, *clean* or *sloppy*, *on* or *off*. He does not have a separate moral lexicon; ethics for him is craft-quality applied to behavior. This is why moral argument bounces off him: the words register as inapposite, the way one would not critique a meal in metric units.

**The absent vocabulary.** Words and word-classes he almost never produces: *sorry*, *afraid*, *hurt* (in the first person), *love*, *miss*, *wish*, *should have*, *I was wrong*. Their absence across hundreds of pages of dialogue is not stylistic; it is structural. The subject's lexicon is missing the entire apparatus of repair. When a writer puts any of these words in his mouth (rare, late-era, usually preceding manipulation), it reads as ventriloquism — which is precisely what it is, intradiegetically: he is using borrowed language to produce an effect he does not feel.

---

## 6.3 Rhetoric & Argumentative Pattern

His rhetoric is built on three moves, deployed in rotation:

**The inversion.** Accusation becomes accusation-of-accusation. Caught stealing, he frames Clint's reporting as the moral failure. The grammatical form is reliable: "You— you'd turn on *me*?" The pronoun stress, the incredulous lift, the relocation of the verb of betrayal onto the witness. This move is so automatic it functions like a reflex arc rather than a thought.

**The credentialed dismissal.** Any challenge is answered first by reasserting his standing as the teacher, the source, the one who made the challenger possible. "Everything you've got, you got from *me*." "Who put that bow in your hand?" "You were nothing — a runaway with a sore back — before I—" The structure is invariant: a possessive claim on the interlocutor's competence, followed by an implied debt. He does not argue the point at issue; he argues his standing to be heard, and treats the establishment of that standing as the argument's conclusion.

**The craft-demonstration as rebuttal.** When verbal pressure exceeds his tolerance, he shifts modes — he shoots. The pulled bow, the demonstration shot, the wordless display is, for him, a complete rhetorical act. He believes the demonstration has answered the question. This is consistent with the cognitive style profiled in §3: he does not have a conceptual register adequate to the conflicts he is in, so he routes the dispute back to the only domain in which he is articulate.

He does not joke well. His humor is exclusively at the expense of others' competence, delivered deadpan, often missed by the targets as humor because there is no warmth carrier. ("Nice grouping. For a blind man.") This is the carnival roustabout's needle, never the comedian's invitation. Laughter, when it occurs, is a single short exhalation through the nose, not a vocalized laugh — a tell so consistent it can be used as a polygraph: a vocalized laugh from this subject is performed and should be treated as preface to manipulation or violence.

---

## 6.4 Communication of Affection

The subject does not say affection; he encodes it in three substitutional channels.

**Critique-as-care.** The harsh correction is, in his economy, the affectionate gesture. To bother correcting a man is to invest in him. Silence and dismissal are the punishments. Early Clint flashbacks show this clearly: Buck's longest speeches to the boy are technical breakdowns of error, delivered in a sustained low tone without anger — the closest the subject comes to tenderness. The protégé who learns to read this dialect feels loved by the criticism, which is the trap.

**Tool-transfer.** Gifts of equipment — a bow, a quiver, a particular arrow — function as declarations he cannot otherwise make. The handing-over of a personal tool is, for him, an utterance in a private language. The deathbed bestowal of name and weapon to a successor is the maximal form of this and should be read as the closest thing he can produce to a love-statement, however contaminated by control.

**The withheld praise that arrives once.** He banks praise and pays out a single phrase, late, after extended withholding. "You'll do." "Not bad, kid." "You can shoot." These flat compliments, calibrated to seem grudging, are his I-love-yous. He gives them with deliberate undervaluation because to give them at face value would expose the affect. The undervaluation is the affection's *signature*; a fulsome compliment from this subject would be a lie or a setup.

He cannot say the word *love*. Across canon, he does not produce it in earnest in any documented instance. When he gestures at it on the deathbed, the construction is invariably oblique — *you were the only one who*, *I never had a*, *the closest thing I ever* — a syntax of approach-without-arrival that lets him point at the feeling without ever placing it in his own mouth.

---

## 6.5 Communication of Threat

Threat-language is where the subject is most stylistically distinctive and most disciplined. He does not bluster. The shouted threat, the chest-puffed challenge, the gangster's elaborate promise — none of these. His threats are characterized by four features:

**Low-volume delivery.** Threats drop a half-step in volume below his conversational baseline. The voice does not rise; it goes still. This inversion of expected acoustics is one of his most reliable tells: when the subject quiets, the room should clear.

**The conditional as warning.** Threats are framed as descriptive forecasts of consequence rather than declarations of intent: "Man pulls on me, he doesn't pull twice." "Kid talks like that, he loses teeth." The third-person generic-masculine construction is consistent; it converts the threat into a statement of natural law, distancing him from authorship of the violence he is promising. The grammar exonerates in advance.

**The skill-referent.** Threats name the weapon and the body part in technical proximity: "I can put one through the *meat* of your hand from across this lot." The specificity is the menace; he does not threaten harm in the abstract, he threatens a particular shot. This is also how he flirts with violence in non-violent settings — a casual reference to a precise anatomical target inserted into ordinary conversation, monitored for the listener's reaction.

**The pause before draw.** Verbally, this manifests as a terminal silence at the end of a threat-sentence — not an ellipsis, a full stop and then quiet. He does not fill the air after the threat. The silence is part of the utterance.

He does not issue warnings he will not carry out. The bluffing register, common in mercenary peers, is absent. This makes his threats unusually credible and is one reason competent adversaries take him seriously despite the relatively old-fashioned costume of his persona.

---

## 6.6 Communication of Grief, Loss, and Fear

The subject has no native dialect for grief. When grief-pressure is on him, three substitutions appear:

**Anger-displacement.** Loss is expressed as accusation of whoever is nearest. The death of confederates (the Swordsman, eventually) produces in him not mourning but a brief, vicious targeting of a proximate other — usually phrased as a complaint about the dead man's competence. ("Damn fool stood where I told him not to stand.") The grammar of mourning collapses into the grammar of post-mortem instruction, as if death itself were a botched shot to be coached.

**Time-collapse and reminiscence.** Under loss, he becomes briefly garrulous about the past — specifically about technical or operational details from the carnival years, never about emotional content. He will narrate a particular shot, a particular night's take, a particular roustabout's habit, in flat detail, as if reading from a ledger. This is grief in his dialect: the dead are addressed by being inventoried.

**The body-tell substitution.** Where verbal grief is absent, somatic signals appear: a tightening around the eyes, a slowing of speech tempo, a temporary loss of the carnival argot (the dialect markers thin and the speech becomes more standard, more depleted). The flattening of the idiolect is the only audible mourning.

Fear is similarly unsayable. He does not produce *afraid*, *scared*, *worried* in the first person. Anxiety surfaces as *irritation* directed at a proximate scapegoat ("Quit fidgeting"), or as a sharpening of pedagogical attention — under stress he begins to instruct, because instruction is the only mode in which he feels regulated. A sudden didactic turn from this subject in a non-instructional context is a fear tell.

The terminal diagnosis produces, predictably, none of the conventional grief vocabulary. Instead, it produces an *uptick* in two patterns: the credentialed dismissal (he becomes louder about his historical mastery) and the staging language (he begins to speak in scene-directions, as if narrating a final performance — "When you come in, you'll see—" "I want you standing—"). This is the deathbed pathology in linguistic form: he is not dying, he is *directing* his death.

---

## 6.7 Deflection, Evasion, and the Architecture of Lying

The subject is a competent but unimaginative liar. His lies have signatures.

**The pivot to grievance.** Direct questions about wrongdoing are not answered; they are reframed as evidence of the questioner's disloyalty. "You're asking me *that*?" The interrogative pivot is reflexive within roughly half a second of the question; the speed itself is the tell.

**The appeal to record.** He invokes his history as exonerating: years of service, years of teaching, the long ledger of his competence. The construction "After everything I—" appears under nearly every accusation. The clause is rarely completed; he relies on the listener to fill in the debt.

**The categorical denial without specifics.** When he denies, he denies wholesale and refuses elaboration. "Didn't happen." "Wasn't me." "Talk's cheap." A man who genuinely did not do the thing tends to want to explain; the subject's refusal to elaborate is consistent with guilt managed through compression rather than narrative.

**The shift to second-person interrogation.** He moves from defendant to prosecutor mid-conversation: "And what were *you* doing that night?" The switch is rhetorical and usually unsupported by actual knowledge of the interlocutor's whereabouts; it is a procedural move, not an evidentiary one.

He does not, however, fabricate elaborate cover stories. His lying is subtractive — denial, omission, redirection — not generative. He cannot sustain an invented narrative under cross-examination because the invention requires an imaginative range he does not have. Pressed for detail on a denial, he will become hostile rather than inventive. Hostility in response to a request for specifics is, with this subject, a confession-equivalent.

---

## 6.8 Pedagogical Register

A distinct sub-register: when teaching, his voice changes. It drops in volume, slows in tempo, loses the carnival sharpness, and becomes — measurably — the warmest mode he produces. Sentences lengthen slightly. The lexicon becomes precise and almost gentle in its technicality: *anchor*, *release*, *follow-through*, *breath*, *the still point between heartbeats*. He teaches in physical metaphors of stillness and economy. He can describe a draw cycle for two minutes without interruption, with internal consistency and observable pleasure in the description.

This is the only register in which his affect is regulated and accessible. It is also the register he weaponized against Clint — the warmth was real, in this mode, which is why the withdrawal of it as punishment was annihilating. Operators interacting with the subject should note: to draw him into the pedagogical register (by asking a technical question about the bow) is to access his most cooperative state, and is the single reliable de-escalation lever available.

---

## 6.9 Self-Reference and the Naming Question

The alias *Trick Shot* — chosen, retained, defended — is itself a linguistic data point. He refers to himself by it readily, more readily than by *Bernard* or *Buck*. The legal name appears in canon almost exclusively in third-party reference; he does not introduce himself as Bernard. *Buck* is the carnival-era handle, used by intimates of that period (Swordsman, old carnies); *Trick Shot* is the public-facing professional identity. The proportions of self-naming track the eras: in the carnival flashbacks he tolerates *Buck*; in mercenary years he asserts *Trick Shot*; on the deathbed he reaches for *Buck* again, an attempted return to the period of his last unbroken self-image.

The name *Bernard* discomfits him. On the rare occasions it is used to his face by an adversary or a clinician-type figure, he responds with a sharp correction or a refusal to acknowledge. The given name belongs to whatever pre-carnival childhood he has expunged from the record; the carnival names are his self-construction. To call him Bernard is to gesture at the part of him that was made rather than self-made — and the reaction (irritation, sometimes pronounced) suggests the vulnerability is intact.

---

## 6.10 Tells, Summary Index

For field reference, the linguistic tells that warrant immediate attention:

- **Drop in volume below baseline** → imminent violence likely.
- **Shift from second to third person about a present party** → status performance engaged; humiliation incoming.
- **Use of "always" in a self-descriptive sentence** → the statement is false.
- **Vocalized (rather than nasal) laugh** → performed; manipulation or attack pending.
- **Sudden didactic turn in non-instructional context** → fear or destabilization.
- **Thinning of carnival argot, flatter standard speech** → grief or somatic distress.
- **Use of "Clint" rather than "kid" / "Hawkeye"** → either rare affect breakthrough or calculated softening; context-dependent, treat as high-information.
- **Request for technical detail produces fluent warmth** → de-escalation lever available.
- **Request for narrative detail on a denial produces hostility** → confession-equivalent.
- **Scene-direction grammar ("when you come in, you'll see—")** → staging mode engaged; the subject is constructing a tableau and the listener is being cast.

---

## 6.11 Synthesis

The subject's language is the language of a man who learned to be heard before he learned to be understood, and never came back for the second lesson. Every feature of his idiolect — the bark-cadence, the carnival cant, the imperative-heavy syntax, the absent vocabulary of repair, the substitution of craft-words for moral words, the encoding of affection in critique and tool-transfer, the directorial grammar of the death scene — converges on a single portrait: a man whose interior life was routed through performance so completely that he no longer has a non-performed register available to him. Even his silence is staged. Even his deathbed is blocked and lit.

The pathos, and the operational risk, is the same fact: there is a real man inside this voice, with real feeling, and he has lost the linguistic equipment to reach himself. He cannot say what he means because he has spent sixty years building a mouth that cannot form those words. Clint Barton, the long-suffering listener, learned the dialect young, which is why he still hears love in the critique and why the subject can still, after forty years, reach him with a single technical sentence.

— END SECTION 6 —


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Subject: Bernard "Buck" Barton, alias Trick Shot*
*Section purpose: forward-projection of probable behavior in everyday, social, and low-tempo operational settings the canon never depicted. Each entry: GIVEN condition → EXPECTED behavior, with derivation. Confidence flagged where useful.*

---

## A. MORNINGS, ROOMS, AND THE BODY

**GIVEN** a fixed lodging — motel, trailer, rented room, safehouse — over more than three nights.
**EXPECT** the room to be arranged within twenty minutes of arrival into a stable, repeatable geometry: bed against the long wall, single chair angled to face the door, bow case or rifle case at the foot of the bed on the side of his dominant hand, boots placed parallel beneath the chair. He will not unpack into drawers. Toiletries laid out in a single row on whatever flat surface is nearest the sink, in left-to-right order of use. He resents disorder around him not aesthetically but tactically — a man who has been jumped before, and a man whose self-image cannot tolerate the visual disorganization that would reflect badly on him to an imagined observer. *(High confidence; derived from carnival nomadism + dismissive-avoidant control needs.)*

**GIVEN** the first hour after waking.
**EXPECT** a fixed sequence executed without deviation: piss, splash of cold water on the face (no shower yet), black coffee brewed strong enough to chew, then — before food, before dressing fully — a dry-fire or dry-draw ritual of fifteen to thirty repetitions. The body must report to the bow before it reports to the day. Breakfast (if any) is functional: eggs, toast, more coffee; he eats standing or at a counter, not sitting at a table. Sitting at a table is for company, and he keeps no company that would warrant it.

**GIVEN** any mirror.
**EXPECT** brief utilitarian use — shave, comb, check teeth — then immediate disengagement. He does not study his face. Self-image is held in the body's competence, not the face's appearance; the face has been aging and he refuses to negotiate with it.

**GIVEN** a shower.
**EXPECT** cold-finished, brief, the towel folded back over the rod rather than dropped. He will dress before leaving the bathroom. Modesty is not the driver; the driver is the dismissive-avoidant unwillingness to be caught half-equipped by any unanticipated stimulus, even his own.

---

## B. THE DAILY PRACTICE

**GIVEN** any 24-hour period not actively under combat or transit.
**EXPECT** a minimum of ninety minutes with the bow, segmented: thirty minutes of form work at short range, thirty of grouping at standard ranges, thirty of "trick" — moving targets, off-hand, blind draws, the spectacle repertoire that is, for him, the actual identity work. The trick portion is non-negotiable; if pressed, he will skip the grouping work before he skips the trick work. Tells you what the bow is *for* in his psyche: not killing, *being witnessed killing*.

**GIVEN** the practice is interrupted by an observer he did not invite.
**EXPECT** a performance escalation — harder shot, longer range, more theatrical setup — disguised as continued routine. He will not acknowledge the observer until the impressive shot lands. Acknowledgment will be a sidelong line, dry, calibrated to read as indifference while having required the observer's presence to mean anything.

**GIVEN** the practice is observed by a young person who shows talent.
**EXPECT** initial cold appraisal, then a single corrective intervention — usually a wordless adjustment of stance or grip, hands on the kid's elbow, not a sentence. This is the bait. If the kid responds with the right combination of attention and submission, the protégé pattern engages within forty-eight hours. The pattern is involuntary; he has been re-running it, in skeleton form, since Clint.

**GIVEN** a missed shot in private.
**EXPECT** no verbal reaction. A second shot, immediate, to overwrite the miss. If the second misses, equipment inspection — string, fletching, nock — performed with exaggerated patience that is the visible form of the rage he will not name. He does not, in the canon-derived organization, accept that he missed; the equipment missed, the light missed, the wind missed.

**GIVEN** a missed shot in public.
**EXPECT** the same equipment-blame, voiced this time, but with a contemptuous joke layered over it. The joke is for the audience; the equipment-blame is for him. Confidence very high — projection is his load-bearing defense and will not absent itself just because there's a crowd.

---

## C. EATING, DRINKING, SMOKING

**GIVEN** a bar, diner, or roadhouse during downtime.
**EXPECT** a seat with the door in his line of sight and a wall behind him. He will order one of two things — beer or bourbon, never both, never mixed drinks — and nurse it longer than the rhythm of the room suggests. His drinking is steady, not heavy in any one sitting, but daily and load-bearing in the way an inflammation responds to constant low-dose suppressant. Probable hepatic strain by late middle age; alcohol-use disorder by clinical criteria, not by his own self-concept, which would reject the label as the diagnosis of a lesser man.

**GIVEN** food in public.
**EXPECT** plain orders, conservative — steak, eggs, potatoes, coffee. No questions to the waitress beyond what's needed. He will not send food back; he will eat what came and never return to the place. Tips on the low end of acceptable, more if the waitress was deferential, less if she chatted. The transaction logic is *recognition for service rendered exactly as I wanted it*; anything else costs.

**GIVEN** offered a cigarette.
**EXPECT** acceptance whether he is currently smoking or not. The ritual of the shared light is one of the few approach behaviors his repertoire allows.

**GIVEN** a meal with one other person, equal or near-equal in status (e.g., the Swordsman in the old days, a fellow contractor now).
**EXPECT** sparse conversation oriented entirely around work, equipment, mutual acquaintances rated and ranked. No personal disclosure. He laughs at his own jokes more than at others'; he leaves first.

---

## D. SPEECH, VOICE, LINGUISTIC TELLS

**GIVEN** any verbal exchange.
**EXPECT** a low-register, slightly nasal carnival-South cadence — the geographically displaced accent of the touring midway, sanded down but never gone. Short sentences. Heavy use of second-person scolding even in non-instructional contexts ("you don't draw past the corner of your mouth, you draw to it"). The pedagogical register is his default. He instructs in lieu of relating.

**GIVEN** he wishes to insult.
**EXPECT** the insult to be *technical*: not "coward" but "you flinched at release," not "fool" but "you couldn't hit the broadside of a barn from the inside." The cruelty is routed through the skill domain because the skill domain is the only domain he fully credits as real.

**GIVEN** he wishes to praise.
**EXPECT** the praise to be subtractive: "Not bad." "That'll do." "Better." The full sentence "you shot well" is rare and reserved as a structural reward — a coin he keeps scarce so that its issue means something. He learned, somewhere, that praise diluted is praise wasted; it is the only piece of pedagogical wisdom he holds correctly and the one that has done the most damage.

**GIVEN** he is asked about his own past — childhood, family, where he came up.
**EXPECT** deflection via anecdote: a carnival story, usually a story in which he was already the marksman, with no antecedent. The absence of any pre-bow biography in his self-narrative is itself the tell. He has edited his own origin out. *(High confidence; the defense organization requires it.)*

**GIVEN** he is asked about Clint Barton.
**EXPECT** a contemptuous brevity, increasingly performed the more the questioner persists. The phrase will land within two sentences: *the kid was disloyal*. He will not elaborate the embezzlement that preceded the disloyalty. If pressed, the rage spikes and the conversation is over — chair pushed back, money on the table, exit. This is the load-bearing fault line; no other topic produces the same speed of exit.

---

## E. CLOTHING, KIT, AND THE BODY-SURFACE

**GIVEN** civilian dress.
**EXPECT** a narrow wardrobe in repeated forms: dark jeans or canvas trousers, plain shirts (denim, flannel by season), a leather jacket or weathered duster depending on era and region, boots maintained meticulously. No jewelry beyond a watch — analog, wound, not battery. Belt buckles plain. He will wear the same three or four outfits in rotation regardless of resources; this is not poverty but the disinterest of a man whose body's costume is the bow and quiver and everything else is occlusion.

**GIVEN** the costume identity ("Trick Shot").
**EXPECT** it to be worn for paid work and for any encounter staged as theater. The costume change is, for him, *putting on the audience* — it converts a private encounter into a witnessed one. When he wears it to confront Clint, the costume is the message: *we are performing for the crowd I carry in my head*.

**GIVEN** his bow and kit.
**EXPECT** daily inspection — bowstring waxed, limbs checked, arrows fletched and inspected one by one before being returned to the quiver in a specific order. Inspection takes precedence over sleep, food, and almost any social obligation. The kit is laid out in the same arrangement every time he opens the case; a kit reorganized by another hand will be silently restored before use. *(Very high confidence; the prosthetic-self read demands it.)*

**GIVEN** an injury to the right shoulder, draw arm, or eye.
**EXPECT** initial denial, immediate self-rehabilitation regime, refusal of clinical attention until function is publicly threatened. He will work through ranges of motion alone, at night, before mirrors he otherwise avoids. He will not tell a partner or employer. If the injury proves persistent, expect a sharp uptick in irritability, a new willingness to take riskier contracts (proving the body still works), and — if the decline is real and visible — a shift toward the deathbed-style staging: arranging the world so that his decline is interpreted as choice.

---

## F. SLEEP, NIGHTS, SOLITUDE

**GIVEN** a normal night.
**EXPECT** late sleep onset, early waking; total hours often under six. He sleeps lightly, wakes at vehicle sounds and door sounds, reaches for the bedside weapon before he opens his eyes. No partner shares the bed for more than the duration of the act that preceded it; he does not sleep beside other people for long.

**GIVEN** insomnia.
**EXPECT** the dry-draw ritual repeated in the dark — fifteen to fifty pulls of an unstrung or imaginary bow, performed standing, breathing controlled. The somatic loop is his sole sleep aid. He does not read, does not watch much television, does not listen to music for its own sake. The carnival's perpetual noise made silence a luxury he now insists on.

**GIVEN** dreams.
**EXPECT** (inferred) recurrence of two scenes: the embezzlement exposure (the moment the boy saw him) and an undocumented earlier scene of his own subordination to a harder figure. He will not report dreams. If asked, he denies dreaming. The denial is sincere within the limits of his introspective capacity, which are tight.

**GIVEN** true solitude over weeks — no contract, no observer, no protégé.
**EXPECT** decompensation, slow but visible: increased drinking, longer practice sessions oriented toward harder and harder trick shots performed for no one, talking aloud to himself in the pedagogical register, a kind of low-grade depressive flattening that he will not name and will break by manufacturing an encounter — picking a fight, taking a contract, surfacing near Clint. He cannot, for long, be the witness of himself. *(Derived from self-concept-as-audience-dependent; high confidence.)*

---

## G. MONEY

**GIVEN** payment for a contract.
**EXPECT** cash preference, conservative handling — he does not flash, does not spend impressively, does not gamble heavily. Money is held against the next equipment cycle, the next medical need, the next anonymous lodging. He will, however, spend disproportionately on specific high-quality items: a custom-made bow, a piece of optical kit, a particular pair of boots. The pattern is *minimal consumption with peaks at the tools of identity*.

**GIVEN** he is cheated of payment.
**EXPECT** an immediate, technically demonstrative response — not a brawl, a *shot*. Something that says *this is who you tried to short*. He will recover the money or, more often, recover the position; the cash itself is secondary to the established record that he is not to be shorted.

**GIVEN** generosity directed at him — a bought drink, a comped meal, a gift.
**EXPECT** discomfort masked as gruff acknowledgment, followed by a reciprocal gesture calibrated to slightly exceed the original. He will not be in debt, even small, even social. Debt is position lost.

---

## H. SOCIAL POSTURING — STRANGERS, CROWDS, INSTITUTIONS

**GIVEN** a crowd in a public place.
**EXPECT** automatic scan: exits, elevations, persons holding things wrong, sightlines. The scan is unconscious and continuous; it has been running for fifty years. Conversational attention floats over the top of the scan but never replaces it.

**GIVEN** a child approaches him in public.
**EXPECT** stiff, brief courtesy — a nod, a one-line response, no engagement past thirty seconds. He does not perform avuncularity. The exception is a child who shows interest in the bow or a related skill, at which point his attention sharpens predatorily into instruction mode. He does not register this as a shift; it simply happens. Parents present in this scenario should be uneasy without quite knowing why.

**GIVEN** a woman shows romantic or sexual interest.
**EXPECT** transactional engagement at best — brief, physically competent, emotionally absent, followed by exit before morning. He does not date in any sense the word covers. He has no documented sustained partnership; the absence is not accident.

**GIVEN** an authority figure (police officer, federal agent, bureaucrat).
**EXPECT** flat compliance combined with sidelong contempt. He will not antagonize uniforms unless cornered. He will, however, lie reflexively to any institutional questioner — name, business, route — because the institution is, in his cosmology, simply another audience that has not earned the truth.

**GIVEN** a fellow professional with a serious reputation (a known marksman, a known operator).
**EXPECT** a guarded, evaluative warmth — the closest thing in his repertoire to fellow-feeling. He will offer a drink. He will tell one or two of the better stories. He will not ask the other man's personal history and will resent being asked his own. The mutual professional courtesy is the only form of intimacy his structure can sustain without immediately weaponizing.

**GIVEN** that professional later achieves something Buck has not.
**EXPECT** the warmth converts within months to dismissive critique, repeated to third parties, in which the achievement is rederived as luck, gimmick, or the work of someone whose technique he can list flaws in. *(Direct projection of the Clint pattern onto any peer who outpaces him; high confidence.)*

---

## I. THE PROTÉGÉ ECONOMY

**GIVEN** a new student under his direct instruction.
**EXPECT** the following timed phases:
- *Days 1–14*: technical austerity, no praise, demands for repetition until form is correct. The student is tested for tolerance of withholding.
- *Weeks 3–8*: the first scarce praise issued, usually offhand, in earshot of a third party rather than to the student directly. Bond installed.
- *Months 2–6*: increasing private time, increasing personal anecdote (always of his own competence), and the assignment of small loyalties — errands, secrecies, watchings. The student is now being installed as confederate.
- *Months 6+*: the student is invited into Buck's sense of *us-against-them*. Any independent moral judgment by the student in this period reads to Buck as betrayal-in-formation and will trigger pre-emptive coldness.

**GIVEN** the student eventually expresses a values-based disagreement (a refusal of a job, an objection to a method).
**EXPECT** punitive withdrawal within hours and, if the disagreement is exposed publicly, escalation toward physical correction. He will frame this — sincerely, within the constraints of his cognitive style — as the student's failure of loyalty. He cannot perceive his own contribution. This is the Clint loop. He will run it again, on anyone he installs as protégé, until the body stops him.

---

## J. ILLNESS, DOCTORS, MORTALITY

**GIVEN** a symptom that he cannot ignore (blood, sustained pain, vision change).
**EXPECT** delay of medical consultation by weeks beyond the threshold a calibrated person would observe. When he finally goes, he will go to a clinic at distance from his current operating area, under a false name, pay cash, and listen to the diagnosis in silence. He will not tell anyone. He will research treatment via inquiry to specialists under further aliases, evaluate the data tactically, and choose interventions on the basis of which preserve function longest, not which extend life longest.

**GIVEN** terminal prognosis confirmed.
**EXPECT** (and the canon's late-era arc bears this out) reorganization toward a staged exit. Not suicide — suicide is surrender. Rather: arrangement of circumstance such that his death is *performed*, witnessed, and choreographed by his hand even as another hand executes it. The protégé is the necessary instrument; the audience is the implicit one of all the protégés before. The deathbed summons is not departure from his personality; it is its purest expression.

**GIVEN** anyone offers him hospice, comfort, repair, or apology in this period.
**EXPECT** rejection in the contemptuous register, and a probable acceleration of the staged exit to outrun the offer. Tenderness directed at him at the end is the one thing his organization most cannot metabolize. He will leave the room or end the conversation. The cruelty in this period sharpens, does not soften.

---

## K. SMALL TELLS — THE MICRO-PATTERNS A SURVEILLANCE FILE WOULD CATALOG

- *Hands*: when idle, the right hand rests in a partial draw shape against the thigh — fingers curled as if around a string. Unconscious. He will not see it pointed out.
- *Eye blink rate*: low, particularly when sighting any object across a room. He measures distances continuously, unbidden — across a diner, the windows, the parking lot, the next car over. Distance estimation is his idle thought.
- *Posture*: square-shouldered, weight slightly back on the heels, head held level. He does not lean. Leaning is for men who need surfaces.
- *Walk*: even-paced, slightly heel-first, scanning. He does not hurry, even when he should. Hurrying is being shown to be late, which is being shown to have failed schedule, which is position lost.
- *Laugh*: short, single exhalation through the nose. Rare. Tends to precede a cutting line.
- *Greeting touch*: a one-pump handshake, dry, calibrated firm. No embraces. A hand on the shoulder of a student during instruction, removed the instant the correction is made.
- *Closing a door*: with the latch, never the slam — the slam is loss of control made audible, and he will not give that signal.
- *Phone, when he carries one*: kept face-down on the table. Calls answered on the second ring, not the first. Texts answered in bursts during scheduled downtime, never spontaneously.
- *Reading material if present*: shooting magazines, equipment catalogues, the occasional Western paperback. No memoirs, no philosophy, no current events beyond what the bartender's television offers.
- *Music if any*: country of the older generation, kept low. He will turn it off the moment another person enters the room — music heard with him is intimacy, and he does not grant it.
- *Driving*: a single vehicle held a long time, maintained obsessively, replaced only on mechanical necessity. Speed: a steady five over the limit, never enough to be pulled, never slow enough to be remembered.
- *Routes*: varied between any two recurring points. He does not take the same road twice in a week to the same destination if he can avoid it. The variation is automatic, not deliberated.
- *Tipping pattern*: 12–15% at counters where he was unseen, 18–20% at counters where the server addressed him as *sir* without irony. The differential is the price he pays for recognition.

---

## L. OPERATIONAL LOW-TEMPO BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** he is between contracts.
**EXPECT** geographic drift — short-term lodgings in second-tier cities, mid-sized towns, rural waypoints, oriented around shooting ranges and the few remaining venues that will host an old marksman willing to perform for a small house. He gravitates back to the carnival-circuit corridors of his youth. The pull is involuntary.

**GIVEN** he is offered a contract.
**EXPECT** evaluation against four criteria, in order: target difficulty (skill challenge), payment, audience for the work (will it be witnessed and credited?), and only fourth, target identity. He will not refuse a job on moral grounds; he will refuse on insult grounds, if the price implies he is cheap, or on practical grounds, if the geometry is unwinnable.

**GIVEN** the contract pits him against a former student or a peer he once trained beside.
**EXPECT** acceptance with a private gratification he will not name. The opportunity to shoot against the protégé is the structural reward he is, at all times, half-seeking. The contract is the legitimating frame.

**GIVEN** a contract that he completes successfully but without witness.
**EXPECT** quiet dissatisfaction, manifesting over the following days as a longer practice session, sharper drinking, a tendency to drift through towns where someone might recognize him. The shot that no one saw does not entirely count.

**GIVEN** a contract that he fails — target escapes, mission aborted.
**EXPECT** equipment-and-conditions narrative constructed within the hour, never internalized as personal failure, but compensated for by the next contract being riskier and more publicly staged. The miss requires an overwriting hit, the way the dry-fire ritual requires immediate second-shot correction. Pattern fractal: the same loop at all scales.

---

## M. THE COMPULSIVE RETURN

**GIVEN** any extended period — eighteen months, two years — without contact with Clint Barton.
**EXPECT** Buck to engineer proximity. The mechanism: a contract in Clint's operating region, a public demonstration in a city Clint frequents, a recruitment of a known associate, a leaked rumor of his presence. He will not call. He will arrange. The arrangement will be framed to himself as professional opportunism. The arrangement is, in fact, the symptom. *(Highest confidence prediction in this


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

**File segment:** UATU/BB-TS/PM-II
**Scope:** High-stakes behavioral forecasting. Decompensation thresholds. Wound-contact responses. Terminal-phase escalation curves.
**Method note:** Predictions are stated as GIVEN → EXPECT, with confidence bands (HIGH / MOD / SPEC) and observable tells. Each is anchored to the canonical behavioral record summarized in §§1–5; inferences extend the documented pattern into adjacent stimulus conditions a surveillance file would need to anticipate.

---

## A. THE WOUND, NAMED PRECISELY

Before forecasting, the file must specify what *the* wound actually is, because every prediction below routes through it.

The wound is not the embezzlement, not the beating, not the abandonment, not the cancer. The wound is **the moment of being seen accurately by a subordinate** — the instant Clint Barton's eyes registered "you are a thief," and Bernard Barton experienced, for what may be the only time in his adult life, *involuntary visibility from below*. Every subsequent act across forty years of intermittent contact is an attempt to re-establish the proper direction of gaze: the master looked at, the pupil looking up. The beating was not punishment for disloyalty; it was an attempt to physically reverse a visual transaction. He is still attempting that reversal. He will die attempting it.

All wound-contact predictions follow from this one structural fact: **anything that re-instantiates the geometry of "subordinate sees master in moral failure" produces immediate, calibrated, controlled violence followed by narrative reframing.** Anything that threatens to *forgive* him without first restoring the hierarchy produces an even worse response, because forgiveness from below presumes the right to forgive, which presumes equality, which is the prior insult.

---

## B. CRISIS — ACUTE SITUATIONAL STRESSORS

### B.1 — Tactical/Combat Crises

**GIVEN:** Active firefight, outnumbered, conventional cover-and-engage scenario.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Composure unaltered. Heart rate elevation modest (estimate 90–110 bpm at peak engagement based on observed draw-cadence in WCA-era depictions). Shot selection becomes *more* economical, not less — under acute threat his decision tree shortens to the practiced root. He will engage from elevation when offered, will refuse close-quarters unless cornered, will favor a single decisive shot over suppressive volume. Reload cadence will be metronomic; quiver discipline absolute. He does not shout in combat. He does not curse missed shots; he simply takes the second.
**Tell:** A small exhale through the nose between releases — not breath control technique, an autonomic discharge. Operators in proximity have time to mark it; it precedes the next loosed arrow by approximately 0.4–0.7 seconds.

**GIVEN:** Tactical surprise — taken by ambush, position compromised before he sights the threat.
**EXPECT (MOD–HIGH):** Brief micro-freeze (estimate <300 ms) followed by lateral movement to break line of sight, then aggressive re-establishment of *his* visual angle on the attacker. He cannot tolerate being the object of an unseen gaze; recovery of optical dominance is prioritized over hard cover. This is an exploitable bias.
**Tell:** He will move toward angles that give him sight before he moves toward angles that give him safety. A handler reading the room can predict his next two positions from his eyeline alone.

**GIVEN:** Equipment failure mid-engagement (string break, fouled draw, bow damage).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** No verbal reaction. Immediate transition to backup — knife, sidearm, environmental improvisation. But: the *post-engagement* affect will be disproportionate. Equipment failure is a body failure by proxy; he will spend hours afterward in silent maintenance and will not speak unless addressed. Confidants (if any existed) would learn never to remark on it.
**Tell:** Within 90 minutes of incident he is somewhere alone with the failed equipment, examining it with a focus that exceeds the diagnostic need.

### B.2 — Capture and Custody

**GIVEN:** Apprehended, restrained, processed into custody.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Total compliance at the physical level. No theatrical resistance. He will not speak beyond name. He will not request counsel until counsel becomes a tool. He sits well — back straight, hands composed, eyes level with the interrogator's eyes (never down, never aggressively up). He will eat what is offered, sleep when permitted, and read his captors with the same attentional discipline he brings to a target.
**EXPECT (MOD):** Within 48–72 hours he will have identified the weakest staff member on his rotation and will have begun, in the most minimal possible increments, the work of being looked up to by that person. Not flirtation, not recruitment — *posture*. He cannot live in a setting where no one beneath him exists; he will manufacture the hierarchy.
**Tell:** The same guard begins to linger at his cell. He has said almost nothing to that guard. He has, however, allowed himself to be observed performing some small act of self-discipline (a perfect set of push-ups, a precisely folded blanket) within the guard's sightline.

**GIVEN:** Interrogation, accusatory frame, evidence presented of past crimes.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** He will not deny. He will not confess. He will reframe — not to the interrogator's satisfaction, to his own. "That wasn't theft; the carnival took more from me than I ever took from it." The reframing will be delivered without heat, as if reading the weather. He genuinely believes it. This is not a lawyer's evasion; it is the architecture of his cognition rendered audible.
**Tell:** The pronoun shift. Active voice for his skills, passive voice for his crimes ("things happened," "the money went," "the boy got hurt").

### B.3 — Bodily Compromise

**GIVEN:** Injury to draw arm, shoulder, or dominant eye — even minor, even temporary.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Immediate behavioral occlusion of the injury from any observer. He will not favor the limb in public. Privately, the rehabilitation work will be obsessive and isolated.
**EXPECT (MOD):** Increase in aggression toward subordinates / contracting parties during recovery window. The somatic threat must be discharged somewhere; it discharges as contempt.
**Tell:** The micro-resetting of his stance — he will redistribute weight off the affected side in standing positions where he believes himself unobserved, and will catch himself and correct when re-entering view.

**GIVEN:** Diagnosis of degenerative condition affecting motor precision (e.g., the documented terminal cancer phase, or any tremor, vision decline, neuropathy).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Within hours of diagnosis: cold calculation of remaining functional window. Within days: identification of the *staging* he requires for his exit. Within weeks: outreach — not to family, not to peers, **to Clint**. The outreach will be framed instrumentally (a job, a debt, a successor question) because direct affiliative request is forbidden by his structure.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** No depressive withdrawal. No grief work. No religious turn. No reconciliation impulses with anyone other than the protégé, and the reconciliation language with Clint will be a wrapper around a coercive demand.
**Tell:** He cleans things. Quarters spotless. Equipment laid out as for inspection. A man composing his own crime scene in advance.

---

## C. BETRAYAL — THE LOAD-BEARING STIMULUS

Betrayal is the master key. He has organized four decades around a single betrayal narrative in which he is the wronged party. New betrayals (real or perceived) do not produce new responses; they produce repetitions of the original response, calibrated to context.

### C.1 — Being Exposed (the original wound conditions)

**GIVEN:** A subordinate, pupil, or junior associate publicly reveals a moral or competence failure on his part.
**EXPECT (HIGH, near-certain):** Three-phase response, observable within a single 24-hour window.
1. **Phase 1 — Cold containment (minutes to hours):** No outburst. Voice drops in volume, vocabulary narrows, eye contact intensifies on the exposer. The exposed information itself is not addressed; the exposer is studied.
2. **Phase 2 — Calibrated violence (hours to days):** Punitive action delivered at a level meant to dominate, not destroy. Beating, professional sabotage, public counter-accusation. Critically: the punishment is proportional to the *audience* of the exposure, not to the content. A private accusation receives a private rebuke; a witnessed one receives a witnessed beating. He is correcting the visual record.
3. **Phase 3 — Narrative reframing (days to permanent):** The exposer becomes, in his account, the betrayer. This account hardens within 72 hours and never revises. Forty years later it will be word-for-word the same.
**Tell across all three phases:** He does not raise his voice in any of them. The man who beats a child for naming his theft does so quietly. Volume is for the carnival.

**GIVEN:** Exposure by an *equal* (a peer, e.g., Swordsman-class confederate) rather than a subordinate.
**EXPECT (MOD):** Phases 1 and 3 occur; Phase 2 is replaced by withdrawal of cooperation and lateral undermining. He will not strike an equal. He will outlast them.

**GIVEN:** Exposure by a *superior* (employer, syndicate principal).
**EXPECT (MOD):** Theatrical defiance. He will not survive long-term in subordinate hierarchies because his structure cannot metabolize the existence of a true superior; under pressure he will provoke the break himself, framing his dismissal as his choice.

### C.2 — Being Forgiven (the wound's exact inverse)

**GIVEN:** Clint Barton, or any former pupil, offers reconciliation, apology, or expression of forgiveness.
**EXPECT (HIGH, every documented instance):** Renewed cruelty. The offer of forgiveness instantiates the very hierarchy he cannot tolerate — to be forgiven is to be judged, and judgment is the prerogative of position. He responds by re-asserting position via attack. This is counter-intuitive to anyone running an empathic playbook on him and must be flagged in any operational planning.
**Tell:** A subtle smile when the reconciliation language begins. It is not warmth. It is the recognition that the appellant has just handed him the lever.

**GIVEN:** Reconciliation offered with the explicit prior acknowledgment of his mastery ("you taught me everything I know, and—").
**EXPECT (MOD):** Brief softening at the acknowledgment, hardening at the "and." The window for affiliative contact, if it exists at all, is approximately one sentence wide and closes the instant the speaker conditions their regard on his behavior.

### C.3 — Being Surpassed

**GIVEN:** Clint Barton (or any successor archer) demonstrably out-performs him in a witnessed feat.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Decompensation. This is, beside terminal diagnosis, the single most reliable destabilizer in his repertoire. The witnessed loss of mastery collapses the self-concept's load-bearing column.
**Behavioral sequence:**
- Immediate: face stills, mouth tightens, no comment.
- Within hours: withdrawal from the scene, no congratulation offered.
- Within days: a re-engagement designed to re-establish dominance on different terms (a more difficult shot, a trick shot proper, a context that disadvantages the rival).
- If re-establishment fails: targeted attack on the rival, increasingly indifferent to consequence.
**Tell:** He will not look at the bow of the man who beat him. He will look at the *face* of every witness in turn, cataloguing who saw.

**GIVEN:** A protégé/successor surpasses him *and* attributes the surpassing to their own work rather than his teaching.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** This is the maximally destabilizing condition. The narcissistic extension is severed in the same gesture that severs the mastery claim. Expect immediate, sustained, lethal-intent action against the successor. The deathbed-summons pattern is the late-life sublimation of this drive; healthy and armed, the response is direct.

### C.4 — Being Disregarded

**GIVEN:** He is ignored — not opposed, not addressed, simply unseen by a former pupil or audience he expected to register him.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** This wounds more than opposition. Opposition acknowledges him; disregard erases him. He will engineer a situation that forces address — an unmissable provocation, often a public act of skill or violence that cannot be unseen.
**Tell:** The provocations have a performative cleanness — they are constructed to be witnessed, not merely to harm. The body found in a posture; the shot placed where photographers can document; the demonstration timed for the protégé's arrival.

---

## D. TEMPTATION — WHAT HE WILL AND WILL NOT TAKE

He is not significantly tempted by money beyond operational sufficiency; not by sex (notably absent from the entire record, which is itself a datum); not by drugs beyond probable functional drinking; not by ideology of any kind.

**He is tempted by:**

### D.1 — A Worthy Pupil

**GIVEN:** Presentation of a young, gifted, deferential potential successor.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Engagement, even at significant operational cost. He will take the contract that puts the pupil in his orbit; he will travel to assess; he will offer instruction before payment is discussed. The instinct to make another in his image is the closest thing in his repertoire to a passion.
**Caveat:** The pupil must be *gifted* and *deferential* in that order. Mere deference produces contempt; mere gift produces threat. The narrow band — high talent, posture-of-the-student — is the seduction.
**Tell:** He shows up early. For nothing else in the file does he show up early.

### D.2 — A Restaging of the Wound

**GIVEN:** An operational scenario that allows him to re-enact the original betrayal sequence with himself in the master's seat and a new actor as the betraying pupil — to win the scene this time.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** He will accept under-priced, under-resourced, even strategically foolish contracts that put this dynamic in play. The compulsion to repeat the scene is the strongest behavioral driver in the file outside of self-preservation, and at terminal phase it overrides self-preservation.
**Tell:** He selects targets that resemble Clint in age, build, or skill profile when alternatives are available. A surveillance officer should track the morphology of his contracts; the visual rhyme is the giveaway.

### D.3 — An Audience

**GIVEN:** A scenario that promises witness — a public job, a recorded confrontation, a performance before peers.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Greater willingness to engage; reduced bargaining over fee; increased risk tolerance. He is a carnival man. The crowd was always part of the contract. Even an audience of one, if the one is the right one, suffices.

**He is NOT tempted by:**
- Money beyond competence-display thresholds.
- Power positions that require sustained subordination to a superior.
- Romance, family-reconstruction offers, communal belonging.
- Mercy framed as gift to him.
- Legacy framed as institutional (a school, a foundation, a name on a wall). His legacy must be a *person*, looking the right direction.

---

## E. THE TOUCHED WOUND — CONTACT SCENARIOS

This section enumerates the specific stimulus patterns that contact the central wound, with predicted response gradient.

### E.1 — Direct Verbal Contact

**GIVEN:** Someone names the embezzlement aloud, in his presence, accurately.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Phase-1 cold containment. The speaker is studied. If the speaker has no audience, the matter may be deflected verbally and stored for later action. If the speaker has an audience, calibrated violence follows within the operational window the audience permits.
**Variant:** If the speaker is Clint, the response is amplified — the original exposer reactivating the original exposure is the most charged stimulus available short of being out-shot by him.

**GIVEN:** Someone names the *beating of the child* aloud.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Counterintuitively, this lands less hard than naming the theft. The beating, in his cognition, was justified discipline; he does not experience it as moral failure. He will respond to its naming with bored dismissal or a re-framing about discipline and ingratitude. **The theft is the wound; the violence is the response to the wound.** Operators must not confuse the two.

### E.2 — Symbolic Contact

**GIVEN:** Presence of carnival imagery, particularly Carson-affiliated, in his sightline during a vulnerable moment (illness, post-failure, intoxication).
**EXPECT (MOD):** Brief flat affect; topic-change; potential later seeking-out of solitary engagement with the imagery (a returned visit to a carnival ground, a request for a particular kind of food, a half-completed sentence about a name he hasn't said in years).
**Tell:** The only sentimentality in his record routes through the carnival object. It is the closest he comes to grief.

**GIVEN:** Presence of the original bow, or its equivalent training equipment, in a context that frames it as artifact rather than tool.
**EXPECT (MOD):** Discomfort. He will pick it up, handle it, and either re-functionalize it (string it, shoot with it) or remove it from view. He cannot tolerate his instruments being seen as historical; that frames him as historical.

### E.3 — Relational Contact

**GIVEN:** Forced proximity to Clint Barton in a non-combative setting — a hospital room, a stalled vehicle, a long wait.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Behavioral discipline holds at the level of action; speech becomes either minimal or didactic. He will revert to instruction — commenting on Clint's stance, equipment, recent shots — because instruction is the only register in which he knows how to address this person. The teaching is the language he has for love.
**Tell:** If Clint allows the instruction, his face softens microscopically. If Clint rejects the instruction, the softening collapses to contempt within seconds. The window between these two states is the entire emotional range he has available for his most important relationship.

**GIVEN:** Forced proximity to Barney Barton (the brother), in any setting.
**EXPECT (LOW-MOD intensity, HIGH avoidance):** Barney was not the chosen extension; Barney does not carry the wound. He will be cordial and distant. Operationally Barney represents a road not taken in his pedagogy and is therefore a minor narcissistic irritant but not a destabilizer.

**GIVEN:** Presence of Jacques Duquesne (the Swordsman) or his memory invoked.
**EXPECT (MOD):** Confederate frame holds — affectionate disdain, the bond of two thieves. He speaks of him as one speaks of a brother who disappointed in expected ways. This is, oddly, the healthiest relational register available to him; an interviewer seeking to relax him should route through Duquesne.

### E.4 — Mortality Contact

**GIVEN:** Confrontation with his terminal condition by a medical professional who uses standard hospice language (comfort, acceptance, time with loved ones).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Silent contempt. He will not argue; he will simply not use the framework. He will switch providers if able.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** He will refuse palliative sedation past the threshold where it would compromise his hand. He intends to die with the hand working.

**GIVEN:** Confrontation with his terminal condition by Clint.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** The deathbed scene long since prepared. Coercive intimacy: a final demand framed as a final gift. Possible variants: insistence that Clint kill him; insistence that Clint train the successor; insistence that Clint acknowledge mastery before the end. All are versions of the same demand — *re-establish the geometry of gaze before I close my eyes*.
**Tell:** The room will be staged. He will have chosen the lighting, the seat angles, the placement of his bow. The mise-en-scène is the message.

---

## F. DECOMPENSATION CURVE — TERMINAL PHASE FORECAST

The file's most consequential prediction is the shape of his ending, because his ending is where his pathology achieves its purest expression.

**Stage 1 — Diagnosis to ~75% functional capacity (months).**
Behavior largely unchanged. Increased operational tempo — he takes more contracts, executes with elevated precision, *increases* his presence in the visible market. The terminal knowledge has not yet been integrated; he is testing whether he can outrun it. Aggression toward subordinates rises modestly.

**Stage 2 — 75% to 50% capacity (weeks to months).**
Contract selectivity collapses inward toward wound-restaging scenarios (§D.2). He will accept work that approximates the original betrayal geometry. The Clint outreach begins here, framed instrumentally. He may attempt to identify or designate a successor. Public skill demonstrations become more frequent and more theatrical — he is laying down evidence for the legacy claim.

**Stage 3 — 50% to 25% capacity (weeks).**
Cruelty surfaces undiluted. The defenses that depended on bodily competence are no longer affordable; affect that has been routed through the bow for sixty years has nowhere to go. He becomes harder to be in the room with. Subordinates who have tolerated him for years will leave. He will not register their leaving as loss — he will register it as their failure of nerve.

**Stage 4 — Final functional window (days to weeks).**
The deathbed scene is constructed. Setting selected, equipment arranged, Clint summoned. He will sustain skill demonstration through severe physical compromise — a final shot, a final lesson, a final ceremony. Pain management refused or titrated to preserve hand function. He is composing the image that survives him.

**Stage 5 — The ending itself.**
**EXPECT (HIGH):** He will attempt to die with the bow in his hand, with Clint in the room, with the geometry of master-and-pupil re-established in some form — even if the form requires Clint's complicity in his death. He will not die in his sleep; he will not die alone if he can prevent it; he will not die surprised. The ending is the last performance. The audience of one is the entire point.

**The single most important prediction in this file:** If Clint Barton refuses the role — refuses to kill him, refuses to accept the successor commission, refuses to acknowledge mastery, refuses to be in the room on his terms — the entire architecture collapses, and Bernard Barton dies in the only state he has spent his life refusing: unwitnessed in his preferred posture. That outcome is the only available form of justice the case admits, and it is also the cruelest possible thing anyone could do to him. Operators and the protégé himself should understand both halves of that sentence before choosing.

---

**End PM-II.**
**See PM-III for low-prob


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON (TRICK SHOT)

Classification: Tier-3 Adversary / Mentor-Class Antagonist
Purpose of this section: a complete inventory of the levers by which Subject can be reached, calmed, redirected, persuaded, provoked, predicted, or destabilized — assembled not for hostile exploitation but so that any party forced into a room with him (operator, family member, hospice worker, or — most often — Clinton F. Barton) can survive the encounter, contain its damage, and, where possible, deflect it.

The principle organizing every lever below: **Subject is a narcissistic structure built around perceived mastery and conditional regard. Every reachable surface of him lies along the gradient between *being recognized as the master* and *being exposed as not*. There are no other handles.**

---

## 1. THE PRIMARY ARCHITECTURE OF VULNERABILITY

Before enumerating individual levers, the file requires a clear map of the *load-bearing* weaknesses, because most tactical errors with Subject come from treating peripheral vulnerabilities as primary.

**1.1 The Witnessed Self.** Subject does not experience himself in solitude; he experiences himself through an imagined or actual audience. This is the carnival residue — four decades of being the man in the spotlight whose body did the impossible while strangers gasped. Remove the audience and you remove approximately sixty percent of his operating self. He becomes quieter, less theatrical, less dangerous in the spectacular register — and, paradoxically, more dangerous in the intimate register, because the audience-self that polices his cruelty into *performance* is gone and what remains is the unmediated contempt.

**1.2 The Skill-as-Self Equation.** Subject = bow. Any threat to the instrument, the eye, the hand, or the comparative ranking of his marksmanship is a threat to existence and will be defended as such. Conversely, this is the only currency in which he can hear criticism; moral reproof is inaudible to him, but a missed shot is a knife to the throat of his identity.

**1.3 The Embezzlement Wound.** The single non-negotiable structural injury in his psychology is the moment Clint exposed the theft. He has reorganized his entire subsequent life around the proposition that *he* was the wronged party in that scene. To touch this wound directly — to name the theft as theft, to him, by name — is to detonate his most violent defenses. To touch it *obliquely* (through a third party, through a proxy, through a ledger left on a table) is to destabilize him without giving him a target.

**1.4 The Conditional-Regard Economy.** Subject knows exactly one model of human relationship: I judge your performance, you earn or lose my regard, the asymmetry stands. Anyone who enters this economy can be predicted with high accuracy. Anyone who refuses to enter it — who simply does not seek his approval — becomes illegible to him and is either escalated against or, occasionally and briefly, respected.

**1.5 The Somatic Clock.** Aging, and now terminal cancer, are extracting from him the only thing he believes himself to be. This is the master variable of late-period behavior. He is, in clinical terms, in a long-form narcissistic collapse that he is managing via escalation. Every late-life act — the deathbed summons, the second-Trick-Shot succession plan, the contracts taken specifically against Clint — is somatic-clock behavior.

---

## 2. HOW TO REACH HIM

"Reach," in this file, means: open a channel by which Subject will receive information rather than reflexively reject it. Subject's perceptual filters are extraordinarily narrow, and the channels are few.

**2.1 The Technical Register.** Speak about the shot, the wind, the draw weight, the release, the brace height, the spine of the arrow. He will listen — genuinely, attentively, without the contemptuous half-smile — to any human being who demonstrates real knowledge in his domain. This is not warmth; it is the only form of human contact his defenses leave open. A handler with even moderate archery literacy can hold his attention for hours where a trained negotiator with zero technical vocabulary will not last ninety seconds.

**2.2 The Hierarchy-of-Masters Register.** Reference, accurately, other marksmen he respects or measures himself against. Howard Hill, Saxton Pope, the lineage of the longbow, the great trick-shot artists of the carnival era (Topperwein, the Ad. Topperweins, Annie Oakley as a touchstone he both reveres and resents as a woman who out-drew the men). He will engage with this conversation because it places him inside a guild where his self-worth is socially ratified.

**2.3 The Apprentice-Frame.** If the speaker can credibly position themselves as someone who wants to *learn* — not from sycophancy, which he detects instantly, but from genuine technical hunger — he opens. This is the cruel residue of his proto-paternal capacity: he genuinely wants to transmit the craft, and that wanting is the closest thing in him to love.

**2.4 The Equal-Confederate Register.** With someone he reads as a peer in the criminal-mercenary trades (his Swordsman-coded slot), he is laconic, transactional, and reachable in the language of jobs, fees, and operational competence. He does not friend; he confederates. But within the confederation he is reliable in his fashion.

**Channels that will NOT reach him:**
- Moral appeal of any register (he hears moralism as the bleating of the unskilled).
- Emotional disclosure (he hears it as weakness and updates his contempt).
- Therapeutic framing (he hears it as effeminate and as an attempt to position him below the speaker).
- Religious or spiritual appeal (he is operationally atheist; his metaphysics is "the shot went in or it didn't").
- Appeal to past tenderness ("we were like family") — this is the single most reliable detonator and must be understood as such.

---

## 3. HOW TO CALM HIM

Calming Subject is rarely the goal — usually the goal is to *survive the next ninety seconds without him discharging at someone*. The following techniques have working evidence in canon or are derivable from his structure.

**3.1 The Skill-Acknowledgment De-escalation.** When his affect is climbing toward violence, a *specific, technical, accurate* acknowledgment of something he has done well will reliably step him down a register. Not "you're the best" (generic praise reads as condescension), but "that was a thirty-yard offhand into a moving target in crosswind — I've seen Olympic recurve shooters miss that." The narrowing into specifics signals that the speaker has been watching with informed eyes, which is the form of attention he metabolizes as nourishment.

**3.2 The Audience-Restoration Move.** If something has just exposed him in front of others, the fastest way to abort an escalation is to *re-stage the moment* in his favor. Hand him an opening to demonstrate, redirect the attention of any present onlookers toward an act of his competence. This is a humiliating move for the handler — it requires participating in the very narcissistic theater that is the problem — but it works.

**3.3 The Task-Pivot.** Give him a marksmanship task. Even small, even arbitrary. He will redirect his unregulated affect into the bow because that is what the bow is *for* in his psyche. A handler in a closed room with a furious Buck Barton, who can manufacture a thrown target or a tossed coin to be shot, has just bought ninety seconds of regulated behavior.

**3.4 Silence and Withdrawal of Stimulus.** Subject does not escalate against a non-responsive surface for long. He requires the friction of a reactive other to maintain the climb. A handler who goes flat — no expression, no rebuttal, no eye-contact challenge, no submission gesture either — frequently causes him to lose interest within two to four minutes. This is the cheapest de-escalation tool in the file and is underused because people in distress find it psychologically expensive.

**3.5 What Will NOT Calm Him.**
- *Apology.* He reads apology as confirmation that he was right to be angry, which licenses further anger.
- *Reasoning.* He does not negotiate with logic; he negotiates with rank.
- *Touch.* Do not touch him under any circumstance during escalation; the body-boundary violation will be answered.
- *Invocation of the past relationship.* See §2 — the most reliable detonator.

---

## 4. HOW TO PERSUADE HIM

Persuasion of Subject is possible within strictly bounded conditions. The conditions:

**4.1 The Proposition Must Be Framed as Mastery-Adjacent.** Any course of action you wish him to take must be presented as the action a master would take. Not the moral action, not the kind action, not the safe action — the *masterful* action. He will refuse a benevolent course framed benevolently and accept the identical course framed as the move only a real professional makes.

**4.2 The Proposition Must Preserve His Standing in His Own Eyes.** No persuasion that requires him to publicly or even privately concede error will succeed. The exit ramp must always permit him to walk away believing he chose the course because of his own judgment, not because of yours. Persuasion of Subject is the art of letting him steal your idea.

**4.3 The Speaker's Standing Determines Bandwidth.** A speaker he respects technically can persuade him to do moderately uncharacteristic things. A speaker he does not respect technically cannot persuade him to do anything at all, regardless of the merit of the argument. This is non-negotiable.

**4.4 Time the Ask to His Somatic State.** Subject's persuadability rises after he has eaten, after he has shot well, and in the morning. It falls in the late afternoon, after alcohol, after a missed shot, after any encounter with a mirror that he held longer than usual (a small but recurring observable: he checks the line of his shoulders and the steadiness of his hands in any reflective surface as he passes; visible dissatisfaction with the check predicts a poor afternoon).

**4.5 The Ledger Approach.** Subject responds to the framing of a transaction. If you can present a request as the discharge of a debt owed to him, or as the establishment of a debt he can later collect, you have constructed a structure he understands and respects. Naked requests for help fail; trades succeed.

---

## 5. HOW TO PROVOKE HIM (and Why You Almost Never Should)

This file is benevolent. Provocation is listed because (a) understanding the triggers protects the well-meaning from accidentally pulling them, and (b) under narrow tactical conditions a controlled provocation may be the lesser evil.

**5.1 The Top-Tier Detonators (will produce immediate violence or its near equivalent):**
- Being out-shot in front of witnesses by a younger or less experienced marksman.
- Naming the embezzlement, by name, as theft, in his hearing.
- Suggesting that Clint Barton's success was achieved *despite* his training rather than because of it.
- Suggesting that any of his pupils, present or past, surpassed him.
- Physical contact with the bow without permission.
- Any reference to the trembling of his hands, the deterioration of his eye, or the cancer.

**5.2 The Mid-Tier Irritants (will produce cold escalation, contempt, eventual withdrawal):**
- Treating him with therapeutic warmth.
- Treating him as old.
- Treating him as ill.
- Calling him "Bernard" rather than "Buck" or "Trick Shot" — the legal name belongs to a self he disavowed.
- Discussion of his childhood or family of origin (he will not engage and the attempt itself diminishes the asker in his eyes).
- The presence of children in the room — they expose his discomfort with non-instrumental relating and he resents being made to feel it.

**5.3 The Slow Burns (cumulative, will surface days later):**
- Being praised for the wrong shot — recognition of a technically easy shot he made looking impressive offends him more than no praise at all.
- Being offered help he did not request.
- Being included in plans as an afterthought.

**5.4 Controlled-Provocation Use Cases.** If the operational goal is to make him disengage and leave a scene rather than continue an action, a calibrated humiliation in the technical register will often cause him to withdraw to reconstitute. He does not flee; he *withdraws to drill*. This buys hours, occasionally days. The cost is a worse encounter later.

---

## 6. HOW TO PREDICT HIM

Subject is, despite his theatricality, one of the more predictable hostile actors in the cross-referenced files. His repertoire is small and his triggers are reliable.

**6.1 Daily Predictables.**
- Practices at dawn and at dusk; these are his sacramental hours and he is unreachable in them. Anyone needing to speak with him should target mid-morning or mid-afternoon between sessions.
- Cleans the bow every evening regardless of use. Cleaning is meditative; he is at his least defended during the cleaning, but he is also alone and a watcher will be noticed.
- Eats little, eats predictable foods, eats alone. Carnival-circuit diet: coffee, eggs, hard bread, cured meat, whiskey at night. Late period: same minus the appetite, plus the cancer medications he is non-compliant with.
- Walks the perimeter of any space he sleeps in before he sleeps in it. Carnival residue; lifetime habit.
- Sits with his back to the wall. Always. The one observed deviation in canon was during a confrontation in which he wanted Clint to *see* he was not afraid, and even then he placed himself with line-of-sight to all exits.

**6.2 Encounter Predictables.**
- First thirty seconds: assessment of the other party's bearing, hands, eyes. He is reading you for marksman-tells. If you have them, he sees them; if you do not, he relaxes a degree.
- Opening utterance is almost always a small barb or test. Receiving it without reaction is the correct response.
- He will produce, within the first three minutes, a reference to a past shot of his — sometimes oblique, sometimes direct. This is territorial scent-marking; receive it neutrally.
- He will refuse the first offered seat and take a different one. Do not interpret as significant.

**6.3 Conflict Predictables.**
