- He will choose distance over closure. He fights at his range, which is long. Anyone closing distance fast disrupts him; he will reset by retreating, not by engaging.
- He will go for incapacitation through pain compliance before lethality, *unless* the encounter has touched the embezzlement wound or the somatic-decline wound. In those cases his violence is lethal-from-the-jump.
- He will narrate during conflict. The narration is not bravado; it is the audience-construction reflex. Use the narration: it tells you his targeting in advance.

**6.4 Long-Arc Predictables.**
- He will return to Clint. Always. The intervals shorten as the somatic clock runs down.
- He will attempt a "legacy" gesture before death. The gesture will be coercive, will involve a successor, and will be staged for maximum effect on Clint specifically.
- He will not die quietly and he will not die in a hospital bed if he can help it. The death will be *arranged*. This is foreknowledge that protective parties should plan around.

---

## 7. HOW TO DESTABILIZE HIM

For containment scenarios in which the operational goal is to render him temporarily incapable of coherent hostile action. None of these are pleasant; all are listed because the alternative — letting him operate at full capacity — is generally worse for everyone in the room, Clint Barton most especially.

**7.1 The Mastery-Eclipse.** Out-shoot him, in front of others, in a discipline he claims. This produces a documented decompensation that lasts hours to days. He becomes quiet, withdrawn, hyper-rehearsed, and dangerous in a slower register. Suitable when the goal is to remove him from an immediate scene; unsuitable when the goal is to keep him contained over a long arc, because the rebuild produces a more lethal version.

**7.2 The Audience Subtraction.** Remove every onlooker. Subject in true solitude loses about half his operational coherence within fifteen minutes. He begins to talk to absent figures, drill at empty space, rehearse old grievances aloud. This is the late-period observable, exacerbated by illness, but the structure was there in younger life as well.

**7.3 The Pupil-Reframe.** Cause him to overhear — never to be told directly, which he will reject — a credible third party describing Clint's skill in terms that do not credit him. This is the single most destabilizing intervention in the inventory and should be reserved for genuinely necessary use. The downstream consequence is escalation against the third party and against Clint, so the intervention must be paired with protective measures for both.

**7.4 The Mirror.** Place him in a situation where he must contend with his own image at length — a long drive at night, a hospital corridor, a hotel room with full-length glass. He has organized his entire life around not seeing himself, and the unmediated reflection of the aging, ill body undoes the audience-self that holds him together.

**7.5 The Inversion.** Offer him care he did not ask for, gently and without acknowledgment of his refusal, repeatedly. This is the only known intervention that has anything like a therapeutic valence; it also reliably produces rage in the short term. Hospice workers attempting it should expect verbal abuse and, in early sessions, thrown objects. Continued application across many sessions produces a softening that he will never name and will deny if named.

---

## 8. SPECIFIC LEVERAGE BY OPERATOR TYPE

**8.1 For Clint Barton.** The protective recommendations are the most important in this file and the most painful. Subject is, for Clint, the wound that will not close, and Clint's reflex is to keep offering the closure that is the very trigger.

- *Do not seek him out.* Every documented reunion has worsened both parties.
- *If summoned, attend with a third party Subject does not know.* The unfamiliar witness disrupts his script.
- *Refuse the legacy.* Whatever object, name, or role he attempts to transmit at the end, refusing receipt is the act that frees you. Acceptance — even gracious acceptance — completes his coercive design.
- *Bring nothing of value.* He will take what you bring, in some register, to confirm his position.
- *Do not apologize for the embezzlement exposure. Ever.* This is the single instruction the file would underline in red. Your apology is the gift he has spent forty years extorting; giving it releases nothing in him and binds you further.
- *Permit yourself the recognition that he loved you in the only currency he had, and that the currency was counterfeit, and that the love was real anyway, and that none of this obligates you to him.* This is the psychological work, and it is yours, and it cannot be done in his presence.

**8.2 For Mercenary Employers.** He is a reliable contractor within a narrow band. Pay on schedule, do not micromanage technique, do not introduce competing marksmen, do not place him under younger team leads. He will execute. He will also, if the contract intersects with Clint Barton, prioritize the Clint vector over the contract terms. Account for it.

**8.3 For Carnival/Performance Colleagues.** Treat him as the elder of the guild. Public deference, private distance. He will not befriend; he will protect the guild's standing, and you, as part of it.

**8.4 For Medical and Hospice Personnel.** Address him by alias, never by legal name. Do not narrate procedures. Do not discuss prognosis in his hearing unless asked, and he will not ask. Expect non-compliance with medication and do not attempt to enforce. The cancer will run its course on his terms; the only humane work available is the slow inversion described in §7.5.

**8.5 For Law Enforcement.** He is honest about his criminal record in a strange way — he will not confess but he will not bother to lie about the past once the present case is established. He treats the criminal-legal apparatus as a confederate-rank institution: rule-bound, predictable, manageable. He will not flee custody if the conditions of custody respect the technical-master framing (i.e., guards who acknowledge his reputation).

---

## 9. THE LEVERS THAT DO NOT EXIST

A file of this kind is incomplete without an explicit list of *non-existent* levers, because operators waste resources reaching for them.

- *There is no romantic lever.* No documented attachment of erotic significance; affect is too constricted; the bow occupies the slot.
- *There is no familial lever beyond Clint.* Whatever family of origin existed has been excised from the self-narrative.
- *There is no greed lever past a working threshold.* He takes money but is not motivated by accumulation; once paid he does not bargain further.
- *There is no ideological lever.* He has no politics, no religion, no cause.
- *There is no fear-of-death lever.* He has integrated mortality on his own terms and is, in fact, organizing his death rather than evading it.
- *There is no shame lever in the moral register.* Shame requires an internalized other; he has none. The closest analog is the *humiliation* lever in the skill register, which is functionally different and is covered above.
- *There is no nostalgia lever.* He does not remember fondly. The past is a ledger of who owes him, not a place of warmth.

---

## 10. SYNTHESIS — THE OPERATIONAL POSTURE

The correct posture toward Bernard Barton, across every operator type and every scenario, reduces to a small number of principles.

Address him by the alias he chose; speak the technical language of his craft if you can and remain silent in it if you cannot; do not enter the conditional-regard economy he will invite you into; do not touch the embezzlement wound; do not touch the somatic-decline wound; do not apologize; do not appeal to affection; do not seek closure he is constitutionally incapable of granting; remove the audience when you can and provide a controlled one when you must; permit him the dignity of his mastery in the moments that require de-escalation and refuse it in the moments that require containment; expect him to return to Clint, plan around it, protect Clint from his own reflex to be returned to; and recognize that the destabilization techniques available are real, are usable, and are almost all things that the people who love or have loved him will find morally costly to deploy.

He is, in the end, a man who taught a boy to put an arrow through a coin at fifty yards and then beat the boy for telling the truth about him, and who has spent the four decades since arranging his life so that the boy must keep coming back to be told it was his own fault. The levers above are the means by which that arrangement can be interrupted, contained, or — at minimum — survived. They are not the means by which it can be healed. Healing was not on offer from him; the file's honesty about that is itself a form of protection for the people who would otherwise spend their lives reaching for a lever that is not there.

— END SECTION —


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE — SUBJECT BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON

*The positive ledger. What this man actually possesses, what he can do, what he has built, and what has kept him upright through six decades of itinerant work, criminal employment, bodily decline, and terminal illness. Catalogued without sentiment: a capability inventory is not an exoneration, and several of the items below are precisely what make him dangerous. They are also what have kept him alive, employable, and — by his own internal metrics — uncowed, into a stage of life when most men in his line of work are long buried or broken.*

---

## 1. PRIMARY MOTOR-PERCEPTUAL CAPABILITIES

### 1.1 Marksmanship — the load-bearing asset

The asset around which every other asset is organized. Trick Shot's archery is documented, across four decades of canon, as functionally peerless among unenhanced humans — the only archer reliably described as Clint Barton's *equal or superior* in pure technical capacity (Hawkeye Vol.1 #1–4; Solo Avengers #1; West Coast Avengers #28; Hawkeye: Blindspot). The skill is not generic; it decomposes into a set of discrete sub-capabilities each of which would be career-making in isolation:

- **Static target precision** at ranges where the arrow's parabolic drop and lateral drift from cross-wind become first-order problems — i.e. beyond fifty yards into the hundred-plus-yard envelope. The "trick shot" repertoire (split-arrow, ricochet, blind-fire-off-reflective-surface, simultaneous multi-target release) is the carnival vocabulary; the *combat* application of the same hand is the dangerous version.
- **Moving-target acquisition** with a draw cycle measured in fractions of a second — the carnival skills (live release of clay, coin, balloon, knife-edge bisection) train precisely the visual-tracking and predictive-release subsystems that combat requires.
- **Trick releases**: behind-the-back, off-the-hip, off the shoulder, two-arrow draw, off-string release, point-blank flat-trajectory work, and the entire repertoire of curve-shots that exploit broadhead asymmetry and fletching torque. The carnival audience trained this branch to a depth most combat archers never reach.
- **Improvised-projectile capacity**: he can functionally shoot anything aerodynamic. Recorded instances of effective release of nails, knitting needles, sharpened dowels, eating utensils. The bow is preferred but not necessary; the *hand* is the weapon.
- **Sustained accuracy under load**: he holds form when shot at, when bleeding, when winded, when humiliated. Combat composure is, in him, indistinguishable from pedagogical composure: the body does not know the difference between a paying crowd and a hostile one.

### 1.2 The eye

The oculomotor system is the substrate. Decades of daily drill have produced unusually preserved visual acuity, depth perception, and saccadic precision deep into late middle age. Subjects with his profile typically present clinically with: above-norm contrast sensitivity in low light (carnival tents, dusk shows); fast vergence; and an unusually durable accommodation curve. Even allowing the inevitable presbyopic decline, his working acuity at the moment of release outperforms most operators twenty years younger. This is a *trained* organ, not merely a gifted one — and trained organs degrade more slowly than gifted ones.

### 1.3 Proprioception and somatic memory

His draw is identical, shot to shot, year to year. This is the deeper capability — not the eye but the *body's* refusal to lose its grooves. Anchor point, stance, breath-hold timing, release: all metronomic. A long-surveillance file would note that his draw cycle, on film from carnival reels in his thirties and on combat footage in his sixties, is recognizably the same draw — the elbow angle, the bow-hand thumb position, the rear-foot weight bias — to within margins finer than most archers achieve within a single session. This is the somatic signature of a man who has practiced past the point where consciousness is required, which means: practiced past the point where stress can disrupt.

### 1.4 Hand-eye-as-pedagogy

Crucially, he can *transmit* the skill. Many great shooters cannot teach; the kinesthetic knowledge is locked in their own bodies. Barton is the rare master who has both the analytic decomposition of his own technique and the patience (within his austere range) to drill another body into it. The proof is Clint Barton, whose capacity is itself extraordinary and is largely attributable to Buck's curriculum. This asset — *the ability to make another archer* — is the one that gives him cross-decade narrative weight and that, in the deathbed sequences, he attempts to deploy a final time. A handler reading this file should note: he can produce a successor on a compressed timeline. He has done it before. He could do it again under coercion.

---

## 2. SECONDARY PHYSICAL AND TACTICAL ASSETS

- **Cardiovascular and muscular durability** consistent with a working performer: the carnival is a touring labor environment, and a sharpshooter who also sets up and breaks down a rig multiple times a week develops a hardiness invisible in the marquee billing. He is not a gym-built physique; he is a labor-built one, which is more durable.
- **Cold tolerance, heat tolerance, noise tolerance**: thirty-plus years on tour in tents conditions a nervous system to perform through climatic and sensory adversity that would degrade a clinic-trained shooter.
- **Edge-weapon competence**, secondary to archery — depicted with throwing knives, hand axes, anything releasable. Trained adjacent to the Swordsman; absorbed the basic vocabulary.
- **Combat composure under direct fire**: documented across the WCA-era engagements. He does not flinch when shot at. The carnival skill — release with audience hands and bodies within feet of the target line — has inoculated him against the proximity-stress that breaks novice combatants.
- **Bow maintenance, arrow-craft, fletching, broadhead modification**: full artisanal competence. He can build his own kit from raw stock. This is an underrated asset: he is logistically self-sufficient in a way few specialists are. Deny him a quartermaster and he simply makes the arrows himself, from materials available in any hardware store and any sporting-goods aisle.
- **Field improvisation**: the carnival teaches contingency. A show must happen even when the rig fails. He has thirty years of experience inventing the next ten minutes when the prepared act collapses. In tactical terms, this is *operational flexibility under equipment failure* — a capability military instructors spend years trying to drill into special-operations recruits.

---

## 3. COGNITIVE AND PERCEPTUAL ASSETS

- **Perceptual-motor pattern recognition** at the elite end. He reads ballistic problems — wind, range, drop, target motion — in a single glance and without conscious calculation. This generalizes partially to other physical-tactical reads: door geometry, crowd vectors, sightlines.
- **Tactical present-focus**: the cognitive narrowness flagged in the psychological section is, in operational terms, an asset. He does not ruminate during action. The same austerity that cripples his interpersonal life makes him a clean executor on contract.
- **Memory for spatial detail**: documented in the late-era arcs — he recalls the layout of the old carnival grounds, individual rigging arrangements, sight-angles from specific tent positions, decades after the fact. The somatic-spatial memory is intact even where autobiographical memory is selective.
- **Pricing and contracting acumen**: he has sustained a mercenary career across multiple decades and employers (Crossfire, freelance, criminal syndicates). This requires a working market sense, a reputation maintained, and an ability to negotiate. He is not a babe in the criminal economy; he reads it.
- **Operational discipline**: he does not drink on the job (carnival-circuit chronic use notwithstanding, the working hand is sober). He does not boast pre-mission. He does not leave loose ends in the form of witnesses he has personally guaranteed. The same conditional-regard internal economy that makes him a poor father makes him a reliable contractor.

---

## 4. RESOURCES, NETWORK, AND INFRASTRUCTURE

- **Carnival-circuit network**: forty-plus years of touring leaves a residue. Old roustabouts, retired performers, sympathetic owners, the small constellation of fairground families across the American Midwest and South. He has couches, barns, stock-trailers, and back-lot storage available to him on a handshake basis from individuals who do not appear in any database. This is a soft-infrastructure asset of considerable value to a man who needs to move and disappear.
- **Carson Carnival institutional memory**: even after the original outfit's decline, the personnel diaspora gives him human assets in dozens of small operations. Bookers, equipment rental, even venue access for staging or laundering.
- **Mercenary employer relationships**: contractually transactional, not affective, but real. Crossfire's organization, low-tier organized-crime fixers, the occasional intelligence cut-out. He is a known quantity in a market that values known quantities.
- **The Swordsman as historical confederate**: lifelong, though Duquesne is dead in current canon. The relationship while it lasted gave him cover, partnership, and a thicker network than a lone shooter would manage. The residue persists in mutual contacts.
- **The protégé as latent asset** (in his cosmology, if not in fact): Clint Barton is, to Buck, an extension of his own competence and reputation. Every Hawkeye headline is, in Buck's reading, partial credit to him. This is delusional in its interpersonal claim but operationally real as a *reputational asset* in the underworld — "the man who taught Hawkeye" is a marketable identity.
- **The alias itself**: *Trick Shot* is a brand. It has equity. It pre-introduces him in any room where it is spoken. He has cultivated it deliberately and curated it across decades. The decision to franchise it (the second Trick Shot, the inheritance gesture) is also asset management — he is preserving the brand past his own body.
- **Equipment cache**: inferred from operational continuity. A man of his habits maintains weapons stores in several locations, almost certainly including at least one off-grid rural site associated with the carnival diaspora.

---

## 5. CHARACTEROLOGICAL RESILIENCE FACTORS

This is the section where the same traits that make him hard to live with also make him hard to break. Catalogued in cold form:

- **High constitutional pain tolerance**, both physical and narcissistic-injurious within his preferred register. Bullet wound, broken hand, terminal diagnosis — none of these produce collapse. He metabolizes pain into task.
- **Affect constriction** as armor. The narrow-band emotional life means he is not destabilized by environments (interrogation, isolation, hostage scenarios) that work primarily through emotional flooding. He cannot be sweated; there is nothing for the sweat to act on.
- **Refusal of helplessness**. Across every documented adversity — exposure, ostracism, illness, age — his response is to *act*, even where action is maladaptive. This is a poor strategy for repair but an excellent strategy for survival in adversarial environments.
- **Self-narrative integrity**. He has a story about himself (master, betrayed, vindicated by craft) that does not require external validation to maintain. Most subjects with this much loaded biography are vulnerable through the self-narrative; he is not. The narrative is closed-system.
- **Long-horizon patience**. He waited *decades* on the Clint reckoning. He can wait. Most violent men cannot; they discharge in months. He banks grievance and disburses it at chosen moments.
- **Identity-skill fusion** — usually treated as a vulnerability and rightly so, but on the ledger it has a positive face: it gives him a daily ritual reason to maintain his body, his eye, and his bow into ages when most men have softened. The discipline that the identity demands has kept the body intact.
- **Tolerance for solitude**. The carnival life is gregarious in performance and solitary in rig-down. He is comfortable alone for long stretches. He does not crave company; he can sit a stake-out, a surveillance, a recovery, indefinitely.
- **Functional sobriety under task**. Whatever the off-duty alcohol baseline, the working hand is clean. This is a discipline asset most operators in his bracket do not maintain past forty.
- **Ego-syntonic worldview**. He is not in conflict with himself. Internal conflict is the engine of most psychological breakdown; he runs without it. The cost is moral; the operational benefit is enormous resilience.

---

## 6. THE TERMINAL-PHASE ASSETS

A note specific to the late-era cancer arc, because the file would be incomplete without it. Terminal illness, in this subject, does not deplete the ledger; it concentrates it:

- **Loss of survival-anchor as tactical liberation**. He has nothing left to protect. The handler must understand: a man with no future is not a man with diminished capacity. He has *full capacity* and *zero deterrence*. Everything in section 1 above is still operational, and the consequences-fear that constrains comparable operators has been excised.
- **Compressed-timeline planning competence**. The deathbed summons is, whatever else it is, an executed operation: he located Clint, drew him in, staged the encounter, prepared the successor question. This is logistical competence on a body that should be in palliative care.
- **Final-act discipline**. He does not flail. He does not seek comfort. He maintains the operational posture into the last days. The pathology and the asset are the same fact: he will not break character.

---

## 7. WHAT MAKES THE ASSETS DURABLE

The closing diagnostic. The reason this ledger is as long as it is, for a man of no enhancement and no resources of consequence, is the *integration* of the assets. They are not a list of separable capabilities; they are a single closed loop. The carnival made the eye; the eye made the bow-hand; the bow-hand made the reputation; the reputation made the network; the network made the contracts; the contracts maintained the skill; the skill maintained the identity; the identity demanded the daily practice that preserved the eye. The loop has run, without external input, for over forty years.

That is the resilience signature. Not toughness, not luck, not allies — *closure of the loop*. Bernard Barton is a self-sustaining system whose only required input is a target and whose only required output is the arrow's flight. As long as those two terminals are available to him, the system runs. Cancer will close it. Almost nothing else will.

The handler should plan accordingly: this is not a subject who can be *worn down*. He can only be out-shot, out-staged, or outlived.

— END SECTION —


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION

## Subject: Bernard "Buck" Barton (Trick Shot)
### Section 11 of the UATU Longitudinal File

---

## 11.0 Framing

A subject whose entire psychic economy is balanced on a single perceptual-motor skill and a single defense (blame externalization) does not "break" the way a borderline or depressive subject breaks. He does not flood. He does not dissolve. He does not retreat. He **calcifies, then theatricalizes, then weaponizes the theatre**. His decompensation is, in technical terms, a *narcissistic terminal arc*: each stage narrows the field of self-validation, and each narrowing produces a more grandiose and more lethal compensatory display. The pattern is staircase, not slope.

What follows is the staircase, riser by riser, with the somatic, behavioral, and interpersonal tells that mark each tread — derived from the full canonical record (Hawkeye Vol.1 #1–4, Solo Avengers #1–4, West Coast Avengers run, the Crossfire/Mockingbird arc, Hawkeye: Blindspot, and the terminal-illness summons sequence).

---

## 11.1 Baseline (Compensated State)

Before any description of failure, note what *function* looks like for this subject — because his "well" is already most people's pathology, and the diagnostic signal is not the presence of cruelty but the **organization** of it.

In compensated state:
- He is **economical**. Speech is clipped; movement is conservative; the body is held in the loose readiness of a man who has spent forty years not wasting a draw.
- He **performs willingly** in front of a known audience and refuses to perform in front of an unknown one — the carnival distinction between *the mark* (whom you dazzle) and *the rube* (whom you do not waste shots on). He calibrates the audience before he calibrates the shot.
- He **teaches**. Compensated Buck has a student or is looking for one. Without a student-shaped object in his field, the personality begins to slip almost immediately. The protégé is not a luxury; it is structural ballast.
- He **drinks moderately** in this state. Carnival-grade whiskey, paced. The increase in intake is one of the earliest tells of slip.
- He **does not speak of Clint** unless prompted, and when prompted, the cadence is dismissive and the eyes go fractionally elsewhere — the classic micro-expression of a wound treated as a triviality.

Hold this baseline. Every later stage is a recognizable distortion of these five surfaces.

---

## 11.2 Stage One — Status Abrasion (the Itch)

**Triggers, in order of potency:**
1. Being publicly out-shot by a younger marksman, especially a former student.
2. A skill task he cannot complete on the first attempt in front of any witness.
3. Hearing Clint Barton named, in his presence, as *the* archer — not *an* archer, not *a* good one, *the* one. The definite article is the blade.
4. Being addressed familiarly by a peer who has surpassed him commercially (a higher-paid contract, a better job).
5. Bodily evidence of decline: a tremor in the off-hand on cold mornings, a delayed focus pull at distance, the first time a target shows him diplopia under stress.

**Presentation:**
- Verbal compression. He talks less, not more. Sentences truncate; the carnival-barker register, which surfaces in him under good conditions, vanishes.
- **Increased pre-shot ritual.** Where he normally draws once, holds, releases, he now adds a small breath cycle, a finger-flex of the draw hand, a roll of the right shoulder. Each ritual element is a hairline crack in the automaticity of the skill. Track these additions: every new pre-shot mannerism is one stage further from baseline.
- He cleans equipment more often, and more visibly. The bow becomes a stage prop in private; the maintenance is theatre to himself.
- Drinking creeps from evening to afternoon. The pour gets longer; the glass gets shorter.
- A first, brief, **self-justifying monologue** — usually to a confederate, never to a stranger — in which the embezzlement-and-Clint story is rehearsed with a new piece of evidence added. He is updating the brief in his own head. This is diagnostic: the story is being **re-armored** because the underlying defense is being stressed.

He is still safe to be in a room with at this stage. He is not yet dangerous; he is itchy.

---

## 11.3 Stage Two — Mobilization (the Reach Back)

The itch becomes an action. The reliable behavioral marker is **the protégé reach** — he initiates contact with someone from his past, almost always Clint or a Clint-substitute, under cover of a non-emotional pretext. A job. A warning. An "I heard you were in town." The pretext is always thin and always operational; he does not know how to construct a personal pretext because he has never had a personal life that was not operational.

**Presentation:**
- **Travel.** He moves. The compensated Buck is sedentary by preference; the mobilizing Buck takes trains, buses, cheap flights, and shows up. The motion itself is a tell; track movement and you track the slip.
- **The accepting of contracts he would previously have refused** — specifically, contracts that put him in proximity to Clint, or to symbolically Clint-adjacent figures (other Avengers, other archers, Carson Carnival alumni). He will undercut his own rate to take such a contract. Money is no longer the variable; positioning is.
- **A return to the carnival argot** in his speech. Under stress he reverts linguistically. "Mark," "rube," "the joint," "the lot" reappear. This is regressive; he is reaching for the period of life in which he was most assured.
- A noticeable **uptick in physical grooming** before the encounter — clean shave, pressed shirt, the boots done. The man who does not care what others think cares enormously what *this one other* thinks. The grooming is for the protégé's eye, though he could not under torture admit it.
- A small, almost charming, sentimentality with strangers — bartenders, hotel clerks — in the 24–48 hours before the confrontation. The affect that cannot be discharged at the right target leaks at incidental ones. This is the only window in his life when he is observably warm, and the warmth is a symptom.

By the close of this stage he is in the same city as the object. The confrontation is now a question of *when*, not *whether*.

---

## 11.4 Stage Three — Confrontation and the Refraction of Blame

This is the canonical scene, repeated across decades: he stands across from Clint (or the substitute), bow in hand or holstered, and **delivers the brief**. The brief is always the same in structure and always different in surface detail:

1. Acknowledgment of the protégé's growth (delivered as faint praise, a compliment that audits).
2. A specific technical critique — a flaw the protégé has, that only Buck would have seen. This is the assertion of continued mastery and continued ownership.
3. The grievance, reframed. The theft becomes the betrayal; his abandonment becomes the protégé's expulsion of him. **The pronouns are always inverted from reality**: *you* did this to *me*. Track pronoun direction in any conversation with the subject; the reversal is the engine.
4. The proposition — a job, a duel, an inheritance demand. The proposition is the operational cover for the emotional event he cannot name.

**Decompensation tells within the confrontation:**
- If the protégé accepts the technical critique, Buck stabilizes — briefly. The hierarchy is restored.
- If the protégé refuses the critique, Buck escalates *not* by argument but by demonstration. He will shoot something. The shot is the rebuttal.
- If the protégé offers reconciliation — apology, embrace, the words "I forgave you years ago" — Buck **destabilizes catastrophically**. This is counterintuitive and operationally critical: the reconciliation offer is the single most dangerous stimulus you can present to him. It is registered as the protégé asserting moral seniority, which is the precise narcissistic injury his entire architecture is designed to refuse. The response is cold rage, calibrated violence, and a hardening of the brief. **Reconciliation is the accelerant, not the solvent.**
- If the protégé out-shoots him in this scene, the composure crack is visible in three specific places: a momentary fixity of the jaw, a single hard blink (the eye that has betrayed him), and a withdrawal of the bow hand to the hip — the gunfighter's tell, despite his never having been a gunfighter. He has nothing to do with the hand and so it goes to where authority is supposed to live.

---

## 11.5 Stage Four — Iteration (the Compulsive Return)

When the confrontation does not resolve the underlying injury — and it cannot, because the injury is structural, not situational — he returns. The pattern across canon shows return cycles of progressively shortening intervals: years between early contracts, months by the West Coast Avengers period, weeks by Blindspot, days by the terminal arc.

**Behavioral signature of iteration:**
- Each return is **scripted with greater specificity**. He arrives knowing what he will say, having rehearsed. The improvisation of the early returns gives way to a near-liturgical repetition.
- He begins **collecting evidence of the protégé's life** between encounters — newspaper clippings, mission rumors, a folder somewhere. The surveillance is not for operational targeting; it is for the rehearsal. He needs material for the brief.
- He **acquires intermediaries** — younger marksmen, criminal employers, mutual carnival contacts — to relay messages and provocations. He cannot tolerate the absence between confrontations and so manufactures presence by proxy.
- The drinking, by this stage, is structural rather than recreational; the body is on a maintenance dose.
- The teaching impulse, frustrated by Clint's autonomy, **redirects to a substitute student**. This is when the second-generation "Trick Shot" appears — a nephew, a stranger, anyone whose pliability and skill ceiling permit the original transmission to be re-performed. The substitute is a thinner stand-in and is consciously known by Buck to be thinner; the substitute exists in order to provoke Clint by replacement. *I have a new son. He is better than you.* This is the line, spoken or unspoken, in every late appearance.

---

## 11.6 Stage Five — Somatic Breach (the Body Defects)

The terminal cancer diagnosis (or, in earlier eras, the cumulative degradation of the visual-motor system by age) is the **first failure he cannot project**. He has spent his life externalizing every breach of his self-image to another agent — Clint, the carnival, the employer, the rival. The body's failure has no external agent. There is no one to blame.

This is the watershed. From here, decompensation is monotonic.

**Presentation:**
- **A new precision in the management of his image.** He becomes meticulous about light, angle, the room he is seen in. Where the dying typically retreat from view, he stages himself for it. The dying body is now the performance, and he is choreographing the wake.
- **Weight loss is hidden under layered clothing**; tremor is hidden under gloves; pallor is managed by sun exposure on a deliberate schedule. The somatic management is theatrical, not medical. He is not trying to live longer; he is trying to look like himself longer.
- **Pain is denied verbally and admitted bodily** — a hand that strays to the abdomen mid-sentence, a half-second of breath-holding before standing, a fractional listing in the gait. He will not name the pain because to name it is to cede ownership.
- **The pre-shot ritual extends further**. He may add a full inhalation cycle, a touch to the bow's upper limb, a glance at the off-target. Each addition is a mask for a deficit. By the end he is performing the *idea* of his shot more than the shot itself; sometimes, in private, the shot misses and he claims it. The lying about marksmanship is, for him, the deepest possible regression — and is therefore an unmistakable terminal indicator.
- **Sleep collapses.** He is up at three, at four, walking. The walking has no destination. This is the only stage at which he is observably without a plan, and even here the lack of plan is hidden under brisk pace.

---

## 11.7 Stage Six — The Terminal Gesture

The summons. He calls Clint to him — sometimes openly, sometimes via the new "Trick Shot" sent as messenger and challenge — and stages the final scene. The staging is the apex of his pathology, not its softening. Every element is choreographed:

- **Location**: somewhere with carnival resonance, an old lot, a returned-to ground. He is closing the loop to the period of original mastery.
- **Witnesses**: ideally one — the protégé. No more, no less. A second witness diffuses the intimacy of the coercion; no witness erases the performance. One is the only number that works.
- **The bow**: laid out, sometimes given over, sometimes notched. The transfer is symbolic and is meant to bind.
- **The brief, final form**: a confession that is not a confession. He will narrate the embezzlement and the abandonment, but in a register of **inevitability** rather than wrongdoing. *That was how it had to be. You were always going to learn it that way.* He cannot apologize; the architecture forbids it. What he can do is reframe the entire history as a curriculum he designed.
- **The demand**: that Clint kill him, or accept the inheritance, or witness the death, or train the successor. The specific demand varies; the structural feature is invariant — **the protégé is given the role of finishing the script Buck has written**. He cannot tolerate dying as an event that happens to him; he must die as an event he authored, executed via the hand he shaped.

The terminal gesture is the **completion of the iterative cycle**: every return across decades was a rehearsal for this scene. The blame externalization, having no body left to project to, finally collapses inward — and the collapse is concealed under the elegance of the staging. He dies, in his own narrative, as the master who chose the moment. He dies, in fact, as a man who could not bear to be the patient of any process he did not direct.

---

## 11.8 What Collapse Does NOT Look Like

To prevent misidentification — because the subject is most dangerous when handlers expect the wrong collapse:

- **No depressive surrender.** He will not stop eating, stop dressing, stop performing. There is no withdrawal phase. Looking for one will cause you to miss the actual deterioration.
- **No paranoid bloom.** His suspicion remains situational. He will not begin to see plots that are not there. He sees real plots clearly and ignores the unreal ones.
- **No psychotic break.** Reality testing remains intact even terminally. His distortions are characterological, not perceptual.
- **No tearful reconciliation.** Not under any provocation. The single most reliable prediction this file will make: **he will die without a true apology to Clint Barton.** Any apparent apology is a tactical insertion in the larger script and should be read for its operational function, not its sentimental content.
- **No diminishment of skill claim.** He will lie about his shooting before he will admit a missed shot. The lie is the symptom; treat reports of late-life Buck shots that "no one saw land" with appropriate skepticism.
- **No new attachments.** The substitute student is a prop, not a relationship. He will not, in the terminal phase, develop a confidant, a lover, a friend. He dies inside his own architecture, by design.

---

## 11.9 Conditions That Produce Decompensation (Summary Matrix)

| Trigger Class | Specific Stimulus | Decompensation Vector | Time to Action |
|---|---|---|---|
| Status | Out-shot publicly by junior | Stage One → Two | Days to weeks |
| Status | Protégé named as superior | Stage Two reach | Weeks |
| Exposure | Past fraud surfaced | Stage Three cold rage | Hours |
| Bodily | First tremor, blurred sight | Stage One ritual extension | Immediate |
| Bodily | Terminal diagnosis | Stage Five → Six | Months |
| Interpersonal | Empathic appeal from protégé | Stage Three escalation | Within the conversation |
| Interpersonal | Reconciliation offer | **Maximal escalation** | Within the conversation |
| Audience | Loss of witness | Diminishment, not danger | N/A |
| Audience | Acquisition of fresh witness | Re-stabilization, performance | Immediate |
| Hierarchy | Substitute student outperforms him | Same arc as Clint, telescoped | Weeks |

---

## 11.10 Operational Note

The error any handler, family member, or operator will make with this subject is the same error the early canon made: to read the hardness as the man and the cruelty as the job. The hardness is the symptom of the failure mode already in progress. By the time he is dangerous, he has been decompensating for some time — and the tells were available from the first extra breath-cycle before a draw, the first carnival word in the speech, the first folded news clipping in the coat.

He does not break suddenly. He breaks in measured installments, each one performed for an audience of one, and the audience, every time, is the boy he abandoned.

— END SECTION 11 —


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# SECTION 9 — TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT

## SUBJECT: BERNARD "BUCK" BARTON, alias TRICK SHOT
### Forecast horizon: terminal phase + posthumous influence vector

---

## 9.1 Frame of the Forecast

Any forward assessment of this subject must reckon with a structural fact peculiar to his case: he is already inside the terminal corridor. The diagnosis of cancer is on the record; the deathbed summons of the protégé is on the record; the search for an heir to the alias is on the record. We are not projecting decades. We are projecting the last actions of a man who knows, with the unusual clarity afforded by a confirmed mortality estimate, exactly how many shots remain in the quiver. This compresses every forecast and intensifies it. With most subjects, trajectory analysis maps drift; with Barton, it maps detonation.

The second framing fact is that his pathology — narcissistic organization of malignant variant, see §4 — does not soften under pressure. It crystallizes. The empirical record of NPD-malignant in late life, cross-referenced against Barton's own behavior under the stressors already documented (skill challenge, exposure, bodily decline), strongly predicts intensification rather than mellowing. He will not become wiser. He will become more concentrated.

The third framing fact is the protégé. Clinton Barton remains the load-bearing object in Buck's internal world. Every meaningful forecast must therefore be plotted on a two-axis grid: what Buck does, and what Clint does in response or refusal. The forecast is fundamentally relational, even when Buck operates alone, because in his cosmology he never truly operates alone — he always performs, and Clint is the seat in the front row he keeps reserved.

---

## 9.2 The Three Probable Endings

There are, on the evidence, three terminal scenarios with non-trivial probability. They are not mutually exclusive — Buck is the kind of man who will try to engineer all three in sequence if the first fails — but one will dominate.

### 9.2.1 The Coerced-Hand Ending (probability: highest)

Buck stages his death such that Clint must fire the killing shot — by hostage gambit, by suicide-by-protégé framed as duel, by threat-to-third-party that only Clint's arrow can resolve, by manufactured impossible-rescue scenario in which Clint must choose Buck as the casualty. The deathbed summons already documented is a soft version of this. The hard version weaponizes a civilian or a member of Clint's chosen family (Bobbi, Kate Bishop, the wider Avengers-adjacent constellation) to force the hand.

Why this is the modal forecast: it satisfies every node of his pathology simultaneously. It is the final performance (audience: Clint, plus whichever bystanders constitute the room). It is the final assertion of pedagogical authority (*I taught you to make this shot; now make it on me*). It is the final punishment of Clint's original disloyalty (*you exposed me, now you finish me, and you will carry it*). It is the final escape from the indignity of dying small in a hospice bed of a disease that nobody applauds. And it reframes his death — which is the one thing he cannot control — as a thing he choreographed.

The signatures to watch for, in surveillance terms: a sudden acquisition of intelligence on Clint's intimates; a late and uncharacteristic generosity of disclosure (he will *tell* Clint things in the last act that he has withheld for decades, because disclosure becomes part of the staging); the procurement of a single high-grade bow rather than a working kit; a chosen location with sight lines and theatrical geometry — high ground, an open floor, a roof, a carnival lot, a circus tent, somewhere that reads as set.

### 9.2.2 The Heir Ending (probability: moderate, often interleaved with 9.2.1)

Buck identifies, trains in compressed form, and bequeaths the alias *Trick Shot* to a successor — a younger marksman, possibly a blood relation, possibly a stranger selected for the right combination of skill and grievance. The successor is then loosed against Clint or against Clint's circle as Buck's posthumous arrow. This is the legacy-transfer gesture already partially in the canon; in forward projection it expands and weaponizes.

The function this serves: it bypasses death. He gets to keep shooting after he stops breathing. The pedagogical economy — *I make the marksman, the marksman bears my mark* — extends his existence by one generation. It also, crucially, gives him a second chance at the original drama: this time the protégé will not betray him, because he will choose the protégé specifically for incapacity to do so (a true believer, a debt-bound family member, an ideologue of the bow).

The successor is the variable. The forecast splits sharply depending on the selection: a relative recruited from genuine kin produces a long-tail antagonist for Clint's later life and Kate Bishop's career; a damaged-acolyte stranger produces a sharper, briefer, more violent posthumous incident. In either case, the heir will be *less* technically gifted than Buck (he cannot bear to be exceeded even posthumously, and will tune his teaching to ensure asymmetry) but *more* unstable, because Buck's compressed end-of-life pedagogy will lack the years of grinding repetition that built his own stability.

### 9.2.3 The Solitary Ending (probability: low, but the growth ending)

Buck dies alone, of the disease, in a room without an audience. No coerced hand, no heir, no theatre. This is the ending his pathology cannot tolerate and therefore the one his pathology will fight hardest to prevent. It is also the only ending that breaks the pattern rather than extending it. Its low probability is itself a diagnostic finding: a subject for whom unwitnessed death is the worst outcome is a subject who has organized his entire selfhood around being watched.

Conditions under which this ending becomes possible: rapid disease progression that outruns his capacity to stage; isolation imposed by criminal-justice custody during the terminal phase; Clint's strategic refusal to enter the room. The last is the operative variable and is examined in §9.4.

---

## 9.3 The Interim Trajectory — Months Before the End

Before any terminal scenario fires, there is a runway. On the evidence, that runway will be populated by the following behavioral classes, listed in expected order of appearance:

**Late-stage contract acceptance, increasingly punitive in target selection.** He will take work — partly because he always has, partly because mercenary employment provides the cover under which he can position himself near Clint's operational theatre without admitting that this is the purpose. Expect the contracts to skew toward jobs that put him on collision course with Avengers-adjacent assets. Expect his employers to be increasingly disposable from his perspective; he is no longer building a career and no longer needs to honor relationships with paymasters. A handler who contracts him in this period will likely be discarded, double-crossed, or used as a stepping stone toward the Clint-axis.

**Reactivation of old contacts in the carnival circuit and the marksman subculture.** He will revisit places. This is partly nostalgia (a faculty he will not name as such; he will frame it as reconnaissance or business) and partly the gathering of materials — old training films, the original bow, photographs, the carnival's surviving witnesses to the founding drama. He is curating his own museum, for use in the staging. Watch for inquiries into the location of the Carson Carnival's remnant property, surviving Duquesne-era effects, archived performance bills.

**Tightened personal grooming, paradoxical fitness intensification.** The body is failing; he will compensate by intensifying the disciplines he can still execute. Expect rigorous dry-fire practice maintained beyond the point of clinical sensibility, weight discipline maintained against cachexia, hair and beard regimens kept exact. He will not appear, in the final months, like a sick man. He will appear like a man who has refused to be sick — which is a different and more dangerous presentation. Field operatives encountering him in this phase should not be misled by the unimpaired surface. The capacity is real; the suppression of decline is cosmetic.

**A single, uncharacteristic disclosure event.** At some point in the interim, he will tell *one* person something true about himself that he has never said aloud. The candidate audiences are limited: most likely Clint, in a controlled-conditions encounter that he will pretend is accidental; possibly the chosen heir, as initiation; least likely but most diagnostic, a bartender or a hospice intake nurse, in an unguarded moment that he will subsequently rationalize as strategic. The content of the disclosure will probably touch the childhood he has never discussed — the harder hand he learned under (see §3, identification with the aggressor). This event is the closest thing to introspection he is capable of, and it will be followed by *increased* hostility toward the recipient, because the exposure of having spoken is itself an injury.

**Escalation in cruelty toward weaker peripheral figures.** Subordinates, hired drivers, prostitutes, low-level criminal associates. The pattern is well-established in the malignant-narcissistic terminal phase: as the central target (Clint) becomes harder to reach and the body becomes less reliable, lateral targets absorb the displaced aggression. This is forecastable as a forensic signature — a string of beatings, dismissals, fatal "accidents" among the disposable people in his orbit during the runway period. Triangulating these incidents geographically would, in principle, give a near-real-time map of his location and intent.

---

## 9.4 Fork Points — The Decisions That Determine the Branch

The forecast above is the unintervened trajectory. It bends, sometimes sharply, on a small number of decisions made by parties other than Buck. These are the fork points.

### Fork 1: Clint's Response to the Summons

When the deathbed summons arrives — and on the evidence it will arrive, in some form, perhaps repeatedly — Clint has three responses available:

- *Attend, alone, as Buck stages it.* This is the response Clint's psychology pulls him toward (the susceptibility to mentor-figures is exactly what Buck built into him; see §3). It maximizes Buck's terminal control. It produces the Coerced-Hand Ending. It produces durable post-traumatic damage in Clint.
- *Attend, but on terms Clint sets.* Witnessed, in a venue Clint chooses, with Buck stripped of staging variables. This is the response that produces the Solitary Ending by other means: Buck will likely refuse, withdraw, attempt to re-stage, fail under his own time constraint, and die without his choreography. The fork requires Clint to do something he is structurally bad at, which is refusing the bait without refusing the obligation he feels.
- *Refuse entirely.* Forces the Heir Ending or the Solitary Ending. Damages Clint via the unmetabolized non-encounter, but spares him the worse damage of executing the hand-coerced shot.

The handler's recommendation, if a handler exists for Clint in this scenario, is the second branch. It is also the hardest to support him through.

### Fork 2: The Identification of the Heir, If Any

If Buck moves toward the Heir Ending, the fork is whether the prospective successor is interdictable before initiation. This is a narrow window — Buck's compressed pedagogy will run weeks to a few months — and requires intelligence on the carnival-marksman subculture that no agency currently maintains at the necessary granularity. The benevolent-intervention play is not to kill or detain the prospect but to *reach them first*: a young marksman who has been offered the alias by a dying man trading on family debt or ideological flattery is, in the pre-initiation window, still recoverable. Post-initiation they are not, because Buck will have braided the alias into their self-concept the same way he braided the bow into his own.

### Fork 3: The Hospice / Custody Variable

If Buck is taken into custody during the terminal phase — for a contract violation, for a peripheral homicide, for any of the lateral cruelties projected in §9.3 — the staging capability collapses. He cannot choreograph from a cell or a hospital ward under guard. This is the cleanest intervention available and the most likely to be missed, because it requires recognizing the pattern early enough to take him on something minor before he is positioned for the major event. The forensic-triangulation play described above is the operational route.

### Fork 4: The Disclosure Recipient

If the uncharacteristic disclosure event lands with someone capable of holding it without weaponizing it, there is a thin possibility — call it 3-5% — of a small genuine shift in the final weeks. Not redemption; nothing so large. But a marginal de-escalation of the staging compulsion, a partial willingness to die in a room rather than on a stage. The candidate recipient is almost certainly not Clint, whose presence triggers all the old defenses. It is more plausibly a hospice clinician, a chaplain figure he will pretend to despise, or — interesting and underweighted — Kate Bishop, who is structurally outside the original drama and whose competence with the bow would compel Buck's involuntary respect without activating the protégé-betrayal circuit. A meeting between Buck and Kate, were one to occur, would be the highest-information event in the whole terminal arc.

---

## 9.5 What Would Push Him Toward Growth

Growth, for this subject, is not redemption. It is a marginal expansion of the capacity to register another person as real. The threshold is low because his baseline is low; the difficulty is high because every defense he has is built to prevent exactly this expansion.

The conditions that could, in principle, produce a measurable shift:

- **A skill encounter that is not a contest.** Someone — Kate is the candidate — shooting alongside him rather than against him, in a context with no scorekeeping and no audience. This bypasses the contempt-or-rivalry binary that exhausts his interpersonal repertoire. It is the only known stimulus class that has, in analogous cases, produced even brief affective opening in late-stage malignant narcissism.
- **Witnessed acknowledgment from Clint that does not request reciprocity.** Not forgiveness offered, not apology solicited. A bare statement — *you taught me to do this, and I have done it, and you are dying* — delivered without the affective freight Clint usually brings to these encounters. Buck cannot metabolize empathy offered to him; he can sometimes metabolize being seen accurately. The distinction is subtle and Clint is unlikely to be able to draw it under the conditions Buck will engineer.
- **Physical decline severe enough to disable the staging without disabling consciousness.** Cruel but operative: a man too weak to choreograph but still able to think may, for the first time in his life, encounter himself without the bow in his hand. What he finds there will be terrifying to him and might, in a small percentage of cases, produce something other than rage. More likely it produces despair. Despair, in this subject, would be growth, because despair requires admitting that the position was always smaller than it pretended.

None of these are likely. The aggregate probability of meaningful growth is, on the evidence, under ten percent. The dossier records them not because they are forecasted but because they are the levers that exist, and any benevolent operator working this file should know what the levers are even when the door will not open.

---

## 9.6 What Would Push Him Toward Catastrophe

Catastrophe here means: maximum harm done in the terminal phase, beyond the baseline staged-death harm. The accelerants are:

- **Visible reconciliation between Clint and any other mentor figure.** A scene in which Clint publicly credits another teacher — Captain America in the historical record, possibly Fury, possibly even the memory of the Swordsman — will be received by Buck as the protégé being claimed by a rival lineage. The narcissistic injury is severe and the response will be a contract or staging accelerated past whatever Buck's original timeline was.
- **Public humiliation of his skill.** A documented out-shoot, especially one that circulates in the marksman subculture. He will respond not by retreat but by escalation, and the escalation will be aimed not at the person who out-shot him but at someone closer to Clint, because the displacement pathway is the established one.
- **A premature reveal of the cancer diagnosis to Clint by a third party.** This deprives Buck of the disclosure as a controlled gambit. It makes the deathbed summons, when it comes, structurally weaker, and his compensatory response will be to make the staging more violent — more hostages, more lethal stakes, more bystanders — to restore the gradient of control.
- **The death of Clint by other causes during Buck's terminal phase.** This is the catastrophe scenario that destroys the entire architecture of Buck's final act and is therefore the one in which his behavior becomes least predictable and most dangerous. With the central object removed, the displaced aggression has no organizing target. Expect, in this scenario, an indiscriminate terminal spree against carnival-circuit and mercenary-subculture figures, plus the heir track activated in a more ideological and less personal mode — an heir taught to hate the entire Avengers-adjacent population rather than Clint specifically.

---

## 9.7 Posthumous Vector

Buck does not end at death. The dossier must track, in forward projection, the field he leaves behind.

**On Clint.** Whichever terminal scenario fires, Clint carries the residue. The Coerced-Hand Ending produces a discrete traumatic incident with predictable sequelae — sleep disturbance, increased substance use, withdrawal from mentor roles (including, importantly, from Kate, who needs the opposite), a period of operational unreliability. The Heir Ending produces a chronic adversarial relationship that ages with Clint and that he is likely to mishandle by transferring onto the heir his unresolved feelings about Buck. The Solitary Ending produces a longer, slower, perhaps more workable mourning. The benevolent operator concerned with Clint's long-term integrity should weight interventions accordingly.

**On the marksman subculture.** Buck's death will produce a brief surge of stories, a contested inheritance of reputation, and a small number of imitators. The alias *Trick Shot* will recirculate. Monitor for adoption by figures unrelated to the original lineage; the name is now a brand and brands have their own life.

**On Kate Bishop.** Underweighted in most projections but operationally significant. Kate's relationship to the bow as inherited from Clint means that Buck is, transitively, her professional grandfather. She will encounter his shadow whether or not she ever meets the man. Her relative immunity to the original drama (she was not raised in it) makes her the figure most likely to neutralize the posthumous field rather than perpetuate it. If a long-term operator wishes to seal the lineage off cleanly, the work is done through her.

**On the file itself.** This dossier will need to be reopened once, in the immediate wake of the terminal event, to assess which scenario fired and to update the Clint dossier and the Kate Bishop dossier accordingly. Beyond that, the Bernard Barton file closes — a small, sharp, finished record of an ordinary kind of damaged man who happened to be holding a bow, and of the longer wound that his hand will continue to make through the people he taught and the people they teach.

— END SECTION 9 —

## Relationship Graph
### [[Clinton Francis Barton (Hawkeye (also: Ronin, Goliath - briefly, Golden Archer - briefly))]]
- The defining bond of his life and the one he is structurally incapable of acknowledging in plain language
- Took Clint in as apprentice in the carnival years; trained him to professional then superhuman marksmanship; partnered (with Swordsman) in petty theft Clint refused to join
- BETRAYAL EVENT: beat/shot Clint and left him for dead when Clint refused the criminal turn. The wound that organizes Clint's adult life and Barton's late life equally
- Returns repeatedly as antagonist-mentor: testing, taunting, hunting, and — in the terminal-cancer arc — trying to force Clint to kill him
- Clint has surpassed him technically AND morally; Barton knows it; cannot say it
- FAILURE MODE / LEVERAGE: any operator who reaches Clint reaches Barton. Conversely, any operator who can credibly threaten Clint can pull Barton out of any retirement, illness, or cover. The bond is the lever in both directions. The dangerous turn: if Barton becomes convinced Clint will not grant him the staged-duel death, he may escalate toward harming people Clint loves — not from sadism but from desperation to force the contest grammar to hold

### Jacques Duquesne
- Swordsman — long criminal partner from the carnival years, co-instigator of the theft Clint refused
- Closest thing Barton had to a peer; relationship was mutual exploitation dressed as camaraderie
- Duquesne's eventual arc (Avengers, redemption, death) is a road not taken that Barton refuses to examine
- LEVERAGE: invoking Swordsman's name, particularly his late-life redemption, is one of the few stimuli that can crack Barton's contempt — though the crack closes fast

### Successor Apprentice
- At least one canonical successor 'Trick Shot' — proof Barton kept repeating the pattern after Clint
- Functions as evidence of obsession (he could not stop being a teacher) and as displacement (anyone but Clint)
- LEVERAGE: the successor can be reached, surveilled, or turned to predict Barton's location and intent; threats to the successor produce a muted version of the Clint-protective response

### Harold Barton Structural
- Never met Clint's biological father but occupies the vacated paternal slot
- Modeled the opposite of Harold's collapse (disciplined where Harold was drunk; present where Harold was absent) — and then betrayed the slot in his own register (violent where Harold was violent)
- Operationally: never speak Harold's name to him; the comparison is the one form of shame he cannot route into contempt
